O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	O you, very dear sons, I have completed this book for you which is the last in the science of medicine together with its fulfillment, and I have made an end through its explanations and by its declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to me in a vision that I complete it for you with this treatise which is part of the work of hands, that is to say, "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is neglected in our region and has been lost to all, so its knowledge is depleted and cut off, and nothing remains from it but small descriptions in ancient books that have come down to us.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this has come error and vanity, and intentions have been clouded over and knowledge pushed away.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	Or it seems to me that I want to revive it along with the arrangement of this treatise according to the way of exposition and explanation and abbreviation; and I will come with the forms of cautery irons, and other instruments for the work, together with their adjustment, preparation as necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And for the reason that no good master of hands is found in our time, the art of medicine has become distant.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And it is necessary for anyone who wishes to undertake this to overcome the science of anatomy, as Galen says, so that they know the judgment of members and their forms and conjunctions and separations; and have knowledge of bones, nerves, brains, and the number of them, also movement and moving veins and resting ones, and where they emerge.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And so Hippocrates says that knowledge without action is futile, and it is with practice that one achieves perfection, especially in the art of medicine.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	We tell you in the introduction of this book that one who is not knowledgeable about the aforementioned things should be cautious to avoid error and harming others; just as I have often seen many who venture into this science without knowledge or experience, thus abandoning reason.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	For I saw a foolish surgeon cut into an abscess on the neck of a woman and severed her carotid artery; so much blood poured out that the woman fell dead in his hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	And I saw another surgeon treat a bladder stone in a man with water, and the stone was large; he took away a part of the bladder along with it, and the man died within three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I had already been called to treat him, and saw the condition of the patient and the size of the stone, and if they cut it out, he would die.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	I saw another doctor who took care of our land's duke, who had a broken leg and an open wound with the fracture. This ignorant doctor set the break over the wound too tightly, not leaving any room for the wound to swell, and left it like that for some time. He ordered the duke not to remove it, and so his leg swelled up completely and his foot was lost.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I was called to go to him, and I hurried to come and remove his leg bandage; when I loosened it he felt peaceful and no pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But nonetheless, the corruption was already confirmed in the limb, and I could not heal it; and the corruption did not cease its spread throughout the member until the limb was entirely lost.
Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And there was another evil physician who would burst an abscess open and then inflame it with the malignancy of his power.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For a cancer, when it is caused by melancholic humour, one should not touch it with iron unless it is in such a place that one can remove all the corrupted tissue.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And thus, my dear son, you must know that manual work is divided into two categories: the first being work where there is danger in several situations, and I will show you in each place of this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	For this reason, it is necessary that you be cautious, so that the foolish doctor cannot speak ill of you. Take your weapons with wisdom, approach your patients gently but firmly, and employ the best method so that by God's grace you come to their salvation and are praised; leave terrible diseases for those of severe health; remove your armor from whatever makes you doubt yourself, and have faith in yourself so that you may journey from this world into another with glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Galen says in some of his admonishments: "Do not treat serious illnesses unless you want to be called a foolish doctor.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have devised this treatise in three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapter is about fire cauterization and other medical procedures with hot irons, and this chapter is arranged from the head to the feet; it describes the forms of instruments, the tools for cauterizing, and everything else that is necessary for the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, and cupping, wounds, arrow extractions, and similar matters; and the chapter is arranged with forms of instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and torsions, and similar matters; and it is arranged from head to foot, with the forms of instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Before we recall the work, it is necessary for me to speak of the quality of aid and harm of each humour.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the quality of aid and harm is the longest speech and most subtle science, full of secrets; and many wise men have spoken about it, agreeing on this point; but I will suffice with few words for fear of lengthiness.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that cautery aids universally all complexions where there is matter involved, except for two complexions: namely hot complexion without matter and dry complexion without matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In the case of hot and dry complexions with matter combined, some argued that cautery is a great aid while others said the opposite - that cautery does not help diseases arising from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	As the nature of fire is hot, it should not be used to treat diseases caused by heat or dryness, and those who say otherwise claim that cautery provides great relief for hot and dry diseases occurring in human bodies.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	When you compare the body of man with its moisture to the complexion of fire, you find the former cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this statement.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have found it by experience once.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And in any case, let not he who has not experienced it nor knows by long practice the chapter of cauterization, and the diversity of human constitutions, and their dispositions and causes of illness, and occurrences and duration of time; we have no fear for other constitutions, especially in cold and moist illnesses.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all the doctors agreed and consented to the cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, my child, that fire cautery is one of the secrets of healing and is of greater benefit than burning medical cautery.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and it does not arise except on the member that is cooked, and it harms no other member unless touched.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	The burning medicines spread from member to another in distance, and cause the member diseases of long healing; and by chance they kill the patient The fire due to its height and goodness of substance does not do this if there is no excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And this I have found through experiment and by the length of my service and study in the art, and it is based on the truth of things; and for that reason, I excuse myself for the length of my words, as I do not wish to take away from you the secret that is hidden in fire, and the quality of its work, how it treats diseases of the body, as the philosopher says when demonstrating; now receive this in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, son, that they agreed on when the cauterizations should be performed, and chose carefully.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	I say that cauterization is suitable in all seasons, for the harmful effects are diminished by its help; especially if the cauterizations are necessary to treat pain and urgent cases where there is no time to wait for more severe problems to occur in the limb.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And never believe it, dear son, as some foolish physicians do; for the illness that is cured by cauterization has no relapse; and they say this in such a way; but it is not as they think, because cauterization is only a medicine that changes the complexion and dries up the humors that cause pain, and it is more powerful than any other medicine due to its swift action, and for the strength of its work and authority.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	And it is a notable thing that the illness may come sometimes according to the complexion of the patient and the place of the sickness and its nature; and are gathered in him excesses through the consumption of food and similar things, if not cauterizations administered in places where there is little excess and moisture, such as dental cautery for pain, and similar things, and this pain does not return; but this happens rarely.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And many people do not understand why cauterizations are called the last resort of medicine, and this is true; but they do not believe that cauterization follows medicine in value, their intentions are false, and it is cauterization which is the last resort in medicine because when we administer various treatments for a disease and they have no effect, then we apply the cautery, and it works.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Then it is evident that cauterization is the last resort of medicine, not according to the intention of foolish doctors.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The ancients said that cauterization with a golden instrument is better than with iron, and they attributed this to the quality of gold and its noble nature; and they claimed that the place of cauterization does not get infected, but I have proven this not to be true as it indeed happens in some people; and gold cautery is superior to iron, just like they said.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And yet when you heat a golden instrument, you do not know when it is hot by looking at its color as gold does not change with heat and quickly cools down; and if one heats it too much, it will break in the fire; thus there are enough difficulties with this method.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this, we use fire cautery, which we have adapted to our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Here you have been ordered this chapter of the head to feet, so that the way is easier to find.
dou cautere olivaire	Olive oil cautery.
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	This cautery is beneficial for moisture and cold in the brain, and there are two that are made due to a disease called 'soda', and because of many humours that descend from the head to the eyes, ears, and due to numerous dreams, toothache, sore throat, and especially all diseases that come from cold such as paralysis, soda, apoplexy, and similar illnesses.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The form of this cautery is such that the patient should be purged with a dissolving medicine that clears the head for three or four nights, according to what the virtues, age, and habits of the patient can endure; then have them sleep on their head.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	Then have them sit crossed-legged between your hands, and place their hands on top of yours; afterward, put the root of your palm on the root of their nose between their two eyes; leave your two middle fingers there, then cauterize with the 'olive' iron, which should look like this:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	Place them on a bed of ink, and while descending and squeezing your hand back and forth in a twisting motion; then lift your hand slightly, and withdraw if you see the bone just barely; if not, repeat cauterizing until you do as I've said; afterward, take a small pouch and fill it with soft cotton, place it on their wound, and leave it for three days; after this, put moist cotton wool soaked in butter on top; keep this on until the burning sensation has passed; then treat the wound with an ointment called 'tetrafarmacum' until it is healed.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And the elders said that the longer a wound remains open, the more it purges itself; thus aiding healing.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And some said that one should let the cautery burn until a part of the bone is charred, then remove what has been burned from the bone and it shall be healed.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And others say that one should let the cautery remain in place and press down so hard that it pierces the bone, creating a hole as wide as the reamers used by women on their thimbles, so that the humours may escape; then leave the wound open for some time before cleaning and suturing it.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And these two methods of cautery do not seem good to me at all, except perhaps in certain people where there is a way out of fear; and I must leave it alone because the shoulder is weakened by nature's continuous changes, as we show in other limbs; even when the patient's shoulder is weak by nature, and the first method of cautery seems safer and more effective to me, which is what I use for their overall well-being.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	Of the ancient pain of the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When in the entire head there is chronic pain that lasts a long time, the patient should use herbs and pills called 'cochie', as well as purgatives for the head, oils, and poultices; if they undergo the cauterization we previously mentioned and it doesn't work.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Take care if the patient's shoulder is of a strong nature and not too cold; then cauterize below that cautery a little bit, as we mentioned above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est I leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	Afterwards, perform the cautery on each corner of the head up to the bone, as we said before, and do a cautery where it is called 'vasselz'; these are the places where cups are applied; and ease your hand so that you don't go down to the bone: the patient feels much more pain in this cautery than the others, and I will speak of it later; and make sure that the cauteries on the corners are more subtle than those used for the middle part of the head, and this is how:
dou cautere dou chief	For the head cautery.
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When sudden pain occurs in one part of the head and extends up to the eye, and the head is cleansed with purgative medicines, and other treatments I have mentioned for dividing diseases are performed, but nothing helps: then you make cauterizations according to two methods, that is, with cold medicine and with fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	Cold medicine cauterizations are as follows: take a hazel stick and remove the bark, cut it into two pieces, then slit the temple where the pain is in such a way that you can place the hazel stick under the skin; once placed, bind and hold it tight for twelve hours; then unbind and press the hazel stick firmly with your fingers, leaving the wound like this for two or three days; afterward, apply cotton soaked in butter as long as needed.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the treatment, wait until it is healed; and if you want to do this with certain burning medicines, then look at what I have written in the twelfth treatise on burning medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The iron cautery is done in this manner.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the cautery, which has this shape:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	It is called a "close" because the tip is shaped like a bell with a small bulge in the middle; place it on the painful area, and keep your hand steady but turn the iron slightly so that half of the blade's edge is heated; lift your hand before the artery burns, which is outside, and let the blood flow freely.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	After apply cotton in awe of silk, and place it on the wound for three days; then put moist cotton with butter, and cure the wound by anointing until it is healed; and if you wish to cauterize this migraine with the cautery called 'cultellare', be careful not to cut the artery during this ancient procedure.
de emigraine	of a migraine
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	When you treat a migraine as we mentioned before in the division of illnesses, and it does not improve, and you see that the previous cauterization methods using medicine and iron are not sufficient, then you must heat the cautery called 'cultellare' until it is white; make an incision on the affected area along a line half an inch long, withdraw your hand once, and be careful not to cut the artery or reach the bone; beware of moving the jaw when chewing, ensure that it does not move so as to avoid spasm in the patient, and watch out for loss of blood from the artery if it is severed, which carries great risk especially for those who are uninformed and inexperienced; leave the procedure halfway. I will tell you how to stop bleeding when an artery is cut, and I shall show you where this is discussed in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	And if you see that these cauterizations are not sufficient for the illness, and the patient is still suffering, cauterize him on the head as we have mentioned before, and treat the wound until it heals completely; and if you see fit, use the cautery we described in the chapter about arterial extraction, with a cautery instrument that has two blades; this type of cauterization is better and more effective than the previous one.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	From ear pain due to coldness
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When there is ear pain due to coldness, and one has applied solutive medicines and other treatments as we have mentioned before in the division of this book, but the pain does not subside, then heat up this cautery tool called a "point". This is how it looks like:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche; et ait X poins entor chescune oreille; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After prick around the diseased ear, or around both if pain is felt in both, and move a little above the root of the ear once you have marked the place for incision; make ten pricks around each ear; afterward treat the area until it is healed.
de la torture de la bouche	Upon the torture of the mouth:
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	Treatment of the mouth that must be cured by cauterization is exempt from those caused by wind, as we have said in the division of diseases; and do not apply cautery to similar conditions arising from dryness and nerve spasms.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	When you treat this similar condition of mouth torture caused by wind from the stomach and purging of the head, as well as gargling, and it is ineffective, then you must cauterize the patient with three cauteries: one at the root of the ear, another slightly outside the temple, and a third at the junction of the two lips; apply the cautery to the part that appears healthy, and perform the cauterization on the head near the ear above a little below the crown, and another in the temple as long as a thumb; leave the cautery in place until half of the heart's beat has passed; this is the shape of the cautery:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And it resembles the scalpel we placed before, but it is a little more subtle and the knife should be slightly larger; after treating the place as I said before, until it is healed.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres: II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	When apoplexy is an old condition and you treat it as we have said before, but the patient does not improve and has no fever, then apply four cauterizations: two on the two corners of the head, one in the middle of the head, and one at the place called "vessels" as we have mentioned earlier, and the last cautery is placed over the mouth of the stomach; it should be treated as previously described.
de litargie	Of lethargy.
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil; aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres; et c’est li maniere dou cautere: si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	For this illness, give the patient large herbs and pills that soften the brain; then rinse his entire head with warm water, and apply on the occiput a mustard plaster which is described in the treatise of plasters; and this is how the cauterization is done: if you do it as I said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est; et s’il ne l’est, se li fai III cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere I doi de gros; et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai I cautere en mileu; et se mestiers est, II autres sus les II cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	If it is healed in this way, it is good; and if not, perform three cauterizations on him from the middle of the head down to the neck, leaving a two-finger space between each cauterization; treat him as with the others, and if you wish to add something, and the patient can tolerate it, perform one cauterization in the middle; and if necessary, perform two more on the two corners, treating him until he is healed; and let the cauterizations be those called "olivare", as I have said before.
de la froidor dou chief	From the coldness of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit; aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et I derrier et III sus l’espinee dou col; et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai IIII cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos; et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	You must ensure that the head is cleaned of hair and as we have previously said; after removing the hair from the patient's head, perform a cauterization in the middle of the head and on each corner, then one behind and three on the spine of the neck; if you need to do more, and their body is moist and they can tolerate it, and the illness is severe, perform four cauterizations on the spine of the back; let them be like this until the strongest part of the heart is burned, then lift your hand away; treat him until he is healed, and let the cauterizations be those called "olivare" as we have previously said.
de l’epilempsie	from epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	The epileptic should not undergo fire cauterization unless they are phlegmatic; it is necessary to first modify the brain with herbs and other treatments we have mentioned in the section for adults who are suffering greatly.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes; aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne; et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if it is a child who cannot withstand this treatment, give them gargles and have them chew often with beneficial meat; then lift the head in the middle, and perform a cautery as we have described before, cauterize on the vessel and each corner; and if the patient is strong and suffering, apply cauteries as I mentioned for one who has paralysis and bodily weakness, to the spine of the back and neck, and let the cauteries be olive-shaped according to the method I outlined.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai I cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is a child, perform this delicate cautery as follows:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When due to melancholia the superfluities or corrupt humours and thick phlegm prevail, then cauterize with three cauteries as we have said for one who has paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if due to melancholia the superfluities decline towards it, and the patient's body is moist, then give them something to drink by which their brain may be cleansed, as was said before in the classification.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide; aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief; et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars; aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien; et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir; aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier; et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	First clean the patient's head; then make a well-prepared flax pad, like a circle, and place it in the middle of their head; have the patient sit cross-legged, and hold them steady on all sides; present the liniment, which is best made with old sheep butter; heat it to a moderate fire so that its warmth can be tolerated by the skin; then empty the circle within the head, and leave it to cool; do this for the patient once each week along with other good treatments until they are healed.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	If you see scabs form during the cautery, make multiple punctures across the entire cautery site.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument; et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	This type of cautery moistens the brain equally, then apply cotton moistened with butter and chicken fat on top.
de l’awe des eulz	from eye ache
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When eye ache first arises from the signs I mentioned earlier in this section, you should begin by giving the patient things that clean out their head and guard against moisture while they sweat it out in the bath multiple times on an empty stomach.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai II cauteres sus les II temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as II eulz ensamble, ou en I se li dessendemens est en I; et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple; et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	Afterward, instruct the patient to cover their head and cauterize between the temples twice if eye ache descends into both eyes together or once if it descends into just one; then lance all the veins and arteries underneath the heart during the cautery and ensure that the cauteries are as long as the width of a temple; avoid excessive blood loss, and stem any blood flow if you see too much come out.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras; et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.	And I will teach you about the extraction of arteries and incision, with caution how to staunch it; sometimes one performs cautery or searing underneath the two rear bones.
dou cors des larmes	body of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors; et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz: I cautere emmi le chief, et II cauteres sus les II temples, et II cauteres ou haiterel desoz les II os; et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout I petit cautere.	When the tears of the eyes are old and accustomed to be on the veins or near the arteries that appear outside the head, one sees they are due to cold phlegmatic superfluities; then one performs the cautery as mentioned at the start for an illness descending into the eyes: I cautery within the head, II cauteries over the two temples, and II cauteries beneath the two rear bones; if more is needed, then one may carefully cauterize above the eyebrow with little cauteries.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	Through the body of tears from within the eyes
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide III nuis cochies; aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire; et fai II cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les II sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous; et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	When you treat him according to what we have said in the division, and he does not benefit, then give the patient to drink three nights cockspur; after raise his head, and make a cauterization in the middle of the olive-shaped bone; and do two cauterizations with the 'clavilis' cautery instrument on both temples, just below the hairline; and be careful of the artery so as not to cut it.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the shape of the 'clavilis' cautery instrument:
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	When the paper of the eye is softened by illness and moisture, then cauterize it with this cautery instrument called 'olivare'.
de coi ci est li forme:	Of which this is the form:
Et se tu vues si fai II cauteres sus les II sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont; et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if you see to make two cauterizations on the two eyebrows as long as the eyebrows are; and do not remove your hand until a third part of the paper is burned, according to the manner I have said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	on the hair that pricks the eye
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	Sometimes it happens that the eyelashes turn inwards and prick the eye, and for this a cauterization is made in two ways: either with fire or with burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain; aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz; puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When they are born and are even, then place the patient in your care; afterwards draw on the paper of the eyes a figure that is like the leaf of myrtle, and let the beginning of the sign be near the hairs; then apply cotton moistened with egg white and parsley poultice to the eye, then heat the cautery for which this is the form:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit; et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil; adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi III jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	After cauterizing the figure you have marked, do so little by little many times until the heart of the problem is burned away; and the sign of a successful treatment is that you see the paper retracting, and the hairs rising to the tip of the eye; then remove your hand, and leave it thus for three days, then apply cotton moistened with butter until the burning sensation is gone; afterwards treat with ointment until it heals.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	And if afterward the hairs grow back and the skin is softened again, then restart the cautery on that same spot as you did initially; and if the hair falls out, cauterize until the skin rises to its natural position, and it is even, without irritating the eye.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	The cautery of burning medicine is that you instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even, then make parchment in the shape of a myrtle leaf; take French soap and quicklime, each weighing 3 ounces, grind them together well; do this quickly so it doesn't cool down, spread on the mold you've made like a myrtle leaf, and place it over the skin around the eye(s); if the illness is in one eye only, work with one, but if both are affected; put some cotton dampened in egg white underneath the eye; let the patient's head be in your lap and rest your index finger on the medicine, pressing it down slightly and massaging gently every time the patient feels a stinging sensation from the medicine, for they will feel a sting like that of fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for some time, remove the medication with your hand.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	And when the inflammation has passed, lift up the wound site, and observe whether you see the flesh raised just as it was raised by the cautery or by incision; if so, then it is well.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If not, apply more medication to the place where it was opened by the previous treatment, until your work is even and your eyes are accurate; then place moist cotton wool soaked in butter until the burnt core falls out, after treat the wound with an ointment called 'dyafenis' or another, until it is healed.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And if it is necessary, ensure you are careful with your work through great vigilance so that none of the medication reaches the eyes.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	And if the paper becomes soft afterward, and the hairs prick in the eye, start over with the medicine on that softened spot, just like you did before; after the treatment is complete and the wound heals. This is the form of the myrtle leaf:
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	And know that the eyes of men are diverse in size and smallness, and according to this be your constraints; and let not the right path be abandoned by one who studies this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	on the treatment of fistula with cauterization
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat a fistula as we have described in the division of diseases, and your treatments are not effective, then it is necessary to perform cauterization in this manner.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	For the sick person, command him to place his head on your hand; hold his head between your hands in such a way that it cannot move or shift; then apply moist cotton wool soaked in egg white or parsley juice onto the eye; afterwards heat up the cautery which is shaped like an arch and together with this cauterization process; if you wish, point it from one end to another, so that it may resemble a tent; however, this arched shape is more useful for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	If the fistula is open, then press it and remove any pus, then dry it; if it is closed, operate on it and scrape away the bowels; afterwards apply a hot cautery shaped like this onto it, holding your hand over the cautery at the knuckle part above the eye so that you do not burn yourself; place the cautery into the fatty tissue of the eye, corrupting it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you cauterize down to the bone, it would be beneficial.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If not, resume the cautery once more, and repeat if needed, leaving it for three days. Afterward, apply moist cotton soaked in butter, and treat with a drying ointment until it heals. If forty days pass without healing, use corrosive medicine to expose the bone; then follow as directed in its chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	There is also a method for cauterizing fistulas, which none of the ancients mentioned.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	Open the fistula, then split the site. Afterward, place into the cleft a fine probe shaped like itself:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	and they make it to the quantity of a third of a pound; and hold your hand or chopstick firmly, and do not move the patient at all, so that the molten lead does not flow into his eye; and you must put on the patient's eye some wet cotton in egg white or yolk: the lead thus closes the place of the fistula, and the wound heals with marvellous health.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the fistula is healed by the cauterization we mentioned, it is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If not, you must administer an opening in the nail, and lead the fistula to the body of the nail according to what is necessary in its proper place.
des crevaices en levres	cracks in lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Very often cracks occur on lips which are called "hair", especially those of children.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe I petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these cracks as we have described in the section above, and the treatment does not work, then heat a small knife-shaped cautery according to this method:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	Place it on the cracks until it reaches the bottom; then treat the area with wax until it is healed.
de l’aposteme de la goule	the abscess of the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When an abscess forms at the root of the throat or in the tonsil, palate, or tooth roots, it becomes inflamed and painful and develops into a fistula; you treat it as we have described in the section above, but if this is ineffective: then you must use a cautery appropriate for the size of the fistula; insert the cautery through the opening of the fistula, keeping your hand steady until the hot iron reaches the base or rear end; do this once or twice after the treatment we have described in the section on treatments, continuing until it is healed; if it heals in this way, that is good; and if not, you must expose the area and remove any rotten bone, as you will find described in its respective chapter.
dou movement des dens	Of tooth movement
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you treat it with medicine but it doesn't work, then place the patient's head on your lap; afterward, heat the cautery that will be described here in such a way that you put a cane over the tooth; and place inside the hot cautery until the patient feels the heat reaching the root of the tooth; after lift your hand and resume the cauterization according to your desire; then have the patient fill their mouth with salty water, and hold it for an hour and rinse thoroughly.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	In this way, the moving tooth is confirmed to be stable, the softened gum restrained, and the corrupted moisture dried up.
de la dolor des dens	Of the pain of teeth
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When tooth pain arises due to coldness, whether it is cold or true, and medical treatments are ineffective, there is a need for cauterization in two ways: cautery with butter and fire cautery.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	Cautery with butter is such that you take cow's butter, and put a piece of it in an iron or bronze spoon; then take cotton and wrap it around the tip of a needle, dip it in boiling butter, and place it on the aching tooth until it cools down; do this often enough for its properties to reach the root of the tooth. If you wish, you can also moisten wool and cotton with cold butter, put it on the aching tooth, and apply hot iron so that heat reaches the end of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	The cautery with fire is such that you take a cane of iron or brass, and make it thick enough so the fire does not reach the patient's mouth; afterwards heat the cautery, from which the form will come after, and place it on the tooth and hold your hand there until the cautery has cooled down; do this often, for the pain will be gone that very day or the next.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And the patient should fill their mouth with good butter during the application of this cautery, and then let it cool afterwards; and here is the form of the cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	And make the cautery for whichever cheek you wish, according to your ability; and here is the form of the cane:
des scrophules	Of the scrofula
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	When scrofula is of phlegm and cold moisture, and it does not obey digestion by medicine, then heat the chimney cautery which comes with this form, and make two openings for the smoke to exit on the other side of the cautery; place the hot cautery on the abscess once or twice if needed until it reaches the base of the abscess; and if the abscess is small, use a cautery according to its size, leaving it for three days; then apply moist cotton with butter until the burning sensation subsides; afterward, treat the area with ointments and dressings until it heals.
Li forme de la cainne:	The shape of the cane:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	When moisture overcomes the channels of the lung, especially when it arises from cold constitution, then the patient must be emptied first with dissolving medicines; afterward cauterize at the root of the throat, and take care not to reach the throat, and only burn a little of the heart.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	After that, perform another cautery at the joint of the neck with the spine, and let the cauterization be done in a manner called "clavile" as described before; treat the area as mentioned earlier until it is healed.
de la toust	Of the cough.
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai ij cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis; et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	When any lung disease is caused by cold moisture, and the patient has no fever or drying out, and it's an old illness, then perform two cauterizations on the axilla in their armpits; and another cautery in the middle of the chest between the two breasts; let the cauterization be done as "clavile" according to the form described before.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles; et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	And if you see fit, perform the fire cautery by pricking with a needle, as previously described in treating ear diseases; and let there be thirty or so such pricks.
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	After treatment of the place according to what has been said before, let there be three rows of cauterization following this pattern:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais III a cop.	And because these cauterizations are lighter, you do three at a time.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	On the shoulder's dislocation:
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit; aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre; et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:	Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit; aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre; et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres; et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres; et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:	and cauterize the heart until it pierces through to the ribcage, and four cautery figures would appear; and for this, a cautery with three irons is used, therefore the pattern of cauterization consists of six cauteries; and the nerves follow according to the subtlety of a tent, and this is the shape of the cautery with three irons:
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce I nerf por coi il i a VIII cauteres.	and sometimes it is adjusted to this one nerve, thus there are eight cauteries.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil; aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	Afterwards, place the small cautery grinder on it; then let the patient rest, and do not move the limb for a long time until it is well strengthened.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	And if it is dislocated again soon after, then quickly perform a cautery on the thick part of the clavicle, or many cauteries in succession.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	For the joints are closed, and moisture is removed, and the patient is healed.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	When cold and excess moisture arise in the stomach to such an extent that they disrupt its natural balance, and catarrh is multiplied within it, and with customary treatments it does not improve, then it is necessary that the patient be recalled onto their back, extending their legs and hands.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture; et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	After that, make three cauterizations below the armpit with a spoon-shaped instrument to the depth of one finger, making each cautery claviform. Make two more cauterizations outside both sides [of the chest] so that the shape of the cauteries forms a triangle, and let there be such distance between one another that they are not joined together when they cast scurf; and let the cauteries be so perfect that they purify both parts of the heart, and let the figure of the cauterizations be according to this form without modification: [insert diagram]
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme; et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche; puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if you want to cauterize with a large cautery in the stomach according to this form; and whoever is afraid of this cautery, cauterize by pricking and bleeding on the stomach at one point according to the amount that you wish to use; then cauterize it completely with what is called a 'point' cautery.
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the treatment of the wound that we had before, until it is healed.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez; et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil; et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient; et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi; et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere; et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez; et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais; et c’est li forme:	When the liver is afflicted with pain from cold and moisture and excessive flatulence, it has been moved away from its natural condition by superfluities; and the patient is treated for this as we have said in our divisions, but it does not benefit them, so the patient must be reminded of their own nature; and apply three cauteries according to this form, figure, and quantity on the liver, outside the hypochondrium, where the ribs meet; and leave a space between each cautery equal to the thickness of a finger; and let the cauteries be along the length of the body, do not press your hand down too hard over the entire cautery; and only burn the outer half of the heart, and have the patient stand upright on their feet; and if they cannot, then let them lie down, extend their legs, and raise their arms; and this is the form:
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors; et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	And if your intention is to cauterize these knife cauteries, if you are skilled and wise in the art, be careful not to burn the entire heart, for you would dry out the whole body; and do not go near the throat, for the heart is very delicate there, and know this by experience.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile: s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort; et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	When there is an abscess in the liver, and you want to know if it is within the flesh of the liver or its membrane: if it is in the flesh, the patient will feel pain but not too severe; if it is in the membrane, they will experience intense pain.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste; et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	And when this treatment is appropriate for such cases, the patient should be reminded about it on their head; then bleed from that place where the abscess is located, and afterwards heat the cautery which resembles a ray, of which this is the shape:
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers; aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez; et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	Et cauterize at the cautery until the heart is burned, and it reaches syphac, so that all the pores are open; afterward cure according to the cure of eschars until it is healed; and no one should use this cautery but those who have studied long in the art of medicine, and by whose hands these illnesses have been corrupted at times.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	Then he may operate boldly, and yet it seems to me that one is better off leaving them alone.
dou cautere de pleuresin	sinew cautery.
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et II cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et I cautere emmi le pis, et I autre sus l’estomac, et I entre II espaules, et II as II costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre II espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	The ancients said that one must make sinew cauteries of aristoloche roots, and in this way: take an aristoloche root which is long, the largest you can find; let it be dry, also as thick and as long as your finger; moisten it with oil, then take it to the fire, and cauterize a cautery between the carotid artery and the neck, and two small cauteries slightly down in the part that is below the beard; two cauteries between the fifth rib and the sixth rib, leaning backwards a little bit; one cautery in the middle of the abdomen, another on the stomach, one between two shoulder blades, and two at the sides of the abdomen outside the cautery which is between the shoulder blades; do not press your hand hard but do this gently as if you were smelling something.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	And some ancient experts said that people use fire cautery similar to the razor, they heat it and place it between the ribs until it reaches the abscess, and removes the pain as we have mentioned in the liver abscess.
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	But in this work there is fear that the patient may die now or develop a fistula which cannot be cured.
de la mice	From the nose.
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent III manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you treat the disease from the nose as we have said in the treatment sections, and it does not improve, then there are three types of cautery that are all good.
Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant; et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos; et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule; et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.
