si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	Insert into the first incision the instrument that is called a "cultellaire," which is very sharp on one side and soft but not sharp on the other, and it has this form:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	Place the sharp side of the instrument towards the flesh above the scalp and the soft side towards the bone, and insert it until it reaches the middle incision.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And clear out all the vessels that descend from the head to the eyes as long as the incision is continuous up until it appears below the scalp, and then do likewise in the middle incision down to the other outside edge; then extract the blood equally, and press the area for the blood to be released; next place into each incision a tent of old cotton, and apply onto soft cloths soaked in wine and oil and egg white, and ensure that no hot abscesses form; on the third day remove the binding, and apply plenty of warm water, then treat with basilicon ointment along with rose oil, and other treatments used for wounds until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	For the kingdom of eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When someone has chronic catarrh with a habit of coughing, and you see their eyes sunken and small, and their vision weakening, and the membranes burning; and hair falls out, and on the head it causes painful sores, and the patient sneezes; then through these symptoms know that this matter and catarrh comes from many veins, and the disease is cured in this way.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And so you instruct the patient to raise their forehead, then make a large incision in the middle of the forehead, and another from the wide eye socket.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	Beginning at the incision of the left temple to the right temple, and let it be an incision down to the bone; keep your hand away from the nerves of the temples that move during eating; and when the bone is exposed, then wipe all blood with a sponge, and then separate between the two lips of the incision and place old cotton there, and tented linen; then bind above with cloths moistened in wine and oil, taking care to avoid hot abscesses; once it is removed, you must rub the bone until flesh begins to grow, then treat it with drying agents that promote flesh.
En teil maniere: pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this manner: take two parts wheat flour and four parts colophony, make a plaster of it; administer to these wounds for the generation of flesh throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	The cleaning of ears.
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All that falls into the ears is one of four things: grain, beast, mineral stone or similar such as iron; seed, like beans, peas and pulses; or flowing matter such as water and oil and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When stone or other matter that does not fit nor grow in the ear falls into it, expose the ear to sunlight.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see the stone, drop a little violet oil or sesame oil and extract it; have him sneeze using condiments, and block his nose as he sneezes, then cover the ear with cloth or wool; finally expose the ear to sunlight.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	Very often fire is used in this treatment; if it does not work, proceed to the extraction with subtle pincers, which are shaped like this:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it is drawn with the pincers, it is good; if not, proceed to the extraction with a subtle small-bladed hook; and if that does not work, make a cane of brass and insert the end into the ear canal strongly, plugging what surrounds the cane with soft wax so that air cannot enter alongside the cane; then apply strong suction, for very often it comes out by suction as we have said; and if it does not come out in this way, take some bird lime and place on its surface an instrument which is sharp to accomplish this, and put a piece of cotton around; press the bird lime onto the stone or whatever object it may be, then apply suction.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if she cannot be cured of all these things that we have said, then hasten to split the ear rather than let a hot abscess come, and spasms; the manner of the incision is such that you first draw off the patient's cephalic blood, and remove blood according to its measure and strength, then make the patient sit between your hands and turn their ear upwards, and make a small incision in the root of the ear at the fatty place below it; let this incision be like a crescent moon, so as to reach the stone, then extract it according to your power, and suck it hastily into your mouth; treat the wound until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if this is a grain which has grown and it swells up, then administer an evacuation; and if it cannot be removed, then use the following thin, subtle spatula in this form.
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	And prepare an incision for that grain.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not do this when you think the grains are moist due to the moisture of the ear, until you have made many incisions; then extract them with delicate pincers and by suction, as we have said, so that the extraction is eased.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In the water that falls into the ear, the patient should first use sneezing remedies and fill the ear with old cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And lie on that same ear where the water is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If it should jump out because of this, it is good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	If not, take many stones according to the length of your thumb and light, and warm them slightly over a fire; place them in the patient's ear opening, and jump on it with your feet from the other side, pressing another stone onto the stone that is in the ear; do not stop doing this stone by stone until all the water has come out, and thus let it jump out completely; if you wish, take a reed, and put one end of it into the ear, while holding the other end over fire until the tip of the reed burns; then remake another with other reeds until all the water comes out, as we have said about stones.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	For the removal of the beast, if it is small-bodied, like a flea and similar things, treat it as we have said in the division; but if it is large-bodied so that one can feel it, then prepare for an extraction with pincers; this thing is lighter to remove than any other from the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	When extracting worms embedded in the ears, if you treat it as we have said in the division and the treatment of distillations but find no relief, then you must examine the ear in the sunlight: if any worm appears, pluck them with fine pincers; if none appear, take the following measures according to this form:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And [the ear] is narrow underneath but wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	And insert the most subtle probe into the ear according to the extent of the patient's suffering, then suck it firmly along the entire canal; do this often until all the wax comes out.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And if they do not obey and come out, then plug the canal with cotton as I have said for stones; and if they do not exit as we have said, so administer distillations that the ancients have proven in the extraction of worms, and you will find this in the treatise on distillations; and distil your oils and medicines into the ear using this instrument, which is formed like so:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And it is made of silver or brass with a narrow tube below and an overhanging top for distillation; and to press the distillation into the instrument, use a well-made brass tool designed for this purpose, and if you wish, take a razor and wrap cotton around its tip; then pour your oil or juice, and whatever medicine you choose from among those mentioned above, into the canal, which is in the ear; then insert the razor with all the cotton inside, and press your hand firmly so that the oil is distilled to the very end of the ear; and let the patient feel it within, and keep the distillation pot moderately warm over the fire rather than hot, for we distill it into the ear; and be careful it is not too cold, as this would make the medicine less effective.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the stuffing of ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without an opening in their ears; and this same thing happens to men due to the stuffing of a wound or wax within the ear, and these stuffings sometimes become embedded inside the ear, so one cannot see them; and at other times it occurs outside the opening, and can be seen clearly.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	That which becomes embedded and cannot be seen is difficult to treat in many situations, and for that which you can see, it is necessary that you place the ear of the patient towards the sun; look inside: if you see an apparent opacity, perform this operation with all these instruments as follows:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And let it be sharp and cutting from the front to the back without any roughness, so that it does not cut the ear; if the opacity is due to wax or flesh of the ear, then take subtle pincers, and remove it lightly until all the wax is gone.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the obstruction is complete in the ear, take a subtle light razor and warm it slightly over fire, then place it in the body of the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you sense an obstruction which the patient feels itching to hear, pierce lightly, and ensure you do not damage the nerves of the ear; then place in the ear a tent according to the width of the hole, and moist it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do not do this on any day when the wound is still open, instead take a tent and dampen it in rose water, and sprinkle it with ground vitriol; and if you see the ear swelling, then you must remove the tent and replace it with another tent moistened in an ointment made of almond oil and wax, until the swelling subsides; then treat it until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if bleeding occurs, immerse a sponge and cloth in cold water, place it on the ear, and employ other treatments that stop the bleeding as described in the section on distillations.
de la char des papieres	Of the paper's flesh.
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	These eye salves that come in paper containers when they are moist and dry out, you must stretch them with tongs and pincers, and cut off the head of a spathilla from its roots; then place powdered vitriol on the affected area.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if any remains after the cortex is removed, then cauterize it with a subtle lenticular cautery, and the cauterizer after incising should be moved; and often it must be repeated, as some part of its roots may remain; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned away and do not return.
de la gresle	Of the hail
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Many times on paper there appear things that seem like hail in their form and hardness, and for this reason, the illness is called "grandine," which is a thick accumulation of moisture above and below the paper; its treatment is as follows: pay attention to whether the grandine shifts from one side to another, and it's easy to tell. Cut it open, then peel away each part lightly with pincers, then cut off that portion.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	If you can't cut it without piercing the paper somewhat, there is no harm to the patient; and if the crack is large, bring it together with a suture, treat it until it's healed; and if it's small, do not use force, for the ointments will heal it quickly and stimulate flesh.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the earwax is descending into the inner ear toward the upper part, turn it upside down, grasp and hold with forceps; then extract the wax from one side to another; even if the membrane is damaged by incising it, there will be no harm; once the wax is extracted, irrigate the area with salt water, and treat the wound until the patient heals.
de la graisse des eulz	From the fat of eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	Exinach is a fat that accumulates on the eye's cornea; this condition occurs more frequently in children than adults and causes severe irritation to their eyes, resulting in morning catarrh and an inability to look at sunlight due to tears rapidly welling up in their eyes; because of this, they lie face-downward and sleep with their corneas beneath their eyebrows moistened by the exudate that has covered their appearance and is visible in the eye.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the place with your fingers, feel the dislocation between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	The manner of the operation is such that the patient puts his head on your palm; then take a linen cloth and prepare a tent-like structure in a circle according to the extent of dislocation from each part, then place it over them; press with your fingers from one side to another so that the dislocated parts are assembled within the circle; then make an incision through the moist flesh using a sharp spatula, but let it not be larger than the wound made when opening a vein; and cut the skin perfectly until you reach the dislocation; in many cases the dislocation appears as a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Extract it then all in one piece of cloth padded between your two fingers on the outside, and turn your hand to right and left until it is spread; and be careful not to approach the gap, so that you do not reach the spatumile at all up to the eye, lest you injure it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	If the splinter does not appear at the beginning of the gap, then slightly increase the gap gently until it appears; then extract it as we have said, then moisten the cloths with vinegar and water, and place them on the site, and bind tightly.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And for those people who grind willow and apply it to corrupt the moisture that remains.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat it until it is healed.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it reaches the warm abscess place, then treat it with soothing plasters until it is healed.
des poilz des papieres	The hairs of paper.
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc IIII manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When hairs grow on paper that are not natural and are left unattended, they harm the eyes, causing various ailments such as accustomed tears, softening of the papers, and albuginea, leading to eye destruction; this ailment is treated in four ways: by cauterization with fire, or with appropriate medication according to what was mentioned before in the chapter on cauterization, and it can be done through incision and suturing or with cannulas, as I will explain.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	Place the patient's head on your lap, then turn the paper of the eye with your left hand; if it is converted, that's good; otherwise, insert a needle with a thread throughout and near the margin where the hair grows; draw the thread across the whole paper over the unwanted hairs, then shave [them] off using a razor; next make an incision underneath the paper under the unwanted hairs along its entire length from the large tear duct to the small one; then remove the thread, and place beneath the paper a small tent made of cotton and cloth; then cauterize over the paper with a shape of enchea, like that of the myrtle leaf, but make sure the shape is according to the amount you want to raise the paper which is divided into parts.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	Et si a teil qui a mestier c'on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; 
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then cut this top part with small equal forces according to the form which is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you are unable to hold the forceps, and the thing is not equal, then take a needle with thread, place it between your fingers; insert one thread near the large lobe, and another thread near the small (one), and bring together both threads equally between your two hands; lift your hand equally, and lift all the skin on which you have worked, as we have explained, then join the two lips of the wound with stitches, treating it until it is healed; if an abscess appears in your incision, calm it down with a cerate and similar soothing ointments; sometimes it happens that the hair on the paper is converted: so you must use what we have said about incisions; but the stitches (are) more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The cure of scurvy is done in this way: you must fold the paper and make a slit in it according to what I have said, then make two canes by art, and two subtle threads as long as the paper and as wide as the thickness of the spatula; cut at the two ends of the two parts where you hold the thread; then assemble one with the other subtly on that which is above the paper of the eye, and stretch the two canes from the two formed sides; leave it like this for a few days, and the skin which is stretched will die and blacken and rot until it falls off by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it takes time, apply some force to it, then treat until it is healed; and when the wound is sealed, remove the paper, and the hairs will no longer be plucked; this is how you make two canes according to this figure, and with these dimensions of length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	li ovraiges est telz  that you take a subtle needle, and in it put a soft and subtle silk thread; then gather the heads and knot one to the other subtly, and let the length of the threads be a palm's width long; then arrange another fine silk thread lightly into the shaft, and tie off the ends of the thread; then have the patient place their head on your hand; and it should be near sunlight so that the operation is illuminated, for this is delicate work requiring small movements, then push the needle through to the base of the hair follicle adjacent, and pierce right through the skin quickly until you reach the natural hair layer; then extract the hairs one by one from the shaft, and place them back into the shaft, if there are 1 or 2 or 3 or more; then draw your hand away so that the hairs come towards the shaft along with the natural hairs.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the arrowhead is treated and the hairs do not come out with it, you will extract the arrow from below along its entire length that you have determined, until the arrow comes out of the hole above and you see it by the sight of the eye; then you will pull out the arrow and the thread, and close the eye and leave it closed for two or three days, until the hair dries in its place and flesh grows over it; if the hairs are small, accompany one long natural hair with them, and let it be raised with that one, until they are elongated, then lift it.
de la porriture de l’oil	Of the corruption of the eye
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this disease which is called "aleacrati" or corruption comes to the eye, it has two manners: one natural, and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it occurs suddenly due to wounds or incisions, from cauterization, and similar procedures.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the method of treatment involves cutting into the wound, separating its lips, and placing linen tents inside, binding it until it heals; one must not use drying or constricting agents in this cure.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	For if you do that, the illness will return worse than before; instead, use softening agents such as fenugreek; cook flax seeds and water or wine in a pot, add melted diakylon ointment to oil, wrap it in a linen tent, and treat with this preparation.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the secret of your cure lies in ensuring it does not heal according to its original form; these treatments we have described are merely temporary measures against this illness, preventing its return to its previous state.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the flesh which comes to the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease that is inflammation, truly called "axacrati", and it is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	The accident comes from a wound and tear and cauterization and similar things; and the way to treat it is that you take a needle with double thread in it, insert it into the flesh, pierce through from left nostril towards right, so that the threads come out of both eyes, then stretch the flesh above the whole needle and cut it with a spatula that is one finger wide.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the shape on the paper returns as it should, that is good; but if not, take a razor and place it in the tear, turn the paper over, and make two cuts along its edge inside the paper; let the ends of these two cuts be at the two corners of the incision you have cut, and make angles so that when they are put together, the shape is like that of a letter with the name "Greek"; then remove this flesh according to how much its sides extend below what follows the paper, and join the two parted parts, sewing them with a thread of wool; then treat it with what we have said about softening medicines and bandages until it heals.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the illness arises from a tear or a seam or cauterization, you must make an incision full of hairs on the papery skin beneath it, and according to what has been said before; then separate between the two layers of skin with a tent, as I have mentioned; and one must perform this operation based on the form of the illness, for it is very diverse in shape, and wise master physicians devise all sorts of devices with all their power to make the figure return to its natural form; and even sick people themselves, according to what kind of treatment and instruments they require in many ways.
dou soudement de la papiere	suddenly from the papery skin
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this suturing occurs in men's hands in such a way that the papery skin is stuck together with the white of the eye, and it cannot move or perform its natural functions, you must therefore put the tip of a razor under the paper and lift it upwards; then stretch it with pincers until you cut off what is hard with the subtle spatula, which should not be too sharp nor too cutting so that the patient does not suffer from the spatula being too sharp hurting their eye; and make your incision where you peel away this assembly lightly, so that the paper returns to its natural form; and heal all of this assembly, sometimes pouring saline solution into the eye, then rinsing it with warm water and colloidal silver; afterwards place a linen tent between the skin and the eye, and put moist wool on the eye soaked in egg white; and after three days use colloidal silver and hot compresses until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	Of the eyelash's nail
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	The nail is of two kinds: it is nervous and similar to the hard surface, and another that is not nervous but resembles white frozen moisture, which when touched with iron cannot be pierced by pincers; both types begin near the large tear duct and grow little by little until they cover all vision, light, and movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	The method of incision is as follows: have the patient lay their head upon your lap, and open their eyes; lift up the eyelid with your hand, then coil the nail around pincers made from small blades, and stretch it upwards; take a needle, attach to it horsehair, or cow or ox hair, along with strong thread; double over the tip of the needle slightly and insert it into the nail, piercing through entirely with the needle, then tie the nail up with thread and pull it upwards, scraping away all the hairs alongside the edge of the nail that adhere to the eyelid and eyelashes until reaching the head, then excise the remainder at the root near the tear duct using a very fine spatula and small forceps, leaving natural flesh around the tear duct so that bodily fluids from tears can still pass through the incision; sometimes one only stretches out the nail with onion juice and thread as we have said previously; then scrape away all with a fine spatula such that it looks like this:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And be careful that the spatule does not touch and tear the fleshy membrane, and that the plumule is not pierced; after making the incision, throw into the eye a pinch of crushed seal, and some collar made of litharge, leaving it until the next day; then cure him with what he needs until it heals.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not nervous and you cannot insert the needle, and the uncines cannot enter, this type of nail is often treated by medicines; and they arise as I have described in the section, and if you see it cut, operate on the patient's eye, and take a light, sharp spatule like this:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And lift the nail carefully, and if you see that it does not decrease in size and the reason presses, then from your mouth, drip into the eye some collar made of litharge, red copper, and crushed seal, and plug the eye until the next day; then begin again this other operation according to this same procedure until it is completely removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing is contrary to the eye, such as a hot abscess, then milk it and treat first the hot abscess until it is healed, then resume the work as before until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of flesh in the eyelid harms the eye greatly, then suspend it with a hook and cut off a part but not all to prevent tears from coming out; then instill into the eye red colloidal solution made of litharge.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of flesh that grows over the pupil
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	In some men's eyes, red flesh sometimes grows and covers the pupil, restricting their vision, resembling a rose petal; in this case you put his head on your lap, open up the eyes, then remove all of that flesh with appropriate hooks, supporting it forcefully; cut away the first piece of flesh and continue shaving off all the rest down to the end, taking care not to injure the eye during treatment; use a spatule as described before for nail incisions and small levers to remove sebaceous material, just like this chapter illustrates; once incision is complete and all flesh removed, fill up the eye with boiled silk or instill red colloidal solution along with similar corrosive medicines, then place cotton soaked in egg white on top of the eye so as to secure it from hot abscesses; if there's no remaining tissue left but instead a warm blood flow that you suspect may be an abscess, leave the eye alone and treat the suspected abscess using soothing remedies for abscesses; return later once healed up again, repeat until all flesh similar in this way has been readjusted within the eye.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But nevertheless, you must ease the treatment of each weak eye according to its natural way; and in the case of an accidental injury involving iron, do not put your hand into any of these treatments until you see that this limb can withstand such a procedure.
des voines des eulz	the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	These red veins that are visible under the eye hinder vision and weaken the eye every day.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary for you to first examine the eye and determine if this redness is the only issue and there are no other diseases present apart from the redness; then treat it in such a way: instruct the patient to place their head into your lap, then gently press on these veins all around according to your knowledge, and let your fingers be very gentle doing so twice following this form:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	And they are two inches apart by degrees inside the body according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then one coils the forceps around those veins carefully, and removes the blood hour after another, until you see those veins move away from the eye; and be careful not to injure the eye with the tips of the spatulas, and perform this work at midday in front of the sun, being very hot in your work so that you cut only those veins; and when you have done this, then instil into the eye green and red collyrium to corrupt that which remains from the ciliary body.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you are unable to take all of it in that hour, then make a plaster over the eye with things that soothe the pain of the eyes, and leave it for some days until the pain is eased and there is assurance of warm abscess, then begin again according to this method which is given above until it is healed; and this is the form of the forceps:
de la fistule de l’oil	Of the eye's fistula
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The surgeon calls this "arissati" fistula: when you treat it with cauterization and burning medicine as I have previously stated, and it is not healed, then there is pus inside that you must open over the abscess, where it should die, and drain all the moisture until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is exposed, and you see the corruption and blackness, then remove all the instrument of which this has the form; and it is called "rough head", and should be made of iron until its head returns, and be pointed like a file as it is in the present shape.
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And place on the location of the corrupted bone, then turn it between your two fingers, and press your hand gently until you know that corruption has ceased; do this several times, then restore the area with drying medicine.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	if the flesh is welded and hair grows there, and the body of the bowel is also welded, and remains so for forty days without renewal or abscess formation, and no harmful accident occurs, know that it is healed; if not, then there is another remedy to bring the fistula back to the navel opening according to this procedure: it is necessary to uncover the bone a second time with an iron instrument and sharp medicines, and when it is uncovered take one chisel shaped like this, which has three angles, and the handle should be tapered until the point as you see here
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	then place it on the bone near the ridge, keep your hand an inch away from his eye, then turn the handle round until it pierces through the bone and he feels air passing through as you hold your hand over his navel; after restoring the position with dry medicines, as I have taught you, when the flesh grows back and the hair hardens, the matter will return to the navel; this is an easier course of treatment for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	From the eye socket.
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eye is open from all around and there is no obstruction of the nose or narrowing, you must bind the patient; then treat, and then apply cups or leeches without injury to suck; then place on the eye a poultice made of aconite, aloe, incense, and gum mastic; then withdraw the eye, and place the plaster over with bandages and soft cloths; and the manner of these cloths is such that you take soft cloths, each folded four times, and then place one upon another according to the amount the eye needs; then bind firmly above with a hard bandage, and repeat the cups to suck without injury; then remove the cups and leave the eye withdrawn day and night, and if the bindings loosen, you must tighten them greatly; then remove the bindings after daytime and nighttime, and if you see the eye healing, it is good; if not, then repeat the plaster, cloths, bindings, and cups until it heals.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	From rupture of dry skin
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When disruption occurs in the dry skin, it opens up and produces pus like resin grains, and is terrible to behold; if you see it breaking open, the procedure is such that you insert a needle into the root of the lower eyelid until reaching the upper part, then insert another needle with double thread at the lash line; make it pierce through, leaving the first needle in place; remove the double-threaded part and tie a piece of dry skin around it, tightening well, then withdraw the needle and apply moist woolen cloth dipped in egg white; leave until the threads contract along with the dry skin, then treat the eye with comforting substances until the wound is healed; sometimes the wound is constricted by the dry skin on both sides with a circle of cloth until it heals.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eyes appear to have great inflammation, pierce them with a thin spatula that reaches deep into the eye, drain the white moisture and lower the eyes, and enter immediately thereafter; then extract it once it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	of the bow of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This disease, called "alcunnati", is nothing but the bow of the eye that gathers in the eye, resembling descending water, and it is not water; and the manner of its appearance works such that you should have the patient sit on a chair with a straight back, then take their head between your two hands, moving it until you see the bow rise above your eyes; then let it be pierced, and do not lower or block the light, and the patient will see things as they used to; and if it does not descend below, know that it is water, and if the descent of the bow is not arranged as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you seat the patient between your hands, then take the subtle spatule and make an incision on the horny tissue one inch long along the continuation of the conjunctive with the horny tissue and the crown, until the bowels exit; when they do, instill into the eye warm water mixed with honey or boiled fenugreek and honey, then cure it with another cure until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	Water from the eyes.
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have found similar water in the incision, and what is needed to pierce it; we act according to healthiness.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	Have the patient sit between your crossed hands, away from light so that they do not see the sun, and bind their healthy eye tightly; place the paper of the affected eye in your left hand if it is the left eye, or your right hand if it is the right eye; then take with your right hand (if the eyes are left) or your left hand (if the eyes are right), the instrument called "almagda"; position the tip of the instrument alongside the crown, as wide as a line at that bright spot of the eye where the lower tear duct ends, and push the "almadga" instrument forcefully, turning your hand until it pierces through into the brightness of the eye; ensure the length of the almadga is exactly matching the depth from the plum to the end of the pupil, which constitutes the crown of the eye; then you will see bone in that paper due to the clarity of the horny tissue, and can place the instrument up until where the water is, and express it through another opening.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If the water drains now, the patient sees before them and an instrument in their eye.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After resting briefly, and if the water rises again through the second route, place fire with the instrument, and when it is firmly fixed and does not rise, extract the almagda lightly by turning your hand back and forth; then replace a piece of seal gem in the water, and remove this from within the eye.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then apply oil-soaked gauze or wet linen to the eye from outside, and bind it with a healthy eye.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	We, and those of our time, apply ground cumin with plenty of egg on it.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the ointment cannot enter the eye due to its hardness, as there are such men who have very hard eyes, then you must take the instrument known as 'alberit', of which this is the form:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	Pierce only the conjunctiva then, and do not go too deep, but make it a subtle incision; then put in the ointment as we have said; and upon completion of this work provide for the patient an appealing bed, where he can sleep on his back in a dark place; and remain still from all movement, and take light foods, and do not move their head to the right or left, and be bound according to his disposition until the third day; then untie them in that same dark room, and test their vision, and let them see certain things, and then re-bind them for seven days; and it is not good that you perform this during the hour of treatment nor after incision just now, but rather wait until later so as to avoid an ascent of moisture.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	If an abscess becomes hot, you must remove the eye before the seventh day, and treat it according to the method used for abscesses; once it is healed, release your gaze and apply some ointment to cover it for a day, then remain in that dark room thereafter.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	Leave that dark room slowly, step by step, and gradually adapt to your surroundings; know that no disciples should interfere in this process.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And then someone came to us from Iberia who told us that in his country they make a perforated alembic for sucking out water, but I have never seen any such thing in our land and nor do I read about it in the ancient books; perhaps this is something new.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the appearances of the shapes of almagda, so that those who do not know them may see them; and they should be made properly from bronze.
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And let the head of the ears be made from this same subtle material, while the back end is in three sharp corners.
de la char sor le neis	over the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	There are times when nails of various sizes grow close together, so that some appear like scorpions with many feet; and if there be such where the nail is adorned with different colours, or has soft skin in one colour.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	In the case of these soft nails which are not adorned, you must make the patient sit between your hands facing the sun; and open their nostrils, then blow on those nails, pulling them hard; then cut what you can sustain with a slender sharp spade, until you know that this nail is entirely removed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if any part remains that cannot be cut away, open it with all the subtle instruments lightly so that nothing is left behind; and if it overwhelms you, or the abscess is hot, then treat it as necessary; and if it is malignant abscesses, hurry and cauterize until the blood has stopped flowing and all the flesh is removed, then apply either cold water or wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If the water flows and moisture reaches up to the palate, know that it is healing; and if the moisture does not drain properly, understand that there is uncut flesh on top of the bone where your tools cannot reach: in this case you must insert a thread of linen slightly thicker than normal into his nose until reaching its furthest end, then tie each end with your own hands leaving about an inch or less between knots; have the patient hold one end of the thread at their nostril and pull it out through their mouth while sniffing until it comes out; many schoolchildren do this, which is easy for those who wish to try it; finally, take the piece that came out from the nose with one hand and the other part coming out of the mouth with your other hand and pull them apart carefully by the knots.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Do this so that you know that the worms have corrupted that flesh, then draw out the son, wipe away the blood, and moisten the thread with Egyptian ointment, and replace it in the nose as before; do this for three days or more, until the ointments corrode all remaining flesh; and then place a leaden tube in the nose for some days until it is healed, and if there is need of drying medicines, use them; and this is the form of the instrument to cleanse the head, into which one distils oils and medicines.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And let it be of silver or brass, resembling an open lamp, like a tube, and its conduct is also so; and if you wish, make a closed tube, and let the instrument be full for cleansing the head; and have one handle at the head to hold it when one heats oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	From the flesh above the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Often a disease arises on the head of the nose called 'telul', and it grows and becomes large over time, becoming an unsightly thing to behold; for this you must cut it out at its beginning, and remove it entirely, then apply either cauterization or burning medicine; if one waits too long to cut it while it is still small, take heed if it is hard, of dark color, and has poor sensation: do not touch it with iron, as it is an entrenched abscess, for when it is cut once, great harm comes to the patient; but if the abscess is soft to the touch, not of dark color, and you see that it can be entirely removed, then purge the patient and remove it without fear, and treat the area with drying and constrictive agents.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the nose is cut and sewn [back] up.
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Know that when the cartilage-related work of this chapter continues for a long time, it provides little benefit, except in some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is necessary then, when this happens to any man, to examine if the wound is fresh and full of blood; and accordingly, align the two lips [of the wound] for suturing, then treat it until it heals; and if the lips are already separated on both sides, you must remove all heart tissue from the parts that bleed, then bring together the two lips for suturing, hold them in place, and dust with powdered dragon's blood and ground frankincense; and place upon the powders a piece of strong emplastrum [a type of plaster] or another sealing ointment, leaving it until it dries by itself, then treat with an ointment until healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of suturing is as follows: you bring together the edges by needles, as we have said in abdominal suturing; or with thread, as I made known to you.
des apostemes des levres	From the lips of apostems.
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	Men with hard apostems inside the lips, similar to grains of wheat, smaller and larger; then you must turn back the lips, and cut open each one, take them with pincers and crush in each part; then apply finely ground vitriol powder after the incision until the blood stops; and then leave it uncovered, and treat the area with dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	On the flesh of the gums.
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times a fleshy growth appears on the gums, which the ancients call "albulus"; you must hold it with tongs and cut it at its root, allowing the bowel or blood to pass; then apply crushed vitriol or other restraining and drying powders; if this flesh grows back after incision, and often does so, cut it a second time and cauterize: it will not return after cauterization; these are the forms of the instruments for cutting.
