des sordens	Of wounds
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes excrescences are gathered at the root of teeth inside the mouth between the gums, scabs that are ugly and rough; sometimes the tooth is black or yellow-green and putrid, so much so that corruption reaches the gum, and the tooth stinks; you must have the patient sit in your lap with his head in your hands, then pull out these excrescences or scabs until there's nothing left; do this for the dark ones, the greenish ones, the yellow ones, and other defects until they're cleaned up; if you remove what causes this at first instance it is good; but if not, start over on the second and third days until everything has been removed; know that teeth require various forms of instruments to clean depending on the job, since the reamer used for cleaning outside the teeth has a different form than the one used inside them; these shapes should be with you fully equipped.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you treat the tooth for its pain that you delay extracting as much as possible, because this should not be done; it is a very high structure until such time as one has no excuse to remove it.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Then when the patient is compelled to extract, you must be certain of the tooth causing pain.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Many times the pain may deceive the patient, and they think it is in a healthy tooth, leading to extraction of a good tooth; however, the pain does not subside because the real issue remains, as we have already seen with these sufferers; and when you are certain of the offending tooth, you must scrape all around it with a strong spatula to protect the gums from all sides; then grasp it in your fingers or delicate forceps at the first hole and extract, ensuring it is well loosened, then firmly hold the forceps; let the patient's head be in your lap between your knees, holding it still.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After extracting the tooth properly without breaking it, and if there is no fracture, take one of these instruments and gently insert it into each side, moving it like you did before.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the tooth is perforated and worn down, you must fill it with small pieces of cloth where the holes are; gently grasp it with forceps so as not to break it when extracting; and be very careful working around the gums to loosen the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	Take care not to break it during extraction, leaving any part behind, as this can cause the patient greater pain due to the root's cunning nature.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	Beware not to act like the ignorant surgeon who, due to their haste and boldness, sometimes breaks the jawbone, failing to manage what we have described; instead, they bring about severe ailments due to roots left behind or a broken jaw, as we often witness; once the tooth is removed, clean the area with wine or oil and silk; if there's bleeding, which often happens, fill the place with powdered vitriol; if this doesn't work, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the instruments, with which one loosens teeth first, should have long points and thick handles so that they do not bend when you extract the tooth. And these are the forms/shapes/patterns:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And they should have thick handles so that they do not bend when pulling (the tooth), and they should be well-made iron, and toothed in order to hold it firmly.
de la racine des dens	From the root of the teeth.
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains after extraction, it is necessary that you place moist cotton mixed with butter on the site for one or two days.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	Until the site is softened, you can insert pincers called "algefri", which resemble a bird's beak; they should be shaped like this (inside) as well as a file, and this is their form/shape/pattern:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to emerge from all these tongs, you must uncover the flesh all around the root and insert the instrument known as "althali", which is a plainch, of which this is the form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And let it be thick and strong so that it does not break, and if the root jumps through this [process], then it is good. If not, you will use all the tools, which are as follows in form:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one requires assistance from this tool with two prongs, of which this is the form:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other iron tools which are placed in front of the teeth, and from this tool resembling large tongs, of which this is the form:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And let these instruments be durable and unbreakable, and know that there are many dental instruments; and also other instruments which aren't mentioned; the wise subtle masters find their own instrument by themselves according to what their works and the illness require because in cases of illnesses where ancient doctors did not mention any instrument for it due to its diversity and if one bone doesn’t break nor decays, then they search for the corresponding instrument that is needed as I told you before and this is a help with gestures which are made like this:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	They should be thick and strong to hold the bone securely so it doesn't slip away but can be held and removed; then restore its place with appropriate medicine, and if there is decay in the bone, which is small, treat it entirely with this instrument.
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the teeth appear not according to their natural form, and their shape is ugly, especially in virgin women, you must know if the tooth has grown after the others and is not in its proper place, and it cannot be treated or filed: then you shall cut it; and if it is connected with another tooth, take this instrument which here we present to you, whose form resembles a small beak, and make sure that its end is sharp made of iron.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And hit it repeatedly with a hammer many times to harden the tooth, and to avoid moving others, and if it is visible enough that you can file it, then use this kind of lime as shown here.
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	Which is like a needle lime; and file the tooth gently many times so that it does not move until it is worn out; then smoothen it at the end with any kind of rasp, and if the tooth is too sharp and hurts your tongue, you must level its roughness as much as needed to avoid hurting your tongue or corrupting speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the tooth wanes
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the front tooth wanes, either by percussion or by falling, and the patient cannot press down on it while eating without causing it to fall out, and you have treated it with constrictive medicine, but this is ineffective; in such a case one must secure the teeth using a golden wire, for silver wire turns green and rots, whereas gold never changes; and the wire should be neither too thin nor too thick, according to the space between the teeth; if you wish to align the teeth, then take the wire and pass it double-fold between two sound teeth, then place the wavering tooth or teeth between them, until you have brought the sound tooth on one side into contact with another; afterwards repeat this process of covering over until reaching the part where you began, drawing your hand gently but firmly so that nothing moves out of place, securing it at the root of the tooth in such a way as to prevent escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then cut the shoulder's head with a thread using pincers, and join them together, then reposition it between healthy teeth without damaging the tongue; leave in this tight position as long as possible, if loosened or wire twisted, tighten again with another piece of thread so that it stays put. This can serve as an example for how to fix two healthy teeth and two loose ones - as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	When a tooth falls out, put it back in its place gradually as we mentioned; don't let anyone interfere who isn't knowledgeable and patient; sometimes one makes an artificial tooth from cow bone and places it where the missing one should be before securing it like we said so that it stays for long periods of time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	To cut loose the tongue's bond
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	This bond sometimes comes from beneath the tongue by nature, one is born this way; or it can occur due to a healed wound; and the treatment involves opening the patient's mouth, placing their head in your lap, lifting their tongue; then cut through the broad nerve-bond, so that the tongue is freed from its socket, and if there is any hardness or knot, which comes suddenly after injury, thrust in the hook and sever that bond widely; be careful not to make the incision too deep because of the artery underneath; once you've done this, wash the area with rosewater and oil, or cold water, then place a linen tent beneath the tongue; have the patient hold this each night so that the wound cannot heal.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if there is bleeding, apply crushed vitriol to the wound; and should blood overwhelm you, cauterize with a lentiginosis-type cautery, which is suitable for this; then treat it with another treatment until it is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you see it turn dark or black and harden, such that the patient feels nothing when touched, then know it is cancer; and if it starts to lighten in color and moisture appears, lance it with an lancet, incise it with a thin spatula, and drain it from both sides; and should blood overwhelm your work, apply crushed vitriol until it stops flowing, return to your task until everything has been drained; then clean the wound with lime and silk, and treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	Abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	At no time should a swelling form within the throat called "godath," properly named the two almonds, and when you treat them as we have mentioned in the division and they are not healed, take care: if it is an abscess that is hard with small sense organs and of false coloring, do not touch it with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is swollen, do not touch it with iron due to blood loss; instead, let it soften before proceeding, then you may remove it as it would break on its own; and if it has a white color that weeps, and the root is subtle, prepare your instrument for cutting, but first ensure the abscess has cooled and is calm.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, 
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	When you press the tongue with all these instruments, and you see the abscess, then take the hook and insert it into the almond, pulling it up as much as you can; pull out any thread-like material along with it, then shape it using the instrument, which has the form of forceps; although its tips are curved, one against the other, and they are very sharp, being made of iron or steel.
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you don't have this instrument available, shape it using the pliers, which also has a similar form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	And one side should be sharp while the other is blunt; and when you have shaped one almond, shape the other in the same manner, and after the incision, gargle the patient with hot water, or a mixture of water and vinegar, and if there is any bleeding, then use cold water with the peelings of pomegranates, or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the blood stops flowing; then treat it until it heals; and sometimes other abscesses appear in the throat besides the two almonds, so treat them just like you would these two almonds.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman for an abscess that had formed inside her throat, specifically a small abscess; it had almost entirely blocked her windpipe, so she could neither breathe nor swallow food or drink and would have died if this continued even one more day.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	The abscess had risen to such an extent that two tubes were inserted through the nostrils.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I operated immediately, inserting a tube into one nostril and pushing it in; I pushed the other end out through an incision made on the opposite side of her throat, then opened her mouth and pressed down on the tongue to expose the abscess better; next, I inserted the tube into the abscess itself and cut away part of its inner wall; this allowed only a small amount of blood to escape; thus, I cleared her airway sufficiently for her to breathe easily again, and she began drinking water then wine shortly after; I continued cutting away parts of this abscess over an extended period until it eventually shrank back into the space I had created, but then it started growing larger once more; at that point, I cauterized its interior with a red-hot iron, placed inside her throat; in doing so, I stopped its growth entirely; and having done all I could, I left this woman's fate to God.
de l’uve	Of the grape
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When the grape descends, and it is swollen and long, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is below [is] thick and round, it is called a "grape".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is cleaned as we have said in the division, and the cleansing does not benefit [it], and you see that the abscess is healed, and it is delicate, then you must cut it; and one which is round, gathered, and not long; and it is bloody or of false color or black, then you must avoid incising it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger to the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	It is necessary, when you see it, according to the manner that I have said, of its whiteness and length, that you seat the patient in front of the sun, and press their tongue with the instrument which we have mentioned before; then insert the needle into the grape, and draw it out, and cut it with one of the two instruments I have mentioned for incising the two almonds.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And you must not cut away any flesh beyond the natural limit of superfluity; for if you remove more, it will be detrimental to the voice and speech; and after the incision, follow what we have said about incising the two almonds, and treat it until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient is afraid of cutting, you should employ an engine for cauterization to alleviate their fear.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	The manner of cautery is quick, sharp pain.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	Have the patient place their head in your lap and then press their tongue with an instrument we described in the cautery chapter, immerse it into scalding hot water, but ensure that it is neither too thick nor too thin; this is what the tool looks like...
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; 
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than incision or cauterization; if it is treated by fumigation in this way, take calmatively yarrow, sage, oregano, rue, chamomile and similar herbs and place them all or any of them into one pot with honey and boil. The pot should be well-sealed using strong earth, and inside the pot have an instrument made like this:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And it should be made of silver or copper, and one end of it inserted into the patient's mouth so that the vapour rises to the eye through the nose until the eye is destroyed; then do this frequently again until the eye dries up, but make sure you don't do this at the beginning of a hot abscess as many things can happen; nor should it be done except for in the decline of a hot abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, take a cane and place a piece of egg shell inside the patient's mouth, so that their mouth does not become too hot; for the egg shell does not allow the vapour to harm the mouth, and it is a good remedy along with healing.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Often a fish bone or spine gets stuck in the throat, or any other object; therefore, you must treat what you can see, and press the patient's tongue towards the sun with all your might, so that you can see the object move; and for what does not appear to you and is lodged in the throat, it is necessary that you make the patient vomit before the food is digested in the stomach; perhaps the object will be expelled by vomiting; or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a lettuce root, or a piece of dry bread; and tie a thread to the sponge, then swallow it; when it reaches the right place, it will become stuck, and then you can pull it out; and if it does not come out as we have said, take an instrument made of lead in this shape:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instruments be curved at the head so that they can more easily enter the throat, and have the patient's head raised up; watch out for touching the epiglottis, which could cause choking, or pushing the bone inside; it is better if the patient guides the instrument themselves, as they know where the problem area is; push the instrument downwards, or pull it upwards at any point until the object has been removed.
de la sansue de la gorge	From within the throat.
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	There is no medicine for the throat, as I have said in my division, using medicinal treatments; and when this does not help, look inside the patient's throat with sunlight, then press their tongue to the instrument that I mentioned.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the leech, draw it out with a small hook, or use delicate forceps that are fit for this purpose.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if it is not effective, take a hairy caterpillar and thrust it into the patient's throat; then insert at the end of the caterpillar a hot iron, and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And let the patient drink cold water all day long.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take a full glass of cold water and open the patient's mouth, pouring it in without letting them swallow, and continuously move their hand; as soon as the leech senses the water, it will fall out.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if it does not fall out as we have said, suffumigate the patient with asafetida using the instrument I mentioned in the treatment of eye infections; do this several times for it will soon drop out without harm.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And the manner of the fumigation is that you take a pot with visible coals, and cover it with a perforated lid in the middle, and through this hole place the end of the instrument; then throw your fumigation material into it, and let the patient put the end of the pipe in their mouth, closing their mouth so that no smoke escapes but instead goes to the throat; and from there the phlegm will now come out, if not, repeat the fumigation several times; and let the patient suffer thirst, eating salty things and nothing else, and do not drink water; then it shall be necessary for this process to end in the expulsion of phlegm.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the instrument used to remove phlegm is as follows, when it can be seen, resembling bent tongs to fit into the throat; and it should have a resemblance to a bird's beak, with roughness like that of a file, so that what it grabs cannot be released; and see here its form:
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapter of abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	There are many types of abscesses, according to the information that follows here from one and another in this book, and they vary in perforation and size; there are two main kinds, one being its own likeness, and the other due to moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second kind is for those on parts of the body where they are moist.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For abscesses of the head are different from those of the fundament, and abscesses on soft parts differ from those which occur in joints, each having its own treatment.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And in abscesses, one should not lance before the bowels are dead according to their completion; and if it is necessary to lance those which have formed crusts but are not yet dead as per their completion, like an abscess near a joint.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses appear near joints, and it is left until it has rotted all around, perhaps the ligaments and nerves of the joint are corrupted, which causes a contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	When the abscess is near the main limb, and if you delay perforation until it has died, it will harm the principal member; when it is near the foundation, pierce it before it dies; and one must not pierce an abscess formed without complete digestion unless it is near the foundation, so that it does not rot completely, lengthen inside, become a fistula, and cannot heal for a long time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And you must know the hour of perforation for the dead abscess according to its completion, which is when the pain subsides, and the fever breaks, and the reduction of pain and redness, and of swelling and sharpening at the head of the abscess, and other signs; and one must perform the perforation in the lowest place of the abscess, where it appears soft; and let the perforation be from the length of the body, and if the abscess is on hands or feet, or near joints, nerves, and arteries, and everywhere equal without folds.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In those which bend, according to this member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when an abscess is in soft tissue, it's best that you leave the perforation until it is confirmed to be digested completely, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you pierce it before this, the body of the abscess would have elongated and is full of much dirt; and by chance hardened are the lips and its bottom.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if to someone an abscess is pierced according to the width of its body, according to this which the limb needs.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And you should bring small abscesses with small holes; and for large abscesses, make large holes, and many incisions according to the size of the abscess; and if they are abscesses which need cauterizing, cut; when it is soft like a linen cloth, and dead, then you must treat it as you do boils: and there are some which are divided into three angles, and there are others where you make an incision like the leaf of myrtle, such as abscesses from an anthrax; and there are those on whom one makes a round cut, other cuts and similar incisions.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; 
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For sometimes the spirits twitch with the exit of the bile, which may cause the patient's death, and you would not perceive it.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Avoid this chapter with great caution, and when you have pierced your abscess, then dry the wound, and examine if the abscess wound is small; and if it is a full ulcer, then provide tents made of linen or old cotton; and if it is a large abscess with many holes, then you must insert a tent into each so that they come close to one another; and if you have cut away part of the skin around the abscess, then fill it with old cotton or shaved linen cloth without moisture, and bind it until the third day; then remove it, and treat it with ointment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if hemorrhages occur in your work, bring cold and light water, and wet some cloths, and place them on the bleeding site multiple times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the hemorrhage persists, bring compresses and ointments, and the powders I mentioned in various places in this book, and if it is during winter, and the skin or abscess is very thin, you must place cloths moistened with wine and hot oil on top; but if it is summertime, and the skin is fleshy, you must put on cloths soaked in water and oil, or cold wine and oil, for up to three days, as we said before; then uncover the wound, dry it, and treat it as needed until it heals.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And it is necessary to know this universally regarding abscess treatment; now I have told you how one should proceed in treating abscesses, and here is the chapter.
des soros	scurvy
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Where the brain of the head comes out small abscesses, and are made like nets, just like the breast of a hen, and there are many similar things.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There are some that are fatty and such that they have moisture like pus; and there are others which are hard and stoney to cut into, and there is no doubt if the artery does not act contrary.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the work of incision is such that you must try every instrument which is called an "introducer", from where its shape comes afterwards, and what it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if there is moisture, they will push it from above with forceps.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is evacuated, cauterize without leaving anything of the skin containing this moisture, for it returns when nothing is left there; then soak cotton in Egyptian ointment and apply to the wound if available; if not, use water and salt, and pack the wound with it, leaving it until the next day; and remove whatever has remained overnight.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then renew the cotton, as before, on the second day and again on the third, until you know that nothing remains overnight; then treat the wound with an ointment suitable for healing, until it is fully healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscess holds firm and greasy, lance it in this way, from above; insert your knife-edge and cut away all the pus, removing every bit of it; then focus your entire treatment on drawing out what remains in the subcutaneous layer where it lies; but if an artery presents a problem to you, do as I told you earlier.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And also of the abscess if it is hard, and of cutting and treating as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And the incision on the hard abscess and the moist one is lighter, for they have little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if some of these abscesses or chiefs have no moisture, like one of the abscesses I cut from an old woman's head; and I found the abscess as hard as a stone, rough and white, and it could not be broken; if any had been struck by one, they would have also made a wound just like with a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other abscesses coming to the head, especially those that come to children's heads and at the roots of the ears, let them be opened always towards the lowest point for pus to escape; and treat them as necessary.
des scrophules	Of scrofula
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Often these abscesses occur on the neck, and under the arms, and in the groin, and sometimes elsewhere on the body, and they are very common, and grow intertwined with each other.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each scrofula is properly within its own side, as with the abscesses and sores of the head, as we have said; and there are many types of these scrofulas.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and there are malignant ones that do not want to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	In those that you see with a good disposition to touch, and are similar in colour to the body, and move on each side without being close to the nerves of the neck or the artery or the conduit, and are not deep; it is necessary that you cut above them, and peel off each part, stretching the two lips of the heart outward if needed, as we have said for abscesses of the head; do this gently, taking care not to cut any nerve or vein, and being careful with sharp instruments so that no harm comes to your hands, and do not look too far ahead lest you cut what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you cut the vein or artery, and it does not allow you to work, then apply ground glass or some other hemostatic powder to the wound, and compress the wound; leave it until the abscess is appeased, the wound softens, and begins to rot.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	When the bleeding is staunched, return to your work until it is completed; then examine with your right index finger if there remain any small scrofulae, cut them out and clean them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if there is a large wound in the root of the scrofula, it is not appropriate to cut that scrofula at its root, but bind it with a strong double thread and let it fall off by itself without harm; then dress the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, and cure it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cut out the entire scrofula, then you must bring together the two lips of the wound, and stitch them now, since there is no excess left due to the size of the scrofula.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	you must proceed to cut the root of it, and drain [it], and stitch [it] as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For those scrofula that have excess, make an opening where it appears to die; and perforate [it] thus as the one mentioned before, depending on [the case], then apply dressings with ointment and similar things, so that they remove what is left of the corruption; and when the wound is well cleansed, treat it with healing ointment until it is healed.
de squinance	of dislocation
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients spoke of the procedure to cut into the throat; but I have never seen it done in our land, and this is a record of their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	For those with dislocation, the fold in the throat called the epiglottis must be avoided; and no aid should be given by this method, because all the veins and passages of the patient are affected by an abscess hot in the mouth, or in the throat, or in II amandres.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the illness is in the passage of breathing, it is necessary to cut the epiglottis to avoid suffocation and death.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	Therefore, when we wish to cut the epiglottis, we must make an incision beneath III circles or IIII with a small cross-shaped slit between the II circles or along the quantity of the slit in the sfac, not in cartilage; these are suitable places for incising the epiglottis where there is no flesh and the vessels are long enough.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the master is fearful, he must extend the skin of the throat to the entire incision, then split open the heart until it reaches the lung; remove the blood vessels, if you see anything, and then cut off the windpipe, as we have said; it is proven by the section of the lung's vein that should be there due to the broken place, and by the defect of voice; leave the wound open for a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed from which strangulation is feared, bring together the two lips of the heart wound, and sew them entirely without the cartilage; then apply medications that promote flesh growth until it heals.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasis says that one should not do this until the throat is completely blocked, and the patient is judged to be dying, and breath defect.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Then incise the epiglottis so that the patient cannot breathe, and they will respire through the wound, thus protecting them from death; and for this reason, the ancients instructed to leave the wound open until the evil of the illness has passed, and it is passed in three or four days. Then they ordered to sew up the wound and cure it so that it was cured; and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw a young lady take one knife and plunge it into her throat, severing part of the windpipe; I was called to treat her, and found her as if dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I uncovered the wound and found blood issuing from it, knowing that she had not opened a vein nor ruptured her windpipe such that air escaped through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I hurried and sewed up the wound, treating it until it healed; the only thing that happened to the damsel was that she lost her voice, but she returned afterwards to her normal state; this is why I say one should not fear an epiglottis incision.
de la grosse gorge	Of the swollen throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	This abscess is called a "swollen throat hernia," and it's a large abscess with a yellow color, more common in women; it can be either congenital or caused by an accident; the natural kind has no inflammation.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accidental kind is of two types, one resembling new fat, and the other type resembles an abscess that comes from an artery; it can be dangerous, and you should not operate with fire except on those which are small, and then only after examining all sides: if you find it similar to our fat, and cannot reach any veins, cut it out like a wart, removing its entire covering, if there is one; cauterize early, and treat as required until it is perfectly healed.
des nous	Des nous
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	Maintes manières de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblantes ; et or convient que je die toute la différence qui est entre nout et issu.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	Je dis que l'issue est alors la fièvre et la chaleur, tant que les ébullitions ne sont pas passées, et que la putréfaction n'est pas accomplie ; alors la fièvre et la chaleur s'apaisent.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	Avec notre nout, il n'y a ni chaleur, ni fièvre, ni douleur ; mais il y a un syfac, qui est son propre sac, et qui est selon la couleur du corps ; il commence aussi comme une jaunisse, et devient gros ; et ils sont de deux semblances, ou gras, ou humide, et très différents par leur couleur comme je l'ai dit dans la division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to treat the bone disease 'nout', that you first examine and inquire about all the instruments known as "entromissoires," according to how their form will be used in this chapter.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the method of examining abscesses in children is that you take hold with your fingers at the wettest place where you find it in the abscess, and turn them back and forth until you know that the instrument has pierced its core, then do so according to the size of the abscess; then withdraw the 'entromissoire', taking care not to drop it.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If running moisture flows from it, whatever colour this may be, then do to it as I have said for other abscesses; and if after using the instrument no more moisture comes out, know that it is fatty tissue, so cut across it with a cross-shaped incision, and take hold of it with forceps or pincers; carefully peel back the skin on either side, holding the flap where you made your cut so as to drag it away clean with the disease-causing bone matter (or 'nout'); if you cannot remove all the matter cleanly in one go, then do so by removing small pieces until nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	For if anything remains inside, the pus will return many times; and if a little bit remains and it irritates you, fill the wound with some sharp corrosive powders, secure the wound, apply warm soothing poultices to treat abscesses, and cure it with other treatments until it is healed; and if the abscess is large, cut the two lips of the wound, and cure it with something that promotes flesh growth.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	and if the swelling opposes you or is otherwise contrary, hasten and apply crushed vitriol to it, and leave it there for two or three days until the wound rots, suppressing blood boil; then return to cut out what remains of the matter.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	Observe here the shapes of the instruments to be inserted, and they are of three kinds: large, medium, and small; and there are three types called "albaret", and one type called "breb"; these have three sizes: large, medium, and small, used to probe abscesses and fistulas; they are also like needles for suturing sores; they can be made of yellow brass, iron, or silver, though those which are golden are better; black lead is more experienced at probing the curvatures of fistulas. These instruments come in three sizes: large, medium, and small, depending on the quantity and width of the openings.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The forms of the ounce are very similar, as you can see here: large, medium, and small; and there are ounces with two curls in three ways also; and there are ounces with three curls, and they are also of three types; and there are ounces with two curls, and ounces with one curl only, and these are also of three types; and all these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The heads of these are made sharp, and there are some that only cut on one side, which we use to peel back the skin so as not to damage the vein or nerve; and such introducer instruments have multiple handles, such that the patient does not feel it when opening abscesses; and they come in three sizes: large, small, and medium, as you can see; and they are only used on fleshy parts, such as legs, arms, breasts, groin, and similar areas; and sometimes another small instrument is made, resembling fistula scoops, according to this form, which we use to staunch blood.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	And it is sometimes placed in a position that heals by closing veins and arteries, and other times according to this grand design:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Sometimes the breasts of some men swell when they begin to corrupt, making them appear like female breasts; they remain ugly and swollen, and for those who wish to treat it, one must follow this form from point b to g:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	Flay the fat and treat the wound with meat-based medicine, then stitch together the two lips of the wound, healing it until it is whole; if the breast sags downwards and has softened due to its size like that of a woman's, make two incisions above it through two similar slits; let one be attached to the other at the end of each, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form, from point b to g; then flay the skin between the two lips and remove the fat, applying what we have said about stitching and powders as well as any necessary treatment until it is healed; if it doesn't heal or the incision isn't complete because of the patient's unwillingness to rest or due to bleeding, fill the wound with a corrosive ointment-soaked cotton pad; leave this on until it drains away the remaining flesh and fat, then treat it until it is completely healed.
des apostemes des asselles	Of abscesses of the armpits
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come from beneath the armpits are like hard scrofula with sides, and there is moisture within them.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those that contain moisture should be cut according to this form, from line b. to line g:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus in the abscess is drained, fill the wound with old cotton, and leave it until the next day; then remove all the cotton and treat it with an ointment until it heals.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess is similar to a scrofula, treat it as we have said for incising scrofulas, and if the wound becomes hollow, apply cauterization as we have described before.
de la routure de l’artere	From the rupture of an artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When an artery is ruptured, and the skin above it seals together, abscesses often form, and likewise, the vein becomes swollen and abscessed; and one can recognize that it is due to the artery when the abscess runs lengthwise perfectly; and when you feel it with your fingers, you sense a constriction; and when it is due to the vein, there is outward redness; and it is foolish to cut this abscess, especially when it is below the elbows and armpits, at the neck, and in many other places, as it is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, one must avoid iron treatment, and likewise for those at the head, one should avoid it too; in the case of a swollen arterial rupture, make an incision above the skin lengthwise; then operate with scissors, carefully separating the artery from its surrounding tissues until it is exposed; insert a needle beneath the artery, pierce through to the other side, and tie the artery tightly with double thread in two places as I have taught you for the extraction of the two temples' arteries; prick the area between the two threads with an introducer so that all blood within escapes and the abscess deflates; then administer a treatment involving gentle traction until the ligatures fall off; treat the resulting wound accordingly until it heals; if the abscess is due to the incision of the vein, one must hold as much of the abscess and surrounding skin in their hand before inserting a needle underneath this area, piercing through, and having double thread so that you can draw it from the other side; then suture the abscess as I have said with ligatures from one end of two threads to the two ends of another single thread; if there is doubt that the thread will come off, insert another needle completely beneath all of the abscess at the first incision and tie these threads in four places; then cut open the abscess so that excess matter escapes, then cut away this excess tissue but leave behind what remains bound together by sutures; apply a moistened cloth with wine and oil on top, administer treatment involving tents and ointments until it heals.
des apostemes des ners	Of abscesses of nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Also abscesses come in the artery and in the vein, abscesses come to nerves when they are injured or by too much hard work, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And they occur more often in shoulders and hands and everywhere where there are joints, and it is a severe abscess, and its color resembles the color of flesh, and it has various shapes without pain; and when one presses firmly on it, the patient feels pain, and it is not entirely inside the body but rather below the heart; and it shifts from all sides, and does not go forward or backward, neither beneath nor above, and the one which is in joints should not be cut with an iron tool: perhaps contraction would occur; and those that are on the head or forehead, treat them with a spatula.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscess is small, hold it with forceps and cut it at its root; and if it is large, suspend it using string, then peel it away, remove it, and close the wound by stitching, treating it until it is healed.
des grosses boces pendans	large boils hanging down
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.
