Often the skin of the calves is softened in some men because the tissues beneath are weakened and become visible; when one wants to treat it, make the patient lie on their back and cut away the softened skin over the natural leather; then gather the two lips together with a single stitch; if you wish, first remove any superfluity of the softened skin with three or four firm stitches; then cut between these stitches, and treat it like other wounds until they are healed, and remove the thread.
dou chastrement	The castration.
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	Know that castrations are forbidden in our law, and for this reason, I would prefer not to speak of them in this book; and it is only necessary for two manners: one being that the doctor should know how to respond when asked about it and its cure; and the other, because we often need to castrate some animals to help us, such as goats, sheep, pigs, and others.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I say that castrations are performed in two ways: either by traction or by incision.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In the method we perform through traction, make the animal sit in warm water until its testicles are softened and drooping; then grasp them with your hand, pulling until they are removed and you no longer feel them.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Du chastrement de taille: It is necessary that you hold the beast, and press its skin around the testicles with your left hand, then tie the suspender, and cut each testicle with one stroke once they are well exposed; leave a small amount of the soft and subtle tissue which lies over the vessels; this method of castration is better than the one done by attraction because some tissue may remain with the latter method, causing the beast to still have sexual desire; then treat the wound until it heals.
des hermofrodites	Des hermaphrodites: Of hermaphrodites, where one finds both male and female generative organs mixed together in an individual; this is caused by heat or cold in the womb during pregnancy.
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	Hermaphrodites are of two kinds in men: one is when between the two testicles there appears a formation like that of a woman's genitals with hair, and sometimes urine exits from it.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other manner is found in women, appearing on the wrist like a rod and two knobs.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	The treatment of men and women is the same: you cut all the adhering flesh away and treat it like any other wound; in the second case, for men whose urine passes through the skin of the knobs, there is no treatment.
de la tentigene	For the sting.
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	A sting is an adhering flesh on the natural part, so hideous to look at; some women have it as large as a hand, and that is its treatment.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	You must hold the superfluity of the sting in your hand or with pincers, and cut it lightly; do not go too deep lest blood flow, then treat any other wound until they are healed; and for another flesh that grows at the mouth of the anus, excising it, perhaps a fistula, resembling an egg, thus the ancients called it "egg disease".
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	You must cut it, as we have said with cauterization, and treat until it is healed.
de erratique	of wandering stones
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	Wandering is what happens when the woman's nature is not pierced, or the passage is small; and it is natural by birth, or an accident caused by illness that has arisen; whether it is due to a neighboring scar, or a subtle injury from a tool, and it occurs perfectly in the womb, on its sides, below, or wherever; and it prevents conception, childbirth, and perhaps even having flowers [monthly bleeding]; and such cases are recognized through observation of the belly.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the obstructions are close by, take them out with your fingers or a rod.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If he is of delicate constitution and close to the age of two years, hasten the treatment; do it as follows: place your two index fingers together, and have the woman lie on her back with her legs spread apart; then stretch open the two lips very wide so that the delicate sutures are rounded out, and cover the labia majora; then take wool, moisten it in oil, and put it in place, and make the woman lie thus for a man each day until it cannot fuse together again.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the suture is hard and thick, you should cut it with a spatule similar to a myrtle leaf.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the labia majora are made of flesh not yet born (the membrane), suspend it with a hook and cut it; have blood-staunching medicines ready, such as dragon's blood, incense, mixed with white of egg; then provide a lead cylinder that is wide enough so that the wound cannot fuse together again; and let this remain for some time, and bring her a tent made of dry linen; afterward, treat other conditions until she heals.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when there is a newborn child in the womb, it must be delivered in this manner, unless there are encrusted abscesses.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For an encrusted abscess in the womb, one should not apply cauterization.
des emorroides	Hemorrhoids.
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Hemorrhoids are open veins that usually discharge blood, and when hemorrhoids are old they become hard; we have previously discussed their similarities with others, their signs, and I shall now tell you which ones can be cured.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and hardness, when they are deep in the anus and cannot be felt, should not be treated with cauterization.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those who are at the mouth of the swamp, where one can feel it, are those whom one can cure.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	You must therefore place the woman in a cold house, then extend the ulcer with pincers, and cut it at its roots; then powder it with medicines that restrain blood, such as dragon's blood and incense, and similar things; next, press her feet against the wall for an hour, then put her into cold water. And if there is still any bleeding, have her sit in a decoction of sumac, pomegranate rind, gallnuts, and other similar things; then take barley flour, mix it with honey and egg white, and make a plaster from this mixture to be applied on her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if there is no bleeding, that's good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If not, apply cupping glasses to the back and breasts without injuring them; then take linen, and soak it in plantain juice or elderberry juice with old wine, and place it on the affected area.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Once the abscess subsides, treat the area with ointment until it heals; and the one called "albathir" is red, and resembles a rough head, so you must cut it as I said about "thelul"; then treat it until it heals.
des apostemes de la marris	Abscesses of the breast.
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many types of abscesses occur in the breast, such as cancer, stony abscesses, herpes, tumors, fistulas, hemorrhoids, hot abscesses, and various other diseases that I have mentioned in my classification.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	It is necessary therefore that I speak in this treatise of the hot abscess which forms in the armpit, which is not one of those abscesses which heal; and if you wish to know how to treat it, look to see if the abscess is acute at its onset, full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red when you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Therefore do not hasten to pierce it, but let it die down until the pain subsides; then have the patient sit on a seat, and provide two small seats for them to lean against, supporting their back and bringing their feet up to the outside of their legs; have their thighs spread apart, and place their arms beneath their knees, binding them well with a good bandage. Then suck out the matter towards the right side, and bring forward the instrument used to open the armpit wound, which is then shaped accordingly; when you want to introduce this instrument, be sure to mark first how deep the wound goes so that what enters of the instrument does not go further into the depth than it should, and does not harm the patient. If your instrument is larger, cover its depth with some cloth so that the instrument doesn't hurt the patient; have them hold the horn of the instrument above, while you hold the instrument itself.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	When the abscess opens up, and it is soft to the touch, you must remove it by hand, incising at the top or using spatula-like instruments; and when the wound is empty, place damp cloths soaked in rose oil or dry green oil into the wound; apply a fresh cloth saturated with water or cooked mallow outside of the wound over the skin, then bandage this all together; treat after two days of rest and tending to it as it heals, until it is fully healed; sometimes lift up the scab and wound using a cleansing enema of water and honey, followed by water or boiled lily roots and aristolochia longa; then return to applying ointments.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	If the wound is swollen in the scab, you must avoid cauterizing with iron but treat it as we have mentioned previously.
de l’enfantement	Of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	It is necessary first for the midwife to know the form of natural childbirth and its signs: when you see that the woman hastens below and wishes to smell air, then the child hastens to be born; therefore, understand that such a birth occurs according to nature's design where the baby exits under its head and the second stage accompanies it; and once these signs are seen one should gently press her stomach so that the child is soon released for when it descends on its head the second stage comes with it and the woman rid herself of superfluities through proper cleansing. And those who come otherwise do not arrive naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For sometimes it comes out feet first or the body and head exit together or even hands first, or it may come belly down often enough and be turned upside-down by chance around its neck and in other ways; thus the midwife must be wise and subtle in such matters so as to avoid error and deception, and I will show you all the forms and how one should aid them.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes out headfirst due to natural delivery, and the woman gives birth with difficulty, and her strength is weak, have her sit on a saddle or be held by other women; stimulate her nature with oil of fennel that has been cooked, then insert the small speculum into her vagina.
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	Cut the perineum and scrape under her nail until the moisture that gathers there runs out; press on the woman's belly so the child descends, but if he does not descend then you must give the woman an enema of fennel with oil of sesame seed; have her sneeze from condy seeds, holding her mouth and nose shut for one hour: now extract the child.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	If both hands appear first, you must gently pull them back and forth; if they cannot be drawn in, put the woman on a chair with her feet elevated above her head; then stand the chair up slowly while holding onto the woman so she does not fall during this process; if the hands still do not enter, and the child is dead, cut its hands off using the knife provided herewith and extract it, resetting the body evenly.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	Of the child's birth upon its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child is born on its feet, you must push it upwards; then turn it over and over until it is equalized; then take one of its feet and stretch it gently.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	Once it reaches the thighs, tell them to grab hold, and make them sneeze with force; if it jumps beyond that, may God will it so.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it does not go beyond as we have said, turn it over and over until it is according to the natural shape.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it is lightly done.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if it does not happen as we have said, take some mucilage from the elder tree, and oil of sesame, and melted gum, and grind all this in a mortar; then apply this medication inside and outside the woman's nature, then make her sit in lukewarm water up to below the ribs; and when she is moistened below, make a myrrh collar for her, put it underneath, and leave it an hour; then make her sit on a seat, then make her sneeze and hold her mouth and nose shut, and lightly press her belly, because now the child jumps.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	From the birth of the child upon its knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child arrives in this manner, place the nurse's hands here and there; then be careful around its neck, and let their feet hang down, and let it lie on the bed; fold its hands here and there, then take its hands to its belly, and remove the cushions from underneath until it is positioned downwards; if the child does not suck, take its feet and move them vigorously, then push its belly upwards, then put all your hands in; rock the child here and there; instruct the woman to hold herself steady as long as the child exits.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	From the birth of the child with one hand hanging out
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	I must devise a way to bring back the hand: if you cannot do so, make her get up and walk; if she cannot walk, make her lie on the bed with her legs bent upwards; then prepare the medicine that I mentioned earlier; if she does not give birth, have her sit on a chair, then consider how to pull back the hand; rock the child according to its natural position, make it sneeze, and instruct the woman to hold herself steady until the child comes out fully.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	From the exit of the child upon its neck, and have its hands spread out, and its face turned towards the back of its mother.
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	I agree that the midwife should hold its hand, then turn it little by little, and lift it gently; and when it is equalized, apply the natural muslin dressing with oil, as we have said, then instruct her to move a little at a time; and once you've done this, have her sit on a chair, and tell her to hold still; make her sneeze.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	in the same manner for all secondary dislocations
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it comes out in this manner for all secondary dislocations, press the shoulder with your nail until the moisture is emptied; and if the baby falls on its face or neck, lift its chin so that its airway is not blocked, killing the baby; then push the child back in, until you have repositioned it properly, and tell the woman to hold still once: then gently extract it.
de l’issue des gemelz	Of a dislocated ankle joint.
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins are born many times, and sometimes three or four are born; and this is not a strange thing, and it does happen.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	These are strange things, and they do not live, if born like this; I know that they multiply, and are divided by the midwife who separates them at birth; and sometimes they emerge naturally just as one child does, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they emerge with difficulty, then treat them as we have said, and let the midwife be skilled, and act quickly and gently in what she does; and do so for their well-being.
de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	None of them are formed in the womb I or II or III or IV or V or VI or VII, or more up to XV, and they are all shaped like a child by the measurement of the glorious blood, and it is necessary that the nurse knows all this, for perhaps similar things will happen to him; he should act according to what is appropriate.
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you treat the woman for a dead child in her womb, as I said in the division, and it does not come out naturally, and you have to perform manual work; you must know if the woman is of sound virtue, and has no accident or fear of death; the woman should be positioned on her back, with her hips inclined downwards, and her legs raised; the assistant should hold two parts of her, or she should be tied to the bed so that she is not disturbed during the removal of the child; then rub the mouth of the womb with moist oils mixed with a poultice of althea and fenugreek seed and flaxseed, then anoint the nurse's hands with these oils and mixtures; then insert the instruments gently into the womb, then choose a place where she can put the forceps appropriately, and take care if the foetus is equipped with all its parts that it comes down on its head; so insert the forceps in its eyes or neck or mouth or palate or under the chin or in the armpits or near the sides, and if the foetus presents with feet first, then put the forceps into the groin or lower abdomen; and you must hold the forceps with your right hand, and place the curve between two fingers of your left hand, and insert it with all your hand gently, and put the forceps in any of these places that we have said, until it reaches the empty space; and this is the shape of the forceps:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	Then insert another hook against the other one, or use a third if needed, to ensure equal extraction; and then stretch them evenly by pulling from either side, to remove it, and let the hooks be serrated to hold it firmly, just as shown here:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if any part remains, grease your finger with oil and push it into that part, then pull the other part; and if there's still a point left, place this hook or another higher up, doing so until it all comes out.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	If one hand comes before the other and you cannot reset it due to tightness, then you must wrap it in a cloth until it is completely covered; then cut it at the joint of the palm or with a knife, and do likewise for the other hand and foot.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; 
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the child is on his feet, the attraction is light, and the guidance to the mother's breast is easy.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	If he is constricted in the belly or chest, you must extract him with the cloth wrapped around your hand; and open the belly or chest until the moisture that is there is removed; and if other members are detached, and the head remains, put your hands perfectly on the mother's stomach, and pull it towards the mother's breast; then insert one or two fingers, and pull them out; and if the mouth of the womb is narrowed due to hot inflammation that has occurred, you must not work there, but apply moist and oily substances; and he applies plasters, and uses warm water for softening and moistening.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if the child is lying on its side and you can position it evenly, then manage as we have said for a living child; but if one lacks power to do so, then pull it apart piece by piece, leaving nothing of the caul.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	Once you have done this and the child is managed as we said for hot abscesses that come to a head, if there is discharge of blood, it should be immersed in warm water while being held steady; and other treatments are provided.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whose belly a child had died; then another formed on top of it, and this one also died.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, an abscess formed in the buttock; it swelled until it opened and began to produce a great deal of pus.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to treat [the wound], and I thought about it for a long time, but could not heal/close the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I applied a plaster of strong attraction, and an [the first] bone came out, and after some days another one did too.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was greatly astonished as there is no bone in the belly.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	So I thought it must be bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I explored the wound and extracted two bones from it until [the woman] was in a better condition; and thus she lived for a long time but there remained a little lump at the place of injury, which I have not forgotten from this chapter except that when a master finds something strange, he must know how to help.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	To return the marrow to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	Here comes the form of the compressor, for which we have two sets of straps; then turn to the second set at the heads of the two limbs.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	However, the horns should be more slender than those of the restrictor and made of ebony or boxwood; the mouth of the trunk is two inches wide while its margin is one inch thick; it's half a palm long; between these two sets of straps are two adjustments from this same piece of wood which are fastened on either end, each measuring half a palm or slightly longer; and these two adjustments can be inserted into the marrow's mouth for opening when you turn both horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, similar but more slender and lighter, should be made of ebony or boxwood wood like a pair of pliers; it has two sets of adjustments at its heads that are one palm long and two inches wide as you can see; when you want to open the marrow with this instrument, have the woman sit on the bed with her feet hanging down and legs spread apart; then insert the two adjustments together into the marrow; hold the head of the instrument underneath between her thighs; afterward move your hand across the entire instrument in a way similar to how you would do it with pliers according to the amount that you want to open up the mouth of the marrow, until the patient can do what they want.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	This instrument is all covered up and their appearances are manifold; when the surgeon has them ready at hand then his work will be speedier and more esteemed by men for its quality.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	Do not despair if you do not have the instrument ready, for its necessity is not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the midwife is delayed in childbirth, you must instruct the patient to hold her breath, and then make her sneeze vigorously, holding your hands over her mouth and nose; if she expels it, that is good.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If not, take a pot, and make a hole in its lid, and put herbs that can open the mouth of the womb, such as arsmart, rue, anise, chamomile, cassia, and centaury; cook all these herbs or some of them in water on the fire; then place one end of the tube into the pot, and the other end into the mouth of the womb, and hold it there until the vapours enter the womb; then make her sneeze, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the assistant runs out of medicine.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if the afterbirth remains even after this treatment, and it is not burned, instruct the midwife to moisten her left hand with oil of sesame or muskroot juice, then insert it into the womb, grasping the afterbirth. Once she finds it, grab and extend it little by little, ensuring the mother does not suffer during extraction; move it gently right and left, and pull slowly; this will cause it to come out and become dislodged.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the birth canal of the mother is narrowed, we have mentioned the treatment of inducing sneezing and herbal fumigation; but if it does not work after all that we have said, beware you do not force during extraction; instead tie what is at the birth canal to the thigh of the woman, then administer a four-compound ointment enema; this will soften and restore the area, leading to its removal; however, when this occurs, an unpleasant odor may arise in her stomach and head, causing harm to the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	So it is necessary therefore to use suitable fumigations for this: some of the ancients have tried fumigation with watercress and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The shape of the instrument with which one fumigates a woman to retain her flowers and menstruation is as follows:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it is of glass similar to a tube, and the wise head is placed in nature, and the wide ends are placed over fire; and let the fumigation be on the coals, and leave it until it is consumed, then start with another.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the fundament.
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born without a pierced fundament, but with a subtle plug: so during the bath it is necessary to pierce this plug itself with its own force, and not use a sharp spatula, taking care that she is not touched; then apply moist wool soaked in wine and oil, then treat her with ointment until she is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will heal, insert a piece of lead wire into the hole, leave it for several days, and remove it when the child wants to go outdoors.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	Sometimes this healing process occurs suddenly for wounds or abscesses; you must cut out that sudden growth: it should be treated as we have said about the piece of lead wire.
de la fistule dou fondement	On the subject of anal fistulas.
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that come from under the anus are nodules, and larger growths that come from outside near the anus, or in the space between the two parts; if there is a fistula or multiple, when this nodule is old, it becomes hard, and still moist with white pus or soft boils, and sometimes these fistulas perforate; they are recognized by those who have them through their defecation or flatulence, and perhaps a worm jumps out during excretion.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And so for fistulas that penetrate up to the bladder, and up to half of the penis; they extend up to the hip joint, and down to the knee.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	Thus one recognizes the fistula penetrating the anus and not elsewhere: it is when you place your index finger on the anus, and insert a fine needle of brass or iron into the fistula without twisting it.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if there is any tortuosity, insert a thin probe of bronze or a horsehair until you feel the end of it with your finger; and if you do not feel anything coming out through the aperture, neither air nor faeces, as we have said: know that it does not perforate; so desist from treating it.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula has perforated up to the bladder or up to the urine duct, it allows urine to escape, and cannot be healed by medicine.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it is perforated up to the hip joint, the wound extends that far; if there is no torsion and the pain originates from around the area, then it should be treated with bowels, and medicine or immediate dressing are of no use; in these penetrating fistulas, there is no cure other than surgery, and it is the foolish surgeons who attempt to treat them.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In the case of a non-penetrating fistula that is not old, there is hope for healing with iron, as I have experienced, and it should be done with the patient lying between your hands on their back; then lift their legs up to their thighs, and incline their thighs towards their belly; insert a bronze probe, or lead if there is torsion, until you find where the probe emerges.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels it around the anus, you must put your index finger there; if you then feel that the tendon has been pierced; and if you can feel a gap between your finger and the skin or flesh underneath, know that it is indeed perforated; do not attempt to treat it as it cannot be healed.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	We say nonetheless that some can be healed, though this rarely happens; the aid given is as follows: heat the fine cautery according to the width of the fistula, as stated before; insert it hot into the fistula until you reach the anus; do this twice or three times, until you know that these flawed tissues are burnt away, which look like feathers; then treat with damp bandages steeped in butter until all the tissue is removed, and finally treat with healing ointment that soothes the flesh and seals it.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If he is thus healed, it is good.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If this cannot be healed in any other way; and if it enters but does not penetrate to the bone at the base, and between your thumb and the incision is a thick covering of flesh or skin, and you see the fistula on what binds the covering to the heart; then cut away from the beginning of the fistula, push forward past the incision, and cauterize afterwards until reaching the top of the incision; and the incision will be released and fall out; then clean those faulty tissues which look like a bird's feather, leaving nothing behind.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the blood defeats you, flowing between your thumb and the incision, then cauterize with fire or medicine.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For the fire cautery brings together two good things: namely, burning of adjacent tissues and stopping blood flow as well as drying up moisture; then treat moist wounds with butter or ground substances until the flesh shrinks, and it is after the tissue has been burned in the flesh; finally, cure the wound caused by hot applications hardening tough flesh, and they are dry medicines.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, it is healed and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if the fistula comes up to the anus, and is far from the body, put your finger in the anus and feel it.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the tumor and find skin or sinuous flesh or tissue where it is ready to break open, take no action unless there is reason for confidence and hope through one of three ways: cauterize as we have said, cut deeply, or if possible insert a tent and cure as before; but do not go too deep lest you cut the muscle that holds the anus, causing stool to pass involuntarily; then treat it as stated above. Perhaps it will heal, or remove this covering and clean after cutting near the anus with tent or other pointed instrument; next, remove diseased flesh from the wound as much as possible; finally, consider restoring the wound while preventing a fistula outside of the anus - which would be less serious for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And sometimes fistulas are formed in this manner: it is when you insert the probe into the fistula, and it is located on the side of the rectum near the skin above, take a perforated probe with an end shaped like this...
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	...and insert the curved wire into it in such a way that the probe follows this path.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is perforated into the wall of the rectum internally, then remove the wire from that orifice, as you would insert your finger into the rectum; draw out the end of the wire, and bring together the two ends, bind them to one another, and leave them thus for a day or two; sometimes binding them so that the wire touches both edges which lie between them, and they discharge; then treat the wound until it is healed.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not rupture, make it burst in every way you can, unless it is too deep.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not suitable to operate on if too deep, then treat it as we have said until it heals.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The shape of the sharp-edged spatula used to make the fistula is very acute at one end and pointed; but on the other side it is not, because you do not operate on what should not be operated on, as you can see here:
des emorroydes	Of hemorrhoids.
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Hemorrhoids are of two types: either they are inside the anus like resin grains and there may be small or large ones, which bleed slightly; sometimes there is one, other times many; or they appear outside the anus at its edge; those that show up outside have very little moisture in them, though sometimes a bit of yellow liquid or blood, and their color matches that of the body. Treating those inside involves telling the patient to strain themselves to go to the toilet until the anus opens up and the hemorrhoids appear: then be quick about it; grasp one with pincers or hold it under your nail before cutting off its roots. If they cannot keep ahold because of moisture, grab them with a piece of linen cloth, cotton wool, or camel-skin leather; pull them out with your fingers and cut them open to apply hot powders in place of cauterization; you can also cauterize as described in the chapter on cauterization and then treat it using other methods until they are healed. If the anus won't open up, give him a sharp and harsh enema to cleanse what is inside the anus so that he may excrete openly: once patients strain themselves and the hemorrhoids come out of the anus, treatment becomes easier; you can take hold of them with your nails or pincers and cut them before treating as we have said until they are healed. It helps to avoid incision by iron instruments.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is necessary to suture in this manner: take one twisted thread and insert it into a needle; pass the thread through on one side and pierce the needle from the other side, then turn over twice at both ends of the thread below the needle, leaving it rather broad; tighten the thread firmly, then knot the thread and remove the needle. Do this for all except one, and leave that one to drain off excess blood. Then place on top a moistened piece of cloth soaked in rose oil or ointment, put it on the foundation, and instruct the patient to rest. Leave them until they discharge pus, then treat with an ointment and other remedies until healed
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	dryness of feces or fundament
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times there is constipation of feces in the intestine, and due to the constraint of nature, and when the illness is old and medicine is ineffective.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	You should reset the point of a spatula or your nail to the bark above, which should not be moist; then treat it until it is firm as it should be; and if it cannot heal, repeat the shaving more strongly than before, until it heals greatly, and becomes scabbed; then treat it until it is healed.
dou fremit	where there is trembling
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	Ants are a small faulty appearance between the body, and goes much deeper; and sometimes it finds cold, and one feels it trembling like death, and it spreads throughout the body, more in the hands than other parts.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the cure is that you take a cane made from a goose feather quill or a strong vulture's feather and place this cane on the trembling affected area so that its purple circles touch it all around; then turn your hand over to cover the entire cane and put it in perfectly, extirpating the tremor by its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you wish, make this with a cane of brass or iron according to this form, and let it be hollow underneath and flat on top.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	Do not pierce it to put on your finger, but rather hold and squeeze it; And if you wish, cauterize the tremor in the same way as described in the chapter on cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	of the enema form.
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Sometimes silver or tin is used to make an enema, or bronze that has been melted and formed into wire; sometimes these instruments are small, sometimes large, depending on those for whom they are intended.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those that are used in the treatment of children and for those who are weak and ailing are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The shape of the enema instrument is broad at one end, where the belly is tied in this way:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and if it has a release valve or the belly is tied in this manner, as you see here, and the head end is perforated; have on one side two openings, and one opening on the other; and let the belly where one puts the medicine be made from a beast's bladder or parchment, pierced all around with small holes, leaving an inch between each hole, then pass into these holes a strong thread of twisted gut arranged in a crosswise pattern, and sew up the belly like a goatskin bag; when the medicine is inside, tie it to the instrument before you with a strong thread, then administer the enema. This makes the circular shape:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And let the medicament not be too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head of the catheter with oil or egg white, or something similar, then insert it gently; thereafter have two ministers press their II hands together, until everything is visible, then remove the catheter, and lift the patient's legs against the wall, and if the medicament wants to exit, hold it as much as you can; and if he sleeps a night on his side, so is greater help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you catheterize for a bellyache, and the medicament wants to exit quickly, so redo it until he is cleansed.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if there are haemorrhoids at the anus or abscesses, then let the catheter be as subtle as for a child; and this is the form of the subtle catheter on which the skin should be stretched:
des plaies	wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already spoken about the treatment of wounds in the previous section; now we will discuss the art of healing and medicine, according to its fulfillment.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are inflicted, and where the wounds are located, as well as what has caused them.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	Wounds are caused by various objects such as rocks, sword or knife cuts, lances, sticks, arrows, or similar things; they can also be classified according to the body part affected, like wounds on the neck, head, foot, stomach, liver, and other similar areas of the body. I will explain the treatment for each type of wound, starting with simple head wounds because their memory will come in its own chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound occurs on the head and the bone is not broken, take care if it is due to a stone impact or similar things, and the skin is still ruptured and the wound is large, and you slightly suspect an abscess inflammation: then make him bleed immediately using the cephalic vein especially if little blood comes out of the wound, and let the bleeding be from the opposite side of the affected part; and prevent the patient from overeating wine and fatty meats.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he does not want to bleed, then let his diet be reduced, and let him neither drink wine nor eat meat; and put on the wound, if abscess inflammation occurs, only moist cotton wool in rose oil or in astringent wine; and if there is no hot abscess, then apply on the wound, if it is fresh with all its blood, and has not been moved by air, powder which I will mention shortly; and if the wind moves it, then put on some ointments until it is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like that of a sword cut or similar, and the lips cannot be brought together with sutures, then they should be joined by stitching, as I will explain for wounds in the abdomen, specifically about stitching.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is open to the bone, gaping, and held together only by a little skin, then cut away that skin; then treat the wound with medicine, restore hard flesh in place of leather, and instruct the patient to eat hearty meats like beef and pork, as well as wheat-based foods such as bread and porridge, chicken, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find rotting flesh on the skin, and it has not reached the bone, then cut away all the rot and discard it, then clean the wound; and if there is an artery in the wound that bleeds uncontrollably and cannot be staunched with medicine, then tie off the artery, and if you find it to be loose, bind it with a thread; and if this brings no benefit, cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is light: it is that you put this powder on which welds as soon as the cold has moved away.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	The way of the powder is as follows: take one part incense; two parts dragon's blood; three parts quicklime, and finely powder it, apply to the wound, and hold firmly, until it dries well and joins with all its blood; then bind it well, and leave without untying, if it does not swell; for you remove the medicine once it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes one uses only quicklime powder when they do not have incense or dragon's blood, but the cold has moved away from the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the burn has killed the wound, especially in winter, do not put this powder on it; instead, apply some soothing ointments or poultices made from barley flour with water and honey until it discharges pus; then treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if the bone fracture comes with the wound, and it is small, extract it with fine pincers; I will tell you about head fractures later.
de la plaie dou col	On the neck wound:
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If the wound is on the neck and it is straightforward, there is no significant distinction between this and a head wound; however, if the carotid artery or other arteries in the neck are severed.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is the black humours, there is no other treatment besides letting them drain away, and putting nothing constraining on them, as they cause harm to the black humours and make them retreat; and put nothing cold on the wound, because the substance of the black humours is cold, and their continuity is with the brain, which is the highest organ; but let there be a warm medicine, just like heat washed in sweet water, and mixed with rose oil, and cowhage also washed in sweet water, and other minerals according to this manner, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, cut it open and bind with bandages; then treat it until it heals.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and full of hair and filth, open it at a lower level; and if an artery is cut, and blood flows out, then split it further to see where the bleeding comes from, cauterize if necessary; and if the spinal cord of the throat is cut or the heart vessels guarded for that the meat goes through them, carefully cut the heart above the canal of the throat but do not touch the throat itself instead reset it according to its natural shape; then secure it appropriately, leaving it a few days before treating with drying ointments until it heals; and if the wound has penetrated into bone, open the wound; and if there are broken pieces of bone that you can join strongly together, do so, but those you cannot put back, leave them in place to let the wound fester, then drain and ease its discharge; and if the wound is fresh, dust on it the powder I have mentioned.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and it has formed a fistula, treat it as I have described in its respective chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	Of the wound caused by a spear or knife.
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a spear or knife wound, and the injury is deep, examine whether there are signs of infection as the patient recovers: know then that the wound is fatal. But if it is not deep, and all the blood has come out, do not apply powder nor bind the wound for the first few hours to prevent the blood from clogging up and returning to the heart, which would kill the patient; instead, apply an attracting ointment twice a day. If you have none, put old cotton in the wound to absorb moisture, and make the patient sleep on his injury for three days or four or more: this way spasms, bad tremors of the heart nor strange behavior will not occur. When you see these favorable conditions, know that the wound is healed.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.
