Treat it then with bandages and other treatments until it is healed; if it cannot heal, perform surgery, as there must be a fistula present, so treat it accordingly.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	If the wound is from a sword or knife incision, and it is simple, on the arm or back, treat what is in front; if it is large, stitch it up; if small, use powder; if it has penetrated the bone, breaking off pieces, clean out the wound, and treat any torn blood vessels; if they are not torn, let the wound suppurate to alleviate extraction; for wounds on other body parts, the judgments are as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	Rupture of the abdomen.
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	The breakings of the belly are great and small and minor; from a large wound sometimes the intestines or the nerves of the intestines fall out, due to which water is introduced [into the abdomen]; and the stitching is more difficult, and at times the minor wound is worse than the major one because you put back the intestines with greater difficulty if they were not placed there immediately. This is why a minor wound is preferable since we return the intestine to its place much easier rather than other parts II And know that the rupture of the belly occurs in four ways: two common methods for suturing are used on abdominal wounds, and another two different ones are also commonly applied for other body injuries; however, they are more appropriate for the former, and I will explain each one individually.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small, and some part of the intestine comes out, and it is a serious matter to replace it, this can be done in one of two ways: either because of the small size of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is swollen due to cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, warm it in this way: moisten a sponge or a soft cloth in tepid water only, or cook it in nipping and spicy water, and dampen the intestine until the swelling is removed; and sometimes apply constricting wine, which aids healing by reducing swelling.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling subside, moisten the intestine with water in which almonds and mallow have been cooked, because this eases its entry somewhat; and if it cannot enter, then make a small incision on the wound with an instrument used to cut haemorrhoids; and the first treatment is believed to be beneficial for those who do not need major surgery; these are the instruments to use: they should cut inside along the curvature and outside, and here is their shape:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines have burst out, so replace them dry according to their natural form in their proper place if you can, for it is worth trying.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is large, and it is located below the abdomen, you must lay the patient on their back and raise their legs higher than their head; if it is below the belly, place the head and chest higher than the lower parts; likewise, if the abdominal rupture occurs in one of the two halves, attend to what I say so that the injured part is raised above the other; thus you should manage as I've said for large or medium wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	For small wounds use what is available to you, then have a compassionate assistant hold the entire rupture in their hands and bring together its lips; this is the common manner of stitching, and it goes like this: take one or more needles according to the width of the wound, leave two fingers' breadth at its head, insert a needle with strong thread into it; pierce both sides of the skin and subcutaneous tissue so you perforate that part, gathering together the four edges; then pull a double strand of thread through the eye of the needle in two parts, bring together both sides of the wound suitably, then leave another two fingers' breadth and insert another needle; tie off the thread as you did for the first needle, and don't cease doing this according to your needs with the needles until the entire wound is closed up; the needles should be medium-sized, between fine ones and thick ones, because fine ones cut all the flesh, and the too thick cannot enter well: therefore they must be medium-sized; also, you must not insert the needles too far beyond the flesh and skin so that they do not tear open the wound before it is sewn shut; then clip off the ends of the needles lest they hurt the patient when sleeping, put tents or little cloths at the needle ends to hold them in place, and leave them there until the wound has healed; this manner with needles is more convenient for small wounds, because you need just one or two. The second stitching technique is common: gather together both sides of the skin and subcutaneous tissue into one needle with a strong medium thread; when you've pierced all four edges bring the needle back to where you started in the way cloth is sewn; space each stitch by the thickness of a little finger; this stitch serves men, and I once used it on a wound that a man had on his belly, which was cut open by a knife, and the wound was more than a palm wide, and intestines were protruding two palms wide, and the wound was in the middle of his stomach.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I returned his intestine after it had been outside for twenty-four hours, and the wound healed in fifteen days; I treated him, and he was cured.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And the doctors had judged that he would die, but it was a miracle; I did not treat him with any ointment as I was in a place where none could be found and no medicines were available. I put old cotton on his wound twice daily and washed it with honey water until he healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Now I will tell you about the two proper methods of suturing: take your needle and pass it from outside to inside; once it has pierced through the heart from right to left, leave the tip on one side where the needle emerged, and then pierce again from inside to out. The understanding behind this method is that you should suture like a furrier would sew pelts, leaving some space between each stitch as you go along until the wound is completely closed.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second method of suturing, as Galen accurately describes it, is when some practitioners bring the two parts together naturally and apply one head of the wound to the other in this manner: insert a needle into one chief of the mirror close by, and pierce that place alone, leaving the two heads of the symphysis; then turn the needle and make it pierce from outside to inside at the two heads of the symphysis; then pierce both from outside to inside at the other two heads of the mirror which are on the opposite side; this is the second method of suturing and by far, the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galen says this word, and some testify that one must sew the belly with two needles, each having a thread; and one should push one needle from one side and the other from the opposite, in the manner of those who sew leather straps; and know that when the rupture is in the middle of the belly, then the suture is more severe than for the other places of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgment of the wound is such as the judgments of other wounds: and it is that when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, rather than let it move, treat the intestine first, and sew up the cut; then apply the powder on healing flesh, and if the wound has moved, put some present ointment on top until the wound bows; cauterize the sinews and tendons, then cure the wound like others, until it is healed; and if you have no medicine, put old cotton on as soon as it starts to heal, and change it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	You will not need any other medicine in many cases where the wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound might affect the main limbs, then it is necessary to wet light linen with warm temperate oil or rose oil, and place it around the groin and under the armpits; and if there is pain or inflammation in the belly, which often happens, then administer a tepid wine enema, especially if the inflammation reaches the intestine; pierce it inside, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine that is called "jeun" cannot heal when it is injured, and this is due to the fragility of its veins, and because of the delicacy of the entire body, and the closeness of its nature to nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the swelling jumps out of the wound, return it backward, just like with an intestine, while it is fresh; and if it is old and has turned green or black, you must bind the black area so that no blood runs from it, for there are veins and arteries; then cut away what lies between the binding, and hang both ends of the intestines downward below the wound until outside to facilitate the extraction when the swellings fall, and the wound sinks.
de la routure dou boueil	On the rupture of the mouth
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine is round and the wound is small, it can be restored in some men, for I saw a man wounded in the belly by a lance; the wound was on the right side of his stomach, and became inflamed and turned into a fistula, from which came discharges and wind. I treated him as best I could, never ceasing to clean until he was healed, and the flesh knit together.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw it healed, I feared the patient might have pain in his belly; but he felt no pain, instead remaining in good condition, eating and drinking; some experts said that for a small wound in the intestine one must be bound thus: take large-headed pins, then bring together the lips of the wound, when the pin has opened its mouth, place it on the two lips so that it clamps its mouth shut. Then cut off the head of the pin and this holds fast so it cannot come loose; put another pin there after in like manner as before until the whole wound is taken up; then dress the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, 
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of fistula wherever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that any wound or abscess, when it heals, is universally called a "fistula," especially when it is covered and curved.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And fistula is truly an erroneous hard and white nodulation, where there is no pain felt, and it is also curved like the feather of a bird; sometimes it jumps clear inside, other times dense; at some points shallow, yet deep in others; and I have spoken about this in the division of wounds, that any wound that has not healed, lacking tissue, remains so due to one of nine reasons: namely, the smallness of blood or matter; its malicious nature; there is hardened tissue inside along the lips, preventing new tissue growth; too much curvature; pus present and matter of poor quality; inappropriate medicine in treatment; a particular type of corruption like that of pestilence; locality with delayed digestion; slow healing and swelling by nature; presence of veins or bone: I have already demonstrated all these causes, their signs, and medicinal treatments in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Now is when I must inform you of the treatment for fistula, which is performed manually.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	Fistulas can occur in any part of the body; for there are fistulas that affect large veins, arteries, nerves, skin, intestines, bladder, ribs, spine, or joints of hands and feet; affecting thus the principle member and similar areas.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	All fistulas of this nature are serious and require immediate attention, but only through laborious work and skilled ignorance; if there is any fistula that does not reach the level I mentioned, you have faith in the treatment, and you can identify it, then take a probe of brass or iron, if the fistula is straight, probe it; and if the fistula is twisted, seek with a fine probe of lead, for lead bends along curves; and if the fistula has many openings and cannot be probed properly, then cleanse one opening through an enema, as moisture travels from one to another, cleansing them; then carefully probe as much as you can, identifying if there are bones or nerves, and is hair coming out perfectly, inquire of the patient about pain when pressed by your hand, and where they feel it; once knowing truly its location, and whether it lies close to a joint, nerve, artery, vein, or in any areas I mentioned, then treat as previously stated, removing pus and corrupted tissue from within; afterwards cure until healed, if the fistula is well deep and straightened, cut perfectly as much as possible, insert moist probes medicated with quicksilver, pushing them down to the head of the fistula, so that the medicine corrodes remaining excess; then apply invigorating ointments on healthy flesh, until healing; if not healed this way, cauterize as previously said, and if bone is corrupted by the fistula, cut it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If the wound or tumor does not trouble your main limbs, as we have said; and if the bone is exposed, with decay and blackening, then treat it until all decay is removed, then cure other things growing thereon so that it may heal; and if it is not healed, and returns sickly as before, know that you have not gone deep enough: uncover and probe until you reach the bottom, and remove all decay, then restore its place; and if it thus heals, it is well.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If not, know that the decay is too deep for you to reach; there is another engine which nature leaves behind; and if there is one small bone corrupted, and you can extract it with forceps, then remove it with a suitable instrument, and if there are many bones, pull them all out entirely, do not leave any one behind; and if moisture makes this difficult, and there is no error or fear, then cut away the moisture and flesh, and free the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you cannot remove them within an hour, apply something that encourages putrefaction to the wound, and let it rot around the bones until their tissue becomes soft; then they will more easily extract the bones; and if it is a large bone like from a leg or thigh, only remove as much of its corruption as long as all blackness is removed, then restore the wound; and should a great part become corrupted extending to the marrow of the bone, you must treat and cut away until all that has decayed is removed, then heal it so that it may be sutured; I shall tell you about a fistula which happened in a man's leg so that you can take example from this and apply help to your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	There was a young man around thirty years old who had pain in his leg due to an internal cause, resulting in matter coming out of the leg and forming a large abscess with no external opening; however, the surgeons foolishly operated on it until the abscess opened, discharging much matter, eventually becoming a fistula with numerous holes excreting bowels and bodily moisture; many doctors treated him for over two years, but none were experts in surgery, so I was called upon to examine his leg and the medications used during treatment as well as the large amounts of discharge from the openings; the young man's body became red around these wounds, developing a yellowish color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I set up a tent in one of these holes, and then searched all the holes, and found that one came against the other from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I hastened and cut into one of the holes until I exposed a part of the bone, and found it corrupted and perforated, with the corruption reaching deep into the bone; I removed what appeared to be the corrupt part, and believed there was no other corruption except for what I had taken out; and I began to treat the wound with soothing medicines over a long period, but it did not heal; then I started again, and exposed the bone as before, and found that the corruption had continued into the bone, so I removed it, and attempted to join the place together; but I could not manage this until I cut around one palm's breadth of the bone, which was entirely soft, then I restored it with medicines; and it healed quickly and became joined, without needing further treatment except for the weakness of the patient, who could not bear it, and my fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For due to the blood evacuation he bled often, but he was entirely healed, and in place of the bone grew a hard tissue, which was well-formed and caused no harm or side effects whatsoever, either at present or later on.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, it should be treated as follows: take one linen bandage, and bind it to the end of the bone that sticks out, then instruct someone else to pull it upwards; put another thicker woollen bandage on top of the flesh covering the bone, pulling it taut so you can draw up the flesh away from the area where you want to operate without damaging or cutting into the flesh; put a red-hot iron or piece of wood beneath the bone in order to cut through the corrupted flesh; and one must treat as much corruption as they can see and feel, treating again another time.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	Et se li os est corrumpus, and n'apert mie, and li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l'une partie a l'autre la corruption, and soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; and se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, and soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; and se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t'apert; and la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire and les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os and l’aparance dous, and lor grossece and lor subtiliteit, and lor grandor and lor petitece, and lor duresce; and por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; and saiches que l'uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, and le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.
dou feu	Of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The head decays either from within or from without; and when you have treated that corrosion with medicine and it does not improve, then you must amputate the limb up to the point where the decay originates, so that the patient escapes death, or a worse fate of having their member disabled; and the signs are that the limb turns black, as if burned by fire, and after the blackishness, for that corrosion spreads from limb to limb, taking over the entire body; therefore you must hurry in amputating, and if it is due to the sting of some venomous beast, such as a sea scorpion or viper and their likes, if the decay affects the head of the finger, then cut it off, giving no respite until it reaches the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; 
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	At times an abscess forms in fleshy places and remains there for a long time until it creates a large accumulation of pus; then it ruptures and bursts, and the pus escapes like from a vase; while the surrounding skin is as thin as soft silk and does not extend down to the bone or nerve. A disease of this kind is called "sine" (abscess) but not "fistula". However, if such an abscess extends all the way through to the bone it is called a 'fistula', and then you have to remove that surrounding skin by cutting away around it entirely - especially when it's thin like silk-; and make sure you do this before the tissue becomes corrupted.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if you fear that the skin will become infected but there is no deep corruption and the skin is thick with flesh, then cure it in this way using an enema: first examine whether the breast is large and the bowels within smell foul; then give it an Egyptian medicine made thus: take wax and oil and white lead equally, put them to boil on a fire until the medicine turns red and becomes as thick as honey; then mix what you need of this with water and honey and administer it by enema into the breast, pressing the orifice closed. Leave this in for two hours before expelling it gently. Repeat this many times until the breast is cleansed of pus. Sometimes an infusion of ash-water is used when the Egyptian medicine isn't available; you should take some vinewood ashes and add water to them then strain these through a cloth, and use as enema until you can see that the breast has been well cleaned; but if the patient cannot tolerate this, nor the Egyptian medicines or ash water, then use an infusion of water with honey in which there is a little white lead ground up; or an infusion of honey mixed with wine, for honey cleanses and washes away dirt while wine dries out pus. When you have done these things, and are sure that the breast has been well cleaned, administer by enema what makes flesh grow again - take some definitive plaster made with rose oil in wine; or use some medicine and ointments whose properties I will now enumerate under a treatise on ointments. If the orifice of the breast is small and the nozzle of an enema cannot enter it, then enlarge this slightly using a piece of iron and apply thereon some Egyptian ointment or basilicon until it's enlarged enough; but if the wound is too wide, cut away just enough flesh so that only one place remains where an enema can enter; and if the orifice which discharges pus lies above - well, cut it off at a point below this.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	For when the bowels are in perfect condition, they do not allow meat to be engendered; and if you cannot cut it off from below as you wish, prepare it in such a way that the bowel goes down to its lowest point, for when the bowel is perfect, it does not allow meat to be engendered. And if you cannot cut it off from below as you wish, prepare it like this: let the bowels go gently downward, and leave nothing of them; take consolidating medicines to put on the wound, and spread over a linen cloth that covers all the wound; then cut with force at the top of the wound a hole wider than the first one, extend ointment onto another piece of cloth according to the amount of the opening of the wound. And place it above the wound in order to alleviate the bowel; do not remove the large external cloth until many days have passed once; and that which is on the surface of the wound, take off often for expelling bowel contents: if what comes out is poison or a small quantity or enough, whether digested or undigested. And consider if there is pain or not in the patient's case, and if there has been an abscess or no; when your medicine is thus extended, and you see that which exudes from the wound opening, know that the wound has already healed, and bring the saints close; then untie him in the morning, on the third day. And when one undoes the bandages of the wound, one replaces another piece of cloth: renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast ejects undigested food after many days, know that the breast is not healthy.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poison lingers for a long time, do not despair of health, for healing is near.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	For there are people whose wounds heal slowly with charring, and those who do the opposite; and if undigested food comes out of the breast after many days, know that the breast is not healthy; and if the breast takes a long time to discharge, and is distant, then apply medicines drying moist substances and dry in virtue, such as definitive ointment, for it has a large part of vitriol, and it is the last medicine; take definitive ointment, and make it with rose oil, and mix it with equal amounts of old wine; then cook it and use it; this same one made cooked thickened works better when definitive ointments are not available, or you can take myrrh and aloes and incense, and grind them, and powder them on honey while it is over the fire; and then glue a piece of cloth to it, spread it on the breast, and sometimes they use long aristologist, and roots of celestial lilies, which are like barley flour and centaury; and apply either simple or compound medicines: grind them, make a powder out of them, and mix with the honey I mentioned, then apply it; and if the treatment is prolonged, and this cure doesn't work, know that corruption has reached perfection, and caused pressure on the bone, or hard parts, or ligaments; so heal the fistula as we said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	Of the abscess under the nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Panarice is an abscess that forms under the nail of the finger on the hand or foot, or occasionally in other places; and when it becomes old, if not treated promptly, an enclosed pus-filled swelling appears, and spreads until it reaches the root of the nail, and may even destroy it entirely; and this leads to deep ulceration reaching the bone, causing a foul smelling pain, with enlargement of the affected finger or toe, whose colour turns livid.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the classification, and the treatment does not improve its condition, then you must cut away all that which remains of the nail with an iron instrument, and afterwards cauterise the wound.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	The cauterizations are a great help if the bone is healthy and the nail is sound; and if the nail presses on the flesh, begins to prick it, and causes injury, you should place the needle under the nail that pricks the flesh, push it upward, and cut off this flesh gently and lightly, then apply caustic and corrosive medicines onto the remainder of the flesh in order to remove all [flesh]; afterward cure with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	If the corrosion has reached the bone, cut it away and treat with a cautery, for as long as the corrupted bone remains, it cannot heal; and if you see the finger becoming corrupted, cut it off right away just as described before, then cure until healed; but if it is wounded, and pierced by an object, and experiences great pain, you must first dress the wound; afterward cut away the nail with a sharp spatula by slicing crosswise above, taking care not to reach the flesh beneath the nail, for the patient would feel too much pain; and should this happen, apply some soothing remedy.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain of the wrist joint of the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The two extra fingers that grow in some people's hands may be very fleshy, and sometimes there is also bone, and occasionally they have nails, and any of these can appear at the root of the knuckle or on various parts of the hand.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	Those that grow in the palm of the hand do not move, but those born at the knuckle may sometimes move; the size of the fleshy ones is so slight as to be measured by a broad spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	Those born at the root of the knuckle are difficult to treat, so be careful to cut them out.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	For the one that grows in the back of the hand, you must first cut away the surrounding flesh down to the bone, then cut out the bone with an appropriate saw, and treat it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The swellings that come to the fingers together come through birth, or by sudden wounding, or by burning with fire, or by similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	You must cut this suture so that the edges may repair themselves according to their natural forms; then place between them two tent-like dressings dampened with rose oil, so they do not stick together; or you can put between them two pieces of fine lead until the areas are sutured as they ought.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If swelling comes to anyone's palm of the hand, cut this suture as is necessary.
des vils	weakly.
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	Worms are large open ulcers filled with melancholic humours which come to many body parts; and they occur more often in the legs of those who walk and labour and carry burdens than others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Thus you must administer to him sometimes purging of bile, and then heal with holy water.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The treatment with iron is done in two ways: one is to cauterize it, and draw out the black blood; and the other way is that you open a vein, and drain all of its blood.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The incision is done in this manner: first bathe the leg with very hot water until its flesh becomes soft, then pull the patient's limb from above the thigh down to below the knee; then cut open a vein, either in one place or two or three, with a wide opening, then raise it and draw out the black blood by hand, from one end to the other, so much as the nature of the patient can withstand; and then bind it up, and instruct him to abstain from eating meat that produces dark bile; and repeat the evacuation and healing when the veins are full again, which harms the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The care of the wound is as follows: remove the patient's leg hair if it has a lot, then place it in a bath. Warm the leg with hot water until it reddens and veins swell. If no tub is at hand warm it by fire, then cut across the vein from knee to ankle or below the ankle. Then make an incision on the skin using a sharp blade and strip off pieces of the vein as they become exposed; you will see them red and black, and when they enter under the skin they look like white cords. Next push a rod underneath until they are raised above the surface of the skin then cut lightly with another blade three inches higher up, then make an incision in the skin over the vein so that it is visible. Then remove it with a hook as before; cut into another place two or three inches higher and remove it again. Cut at the toe joint, pull upwards until you reach the second incision, then remove section by section until the whole has been removed. If this cannot be done by pulling and lifting insert a needle with a strong thread doubled over and tie them together, push beneath a rod and turn your hand from side to side so that they come out. Be careful not to cut since if you do they can't be pulled or lifted and harm will result for the patient. When all have been removed place wool moistened in wine and rose oil on top of the wound and treat until it is healed
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if the muscle is contracted and twisted and rolled up together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must cut it open with a twisting motion, but do not cut it off; and treat it as we have mentioned before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The shape of the iron with which one cuts the muscle is curved, and does not slice, so as not to cut the vein; it has a large curve because if it were thin, it would cut through the vein. It should be thick like we have said before, and this is its form:
de la voinne civile	Of the civil vein.
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is entangled in the legs and hot parts where there are no plants or trees growing; it exists also in lands with little moisture. Sometimes they occur elsewhere than in the legs, like the rot that comes from underneath the skin. It occurs within the body as serpents and worms do, bred under the skin's surface.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the sign of the beginning of this vein is that a great inflammation comes to the leg, then its color changes, and the vein starts to protrude outwardly, like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	When the vein opens up, you must wrap around it a piece of lead that is three and a half to two inches long, tie it, and leave the lead hanging on the leg; every time some of it comes out, wrap it again with the lead, and if it's too long, cut off a part of it, and re-wrap the rest, but do not cut its root, until all of it is removed; for if you cut it, it will go back into the flesh, causing abscesses, rotting in place, and serious illness. For this reason, it must be treated little by little up to the top, leaving no part inside the body. This vein can sometimes be five palms long, or ten, and a man came to me once whose was ten palms long; when you cut it, one root or a hole comes out of it, and pierce through until all is removed, and empty its contents, then treat the place with medicines that prevent rotting for some time, then cure it like abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	For this wound is very slight and particularly when it appears in the ankle joint or foot, and from there a lot of discharge comes out, and thus must be drained; treat it therefore as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	Worms that are born between the skin and flesh.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called "ox disease" in our land because it often happens to oxen, and it is a small worm that is born between the skin and flesh, and it travels throughout the body up and down, and one feels its movement from limb to limb, until it bursts through the skin where it was, and must be removed; and it is caused by the putrefaction of certain humors, just as worms, snakes, grubs, and ascarides are born in the belly; and its malice is feared, for when it travels through the body, and reaches the head, and enters the eye, it can destroy the eye; this happens often.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see it being cured and drained, one cannot wait until the time is right: therefore, you must tightly bind the location above and below with a strong bond, then cut above and drain it thoroughly, and if the pus is deep within the flesh, but not found, cauterize it with fire until it dies; its most harmful effect being that it runs into the eye as we have stated, and if you see it coming towards the head near the eye, tightly pinch the eyebrow underneath, then cut above, and drain it thoroughly. The patient must use body-purifying medications to get rid of harmful humors, and should avoid foods which encourage rot.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	Of the pain that arises from windiness.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This illness is called "vakirir" in our land and it's a pain that appears in some limbs and can move from limb to limb, which I saw myself.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to see a sick woman and she uncovered her arm for me, I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm and then I watched it crawl upwards like a worm towards the shoulder; more specifically, it moved like silver when melted from one place to another as the pain left that area and lodged itself at her shoulder before coursing through the rest of her body until it reached the other arm. She said she felt like it was now spinning around in her torso which I could see.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was amazed at how it moved from limb to limb as I had never seen this illness behave in such a way before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	Toutevoie, I had wanted many that were well to move the pain from one place to another, but I had not wished for it myself, just as I saw in the woman; and I thought it was because a woman has a dry body and uncovered veins, which is why this forced windiness appears; and according to this reasoning, they do not appear in those who are fat and have moist bodies and covered veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you treat this illness, and the patient feels that pain, if it opens as we have said, then tie over and under tightly, and then press above until that forced windiness comes out; cauterize the spot; and if you cannot see it with your eyes, cure it by what causes windiness, such as fetid pills, serapin pills, and similar others.
des saiettes	Of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, according to their appearances and the parts of the body they pierce.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The diversity of arrows lies in the fact that there are those with large points, small ones, and barbed; some have two edges, others have long barbs; there are those made up of pieces; and the arrow that pierces any part of the body does so in two ways: either it pierces a vital organ, such as the brain, heart, liver, lungs, kidneys, intestines, bladder, or similar organs.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When the arrow pierces any of these organs, and you notice the signs of death that I will tell you about below, it is necessary for you to beware of extracting this arrow, as many die in various circumstances; and when these ominous signs are not apparent, and the arrow is not deeply embedded, then draw it out and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the sign of brain injury when an arrow falls and pierces the bone, and exposes the dura mater that covers the brain, is when there is blindness, stiffness, and dizziness in one eye, inflammation and redness, swelling, and redness of the tongue, spasms, clouding of consciousness, vomiting bile; and perhaps blood flows from the nostrils or ears; and possibly they lose their speech and voice; also pus discharges from the wound white like pulps, as well as charred flesh; when these signs appear to you, keep away from treatment, and treat the arrow if it is still in there.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The sign of the arrow when it strikes the heart is that it appears near the left breast, and feels as if it were embedded in a hard object, not empty; and perhaps the arrow moves with each heartbeat, dark blood flows out, coldness and cold sweat appear, and syncope: know then without doubt that death is imminent.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign that the arrowhead has not pierced the lung is when there is no foam-free discharge from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient's complexion changes, and they breathe heavily and seek cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrowhead falls onto the under-side of the shoulder blade, it is near the small ribs; it causes great pain and disturbance, and the patient gasps; and all the limbs from the shoulders move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrowhead falls onto the stomach, perhaps something undigested of the meat comes out through the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrowhead falls onto the belly, and no excrement comes out through the rectum, there is no hope in its treatment or extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow falls into the bladder, and the urine jumps out forcefully, and the patient experiences severe pain; know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limb, like the arm and collar bone, throat, shoulder, scapula, spine of the back, ribs, thigh, and legs; these limbs are protected according to many precautions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in a nerve or artery and it is not poisoned, as I will tell you happened to me, so that you may do likewise.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened to a man that an arrow fell on his arm, at the root of the elbow: I seized it and drew it out from below the ear fat, and he was healed without issue.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And thrust into an eye a small arrow that had lodged in the fat beneath the paper underneath, and the arrow was blunt, and it could only be reached with its tip towards the shaft, and the arrow was large, of Turkish make, all iron, light without barbs; the wound healed, and no ill consequences befell him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And drew an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and it was an Arabian arrow with barbs; I dressed the wound, and extracted it carefully, and the Christian healed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And drew an arrow from a man, that had pierced his belly, and I thought he would die; but after thirty days, there was no change in his condition; so I cut into the arrow's path, guided it out, and extracted it, and he suffered no ill effects.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if you see a man with an arrow lodged in his back or shoulder, and the wound has healed over it; yet the arrow remains inside him, causing no change to its natural position nor finding any harm in any of his natural functions.
