Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And see another man with an arrow lodged in his face, the wound has healed over it, yet he remains without suffering great pain or any other similar discomforts.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And treat an arrow wound for the king's prince where it had entered between his nostrils, leaning slightly to the right; the arrow was completely buried within him and I was called in after three days to perform treatment.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound to be very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I sought it diligently throughout its entire subtle tent, and did not feel it; and he felt pricking and pain beneath his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was the tip of the arrowhead I applied an attractive and digestive poultice there so that the flesh would not swell; and the flesh around the arrowhead appeared to me.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I left the poultice there for several days, and the wound healed immediately, and so the patient remained well for a long time, until he felt the arrowhead one day inside his nostril; and he told me this.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I applied to the wound a corrosive medicine for many days until it was open, and I tried [to extract], and felt the tip of the arrowhead which was emerging in that place; then I adjusted at the opening of the wound with this corrosive medicine until the head of the arrowhead became visible to me; and its shaft lasted over four months, and then so enlarged did the wound become that I inserted pincers into it, and moved them from side to side but it could not be extracted; then I ceased not to apply skill and ingenuity using various instruments, until one day with well-made pincers, according to how their form will finally appear in this chapter, until I dragged [the arrowhead] out and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And the surgeon judges that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored; then I would restore it, and the wound is sutured, and the patient is healed entirely.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Or I have told you the quality of extracting some arrows, so that you direct your attention to what I do not say, for books cannot cover everything; but wise masters compare many great things, and for what is missing or present, they invent new procedures and instruments, when encountering unfamiliar situations in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows do not exit the members in which they are stuck for two manners: either through the place where they enter or by another part; and those that must come out through where they entered, these are arrows entering fleshy parts, and this can sometimes be done immediately.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it does not come out now, let it remain until the flesh around is rotten and the outlet is loosened; and also, if it is embedded in bone and cannot exit, let it stay like that for some days, moving it each day; then it will come out, but if it does not come out, pierce all around with a fine bore until the surrounding tissue is enlarged, and then draw it forth.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	If the arrow is embedded in the bone of the head and reaches one of the ventricles of the brain, and any of the accidents I have mentioned appear in the patient: do not draw it forth but leave it until it becomes even after some days; for if the arrow comes near the surface, this means death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is not stuck solely in the bone and does not reach the surface, and the patient remains free of any ill effects for several days, then devise a means to extract it.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is deeply embedded and cannot be extracted externally, then administer the escharotics around as I have told you; afterward treat the wound until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is buried within the body where it cannot be seen, then search for it thoroughly in all directions; and if you can feel it, then extract it with a suitable instrument; and if you are unable due to the tightness of the wound or because of the depth of penetration by the arrow without damaging bone or nerves, then cut away flesh until the wound is large enough; next remove the arrow if possible, and if there are barbs that prevent its withdrawal, then carefully remove the flesh caught on both sides as far as you can before breaking off or bending back these barbs so that they can be removed; finally extract the arrow gently to avoid breakage which would cause more damage.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it at once, leave it until the surrounding tissue is rotten, then pull it out, for its extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the loss of blood makes it difficult for you, apply what we have said about treatment in its own chapter; avoid cutting into nerves or veins, and use any method that allows you to draw out the arrow without danger, quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; place the patient according to how they were positioned when the arrow struck them, because this is the greatest aid there is, and if you cannot, then let nature take its course as indicated by the signs.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	An arrow that comes from elsewhere and shows no sign of itself, or the skin there is swollen if you see or feel it obviously: cut above until forceps can grasp it, then pull it out: this will now be easy.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is retained in the bone, then turn your hand roundly until it enters the bone, and widen the bone, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	If it cannot come out, then leave it alone again, and then restart the extraction process until it comes out; and if there was an arrow inside, push it through the whole shaft; and if the head has fallen off but you need to administer a pushing technique, use a tapered instrument so that the point of the arrow enters the taper of the instrument; then push it through, and if the arrow is tapered, insert your instrument with the pointed end first to ease the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is poisoned, you must cut away all the flesh around it if you can, then treat the wound as necessary.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow falls on the foot or thigh or stomach or bladder or side, and it is close by, and you can cut above it, then cut; be careful not to cut the vein or nerve, then extract it, and close the wound if necessary; treat it until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the pincers used to extract arrows resembles the beak of a bird, as you see here: [image]
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	There are many types of these pincers: large, medium, and small, depending on the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the wooden wedge is also like a bird's feather, to push against the tip of the arrow, as shown here in this image: [image]
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The shape of the pincers for extracting and probing is as follows:
des voinnes dou cors communes	Veins of the body common to all.
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	There are thirty-one veins in the body which can be used for bleeding, of these there are sixteen in the head, that is to say: two jugulars situated behind the ears, called "herbech"; and two arteries appearing at the temples; and two veins situated on the cheekbones beside each eye, called "aspires"; and a vein located in the middle of the forehead; and a vein at the top of the nose; and two glands which are found under the jaw; and two veins that appear above the lips, these are known as "augeherich"; and two veins underneath the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins that are commonly treated for healing purposes are five in each arm: one is the cephalic vein, which is located on the left side; lay people call it "the vein of the head". The median vein is called the "fast" by laymen and is composed of the cephalic and basilic veins. Laypeople refer to this as the “heart vein”; while the basilic resides in the right arm and laypeople name it “the belly vein”. It lies on the flexor surface, being that which is used for healing, appearing visibly at the wrist.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the salvator is the vein that lies between the little finger and ring finger, containing two branches. In the leg there are three veins: one runs underneath the curvature of the hollow on the left side, another the sophic running at the ankle of the right side; while the third named the "nassa" is in the other ankle. On the opposite leg lie three more beneath these.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The bleeding of the veins that are behind the ears aids in treating chronic catarrh and headaches; and regarding the qualities of bloodletting, as I told you, it involves raising the patient's head and rubbing the area where the veins are with a rough cloth; then restrain the patient's neck with a bandage so that the two veins appear behind the ears at two points dependent on the head: feel them with your finger, and where you sense the pulse beneath your finger, make an incision there; then take the lancet, insert it below the vein until reaching bone, then raise your hand along the entire length of the vein, and cut both the skin and the vein deeply twice across, allowing blood to flow as much as you wish; then remove the instrument and bind [the wound] tightly until healing occurs. I have already discussed incision and cauterization in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	The bleeding of the two arteries that are in the temples is beneficial for treating an old and severe migraine, as well as chronic eye inflammation and acute tearing from the eyes; the qualities of this bleeding are as follows: the patient must stretch their neck so that the two veins appear clearly; feel the pulse beneath your finger, then bleed upwards from there; raise your heart above the vein with your index finger and insert the lancet below it, raising the vein as you did for the other two veins, and let the blood flow according to your need; release the patient, applying pressure to the wound with your finger for an hour before covering it in cotton wool; then bind it tightly and leave until healed. We have spoken of their cutting and removal at the beginning of this book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The bleeding of the vein on the forehead is as valuable as the bleeding of the cephalic vein for ancient diseases of the face, and for migraine, and for redness; and its quality is such that the patient tightens their neck by twisting it until the vein appears; then take the instrument which is called a "digging tool", of which this is the form:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	Place the point over the vein and press it down with your hand or something else, allowing blood to flow according to the desired quantity; then release the patient's neck and bind the wound until it is healthy, but never use a wide flame for this operation.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, the flame should not be too sharp, and one must bleed with caution because the bone is close by, and if the flame is delicate it might break when in contact with the bone.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The bleeding of the two veins that are in the temples helps with eye ailments, scabs, redness, and swelling in the eyes, as well as diseases of the face; and the quality of this bleeding is such that the patient should strain their neck by twisting it with some cloth, as mentioned before; then bleed them, and make the incision crosswise, a little above the width of a finger and somewhat broad, for there is no flesh there.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the veins are delicate, they may break accidentally; then make an incision in another place of bloodletting, as much as you need, and afterwards tie it with cotton, and bind it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	Bleeding the vein of the nose is beneficial for fever, sudden madness, and diseases of the face, such as migraine and facial redness, especially when it is chronic; and the quality of this bleeding is that the patient should strain their neck, then pinch their nose with your left hand, and take a delicate long vein, insert it in between the lips in the space between the two nostrils, for the vein does not open there very well, and the blood will now begin to flow; do not go too deep, and bleed as much as you need, then bind it for one night, because it heals quickly; this is the shape of the incision:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The bleeding of the two arteries aids in the widening of the throat, and at the beginning of surgery, and in many diseases, and gout, and gangrene, and herpes, and tumors; and the quality of the bleeding is such that the patient must tighten his neck beneath either one, as we have said; and let the masters be standing on top of the patient's head, and the patient sit on a chair, then open the vein for a long length generously, then draw out the blood moderately, or as much as needed; then redo this in the other vein, then untie the binding, and tighten around the veins gently, so that the patient does not choke; and leave him until morning, when the wound is healed.
de la sainie des leivres	The bleeding of the lips
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The bleeding of veins on the upper lip helps with glue in the mouth and gum corruption, and fissures of lips and nose and around it.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the quality of bleeding is to make the patient sit in front of you and hold their neck as I said; then turn the lip and look at the two veins, one on the right upper lip and the other on the left, and they are known for being black and having small black veins around them: so cut both, and if you do not know them or have doubts, just cut the thicker of each side, and treat similarly the two veins above and below as it is the same procedure.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	Of bleeding under the tongue.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The bleeding of veins below the tongue is beneficial after bleeding from the cephalic vein, and it is done at the narrowing of the throat, for diseases of the eye, and diseases of the mouth; the quality of the bleeder is that the patient should sit between your hands facing the sun, lift their tongue, and look underneath on each side a black vein: so bleed one and the other, but do not go too deep, for beneath are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins of the neck that are commonly bled are bled in two ways: either by piercing with a blunt-ended wide instrument, or with a sharp olive-shaped one like you described, and is called an "anesil"; they are wide and narrow according to the width and constriction of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of Martin's flame is very renowned, and it is so wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it is necessary to open the thick veins filled with coarse blood that contains clots; and this is the form of the olive flame:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	it is more pointed and slender, and it is for bleeding the delicate veins where there is thin yellow blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The bleeding of the basilica vein, which is one of these veins, aids in treating illnesses below the throat, neck, stomach, and belly; and the bleeder must take care to avoid the artery that lies beneath it.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if he cuts the artery and a flow of blood ensues, it must be stopped as I have said; and the flame must not be tight, but loose like a needle.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the vein does not open clearly, you must extract it and change to another one; or you can take a piece of it for analysis, or heal the wound in its place within the arm: it will then open clearly; and treat the inflammation as we have described.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you wish to determine the location of the wound, then you must first extend the arm and touch the area until you feel the pulse; mark this spot with a sign, and then bind the arm, treating the inflammation as we have said; make sure not to cut into the artery when you see the spot swollen, for that is indeed the artery: avoid it.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it protruding like a child's urine, and the blood is red and thin, know that it is arterial blood: act quickly then, and place your finger on it for some time, then remove your finger if the bleeding stops, which often happens; bind the arm and leave it be, without moving it, and keep the patient still; remain fearful, and do not move them until they are healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the blood is not stanched and it overpowers you, cut the artery if it is exposed, for it will save your life; and staunch the blood.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	Take a fustic bark and split it, then take one half and bind it onto the wound until the next day; if the blood is stanched, that is good; if not, treat it as we have said with hemostatic powders; and do not worry about staunching the blood in many conditions due to the small size of the wound and the strength of the arm's ligament.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The bleeding of the vein in the middle helps as it draws blood from the head above and the body below, because it is composed of the basilica and cephalic veins as we have said; and the bleeder must be careful not to cut too deeply into the nerve that lies beneath, for if they hit it and cause swelling, the incision will be severe and may not heal; this nerve often appears but sometimes does not due to its subtlety, so you must use an anesthetic tool and avoid cutting the nerve as much as possible.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, make a long cut to open it.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The bleeding of the cephalic vein is beneficial as it draws blood from the head and aids the eyes; one should bleed by puncturing at the olive branch or the myrtle twig because this is the safest of all veins, for beneath lies neither nerve nor artery.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	Nevertheless, it is best to choose the lightest spot and not press too hard if one misses the first time, then restart; sometimes the vein may swell in some people when pricked for the first time, but this does no harm.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of bleeding depends on your judgment.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you should know about bloodletting is that it is not administered except to maintain health and avoid future illnesses; and the bloodletting must be performed on one of the three veins, namely: the cephalic, the median cubital, and the basilic; and one must bleed in the early morning while fasting, and in autumn or winter after eating when signs of fullness are apparent; and bleeding should take place either on the first day or third day between two and three hours after the meal.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	Bloodletting performed for illnesses has no specific time of day, but rather whenever necessary, be it day or night, at any hour and all times; and one must not bleed children under the age of fourteen, nor a woman carrying a child from the fourth month until the seventh.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	They ought not to be bled who are aged over sixty years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when anyone wishes to be bled, in any manner whatsoever, it is necessary that he cleanse his intestines with a light clyster, if he has much retained faeces, so that the veins do not draw from the intestines harmful superfluities damaging to vital organs; nor ought one who is excessively saturated with meats, or drunken, to be bled until soberness returns, or he who suffers from dropsy; and beware of bleeding after an attack of colic, vomiting, diarrhoea, excessive intercourse, travail, wakefulness, fasting, and also those whose strength has been exhausted by the sword or by the body; then purify the humours, if the blood is thick, through meats and beverages and medicines, provided you have the power to do so; then enter a bath, unless something prevents it, in order to purify the blood, and bleed from that vein on the back of the hand which we have mentioned; and guard against work, exertion, lust, and similar things on that day; be cheerful and joyful, and let the bleeder be higher than him who is being bled, and let him rub his arm twice or thrice, then bind the bandage slightly above medium tightness, because if it is too tight or constricted blood cannot flow out; and then rub the place with your hands until the veins swell, and are perceived; then moisten the bleeder's thumb with a little old oil, then place thy forefinger of thy left hand on that vein below the place where bleeding is to take place lest it should fail when struck;
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	For there are veins that flow like cords to the bleeding, and some are filled with windiness, so much so when one applies a flame it retracts from the flame, and cannot open the vein; thus it is for these [people]; and if one opens the wound, then the wound is too narrow, therefore the surgeons must be mindful of such things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the wound opens on the first try, it is good; but if not, start again a little below or above that place, unless the places are swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the place is swollen and the patient is afraid, leave it for one or two days, without binding his arm: perhaps hot abscesses will appear; do not put them in a bath, then restart the bleeding if he wishes to; and if the opening is small, let the blood flow gently out and you doubt that it does not come as much as you wish, blow right into that same hole with all your breath; and do this slightly above, rather than where the place is swollen; for this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the place swollen, do not restart the incision, and apply a poultice of oil's egg white, for it lightens the body from blood, and is suitable in this place the egg white which the oil contains; and thus administer the egg white of oil in every incision that you heal the veins, to staunch the flow of blood; and the same does triacle and flax seed, when applied to the place; so subtly the blood contracts and separates when it is too large.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if there comes a large abscess, which happens often, especially when it has not been previously incised other than this time or the opening of the vein is small, you should hasten and apply to the place moistened sponge in water and saltpeter a little warm, and press it for an hour; and you must do this after the blood has drained from the wound, and if it remains at the place after some days a blackish color or greenish, do not harm; and when seen, apply something of aloe or myrrh softened in calament juice, pustule, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And often there are abscesses and appearances in the wound of the basilica: so place your hand on it, and if you find the area soft under pressure from the hand, then this appearance is bad.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Avoid anything that might block the artery, but apply a dry poultice to harden the area, then treat it with another remedy until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	Draw out the blood according to its quantity and the colour of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the blood is black, let it out until it becomes red; and if you see it as thick, then let it flow until it thins; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And for one who is full and robust, requiring bloodletting, make a larger wound for him, and let the flames be broad; but do the opposite for someone weak, letting them bleed less often and in small amounts, and always cut across rather than prick; this method of bleeding is safer against loss of blood or cutting of nerves, and it's better than long or wide incisions.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	For one whose body requires bleeding, give moist bread dipped in pomegranate juice; if they are heated, take blood three or four times from them; and if they are of a cold complexion, eat soaked bread in spiced syrup, or aromatic honey syrup with spices like pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, and fragrant syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if he faints during the operation after a great loss of blood, it is necessary that he inhales beef broth, and subtle scented syrup, and uses other things that we have mentioned in the division or chapter on syncope for venous evacuation.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wishes to bleed out his arm, and operate another time, it is necessary that when he is weakened by great bleeding, he bleeds little by little according to the quantity of his strength continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And if he wishes to bleed his arm after the first operation, and has a strong constitution, it is recommended that he bleeds seven hours after the first bleeding or after nine hours.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And if he wishes to bleed from another part of the body, it must be done on the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	For it has too much blood within the body which is already heated, and brings on fever; so one must draw out a great quantity, and enlarge the opening until it stops bleeding; then you should follow all the conditions of healing, and place your hand on their pulse as they heal, so that death does not come to the place of bandaging, and this happens many times when the healer is negligent; and it is not right when you want to free the arm and make blood flow a second time, and the opening is closed, that you press hard upon it; nor if it is curved should you extend the arm forcefully, for this would be bad; but leave it until it heals a second time; or you may prick at the tip of the flame, so that the blood which is congealed escapes from the vein's opening, and apply on it a little salt soaked in water, and press lightly upon it.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the wound is swollen, leave it alone and do not constrict it until the abscess subsides.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if it is necessary to draw blood a second time, then drain it from the same place, or from another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein between the arms is drained in place of the one on the head because it is composed [of two].
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	The method of draining is as follows: the patient immerses their hand in warm water until the vessels are red; then they are tied gently so that the vein stands out well, and now it is drained across the width, neither too narrow nor too wide; the opening should be broad, and the blood should be drained very close to the joint of the hand, and if blood cannot escape, immerse the hand in warm water again and let the blood flow into the water until you have enough; and if this is done during winter, do not re-immerse the hand in hot water, because it is more often used in winter than summer; and draining from this vein is safer than any other veins, for there are neither arteries nor nerves here.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The bleeding of the savatel of the right hand is beneficial for all diseases of the liver, and this is how it is done: withdraw the hand, and immerse it in hot water until the vein is swollen, if one can see it; and if the vein runs obliquely, and you cut through from end to end, it causes no harm; but do not go too deeply, for the nerves are underneath completely denuded of flesh, and then return the hand to hot water if the blood is congealed in the wound, and cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have bled from the blood as much as is necessary for you, put oil and linen on the vein to weld the wound, and do so with each ray.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The bleeding of the one on the left hand is beneficial for the disease of the spleen, and do everything just as I told you regarding the right [hand].
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The draining of the spleen is beneficial for all diseases that are below the body, such as diseases of the womb, retention of urine, kidney disease, and similar ailments in the thighs and legs.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the quality of its drainage is that the patient should immerse their foot in hot water and rub over the vein until it bursts, and bind it above the ankle joint; this vein is located at the ankle, and above the foot there are many kidneys; drain either the larger kidney or at the ankle, whichever you prefer.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you drain it above the foot, be careful of the nerves that are underneath, and drain it transversely just like cutting; let the flames cool down a little.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the blood cannot escape, return the foot to the water, and let the vein empty completely.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the incision fails the first time, begin again a little higher for the skin is salty; do not be concerned about nerves as we have said, and perform likewise on the sole of the other foot equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The skin of the sciatic vein is found at the back of the ankle, and its incision relieves pain in the hip when it is due to hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And the quality of this incision is that the patient must enter the bath, and hold above the ankle for four days by twisting, for otherwise the vein will not open; and if it does open, then lance it in all ways possible, and transversely; it is better to cut than probe, because the skin is salty, and veins are very responsive to manual treatment.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you do not find it, then cauterize any line of the calf that appears at the back of the foot or towards the little toe and beware of nerves; make sure blood flows from your wound as much as possible, then undo the ligature and place cotton on top to compress. It is now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	Cupping incisions.
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Cupping tools are made of horn, or brass, or glass and cupping is performed in two ways: either by piercing to draw out blood without incision, or without perforating the skin.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this non-piercing cupping is performed in two ways: either using only fire or without it; and the piercing cupping with blood extraction is done on 14 parts of the body, one being at the top of the head; another mid-neck; two others on sides of neck; a cup under the chin; cups over both shoulders; cups on hips; cups in middle of arms; cups on legs; and cups on ankles. The cupping draws blood from small veins that are scattered across flesh, and this does not cause weakness as vein incisions do, and should not be administered with fire or without it for any illness caused by excess unless the whole body is first emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if due to the necessity of illness one must be cupped, or for habit, we administer it every hour at the beginning of the month, or towards the end, and in between; for there are those who, when they need to be cupped, have a heavy head; and there are some who experience fullness and redness on their face, and on their neck, and darkness around the eyes; and there are some who find a drop of blood in their mouth, and have an inflamed tongue, and vomit blood; and there are those who dream, and see at night blood and wounds and dead people and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and especially when it is towards the middle of the month, we order that they be cupped after three hours during the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The bleeding of the nose helps with the cracked skin ... that reaches the eyes, and it should not be done after the evacuation of all the body's blood; this venesection is in place of bleeding from the temporal artery, and it should not be used by those of cold complexion or who have a cough, as it causes them great harm; for this reason, the elderly should not use it nor those with cold ailments in their head.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who bleed often become forgetful, so the cupping glass should be placed a little lower due to the fear of forgetfulness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	Bleeding from the neck is in place of bleeding from the head and the basilic vein, and for this reason, it is beneficial for narrowing of the bladder, ruptures in the intestinal canal, coughs, and fullness; and one must be careful not to press too hard, as holding it too tightly can cause forgetfulness or stomach and heart problems.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	The ventousation of the two collarbones is useful for headaches, eye inflammation, migraines, and throat constriction, as well as pain in the roots of teeth, and it is located on the basilica vein; you must instruct the physician to apply his hand carefully so that he does not cut the artery or cause excessive bleeding.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	Ventousation below the chin is useful for mouth diseases, gum inflammation and similar oral ailments; it is located on the two labial veins.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	Ventousation of the shoulders helps with illnesses brought about by heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	Ventousation of the armpits is as effective as the three veins of the arm because it draws blood from these large vessels; instruct the physician not to apply it directly or too strongly since the area is bare skin and has many nerves and arteries underneath.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The cupping glass that is placed on the hip is beneficial for haemorrhoids of the anus and ailments below, and it must be large and made of copper to ensure good suction; but if it were thin it would break and cause large wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The cupping glasses on the legs clearly heal, for they draw blood from the entire body and are beneficial for chronic pains of the kidneys, bladder, and uterus; and they should be placed on the two hips and two ankles, but prolonged use weakens the body and causes fainting in many conditions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The method of applying the cupping glass is as follows: first apply it to an empty space and suck swiftly, then press firmly and move evenly, continuing without ceasing until you see the area red and swollen with the appearance of blood; then remove, and replace the cups taking care according to the condition of the body since some have thick skin while others thin pores; strike only once, making wide and somewhat deep wounds; and suck gently.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the blood is thick, it is necessary to strike twice: the first time to thin out the path of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the blood is very dense, it is necessary to strike a third time; and when we wish to draw out a little blood at a time, we are content with only one blow.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we wish to draw out a lot of blood, we must strike often; and if the blood is dense, pierce fully, and the end result is that the heart is suddenly pierced, and it is necessary for one who has thick and hard skin, and whose pores are narrow, that you anoint the cups of the leeches with apertif and dissolutive oil: if it is in summer, violet oil, or almond oil, or pumpkin seed oil; and if it is in winter, cress oil, or lily oil, or chamomile oil, or something similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess is large and cold, take oil of amaranth, or balm, or aniseed oil, and similar oils.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the wound has tender flesh and large pores, do not apply oil but wash it after the fomentation with rosewater, or cold water, or black nightshade water, or squash water, or china root water, or any similar solution.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And for those with excessive moisture, rise easily with myrtle water, or sumac water, and similar solutions.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And for those with large swellings, rise with old wine, or water of violets, or aniseed decoction, or chamomile, and other similar things; one should not be cupped before a bath nor during the bath, but after the bath by one or two hours; they must not sleep after fomentation, and it is necessary that they walk about when they are to be cupped and when they have been cupped.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And watch out if the patient is choleric and has an excess of hot blood or inflamed blood; in such cases, they should consume cold foods like pomegranates, endives, lettuce, similar things, as well as mint sauce, pork, and moist meat.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And for those with a cold constitution, give them honey syrup and medium-bodied aromatic wine that is neither old nor new, consume less meat, eat mint sauce, small birds, and pigeons; on the day they are cupped, they should drink more than they eat; sometimes one must give some men treacle or nutmeg before or after cupping to strengthen their vital organs; their blood may be thin but those with hot constitutions should not drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The cups that are applied without injury are those placed on the liver, and on the chest, podagra, and on the abdomen, spleen, kidneys, and hip, for these members do not tolerate being struck upon, and it is only to draw blood from member to member, as we place them on the breasts when the child nurses; to remove the viscosity that is in the member, as we apply cups on the abdomen and on the spleen to reduce the member's size; and alleviate pain, where there is an obstruction or stone, by perhaps removing the obstruction through its attractive virtue, or causing the stone to move from its place; and thus it acts when placed on the liver and on the chest in cases of retained windiness. These cups are administered empty for sucking only; sometimes they are administered together with fire, and some are filled with warm water as in cases of pleurisy, and such is how one fills the cup with lukewarm water or water in which appropriate herbs have been cooked.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The method of administering fire cupping is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And it should be two fingers wide and half a palm in depth, with a small hole on the side near the middle, just big enough to insert a needle, and made of brass, soft enough so that it does not injure the patient when applied to the limb; and there should be a rod across the middle made of brass or iron, for holding a burning candle wick, and these may be large or small depending on the illness and age of those who use them; because cupping for children is different than for the elderly, and for the thin compared to the obese.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	One should thus apply this cup as follows: take a candle of wax or a linen wick and place it across the rod inside the cup so that the flame is at the bottom to avoid burning the patient; then put it on the limb with your two fingers over the hole we mentioned, so that when you want to, you can let out the vapors, and remove the cup; take the wick as before and repeat often if necessary.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the cupping treatment used for pleurisy, it is always applied in acute cases, has no rod or opening, and is only administered when it is full of water, being placed on the affected limb solely. And this is its form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Cupping glasses are only used where cupping cannot be applied due to the smallness of the limb, such as lips and gums, and similar areas; also on denuded surfaces, like toes or fingers, and others resembling them; and their use is such that when you find blisters filled with clear sweet water without any scum, take them; place them in clean water for a night until they are familiarized and have nothing in their wombs; then open the vein and cupping wound, rub the limb until it is red, and put on the cups; and when they are full and fall off, if it is where cupping can be applied, apply it there, because this is much better afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If not, lift the wound gently with water and then salt, very well, and afterward let it air out; if there is still too much blood flowing after washing, wet a linen cloth in cold water and place it on top until the bleeding stops; but if the blood has multiplied, use crushed vitriol or gallstones and similar things to stop the flow; instead, you can apply half of the peeled beans over the wound and leave them there until they dry out at the location; and finally, if necessary, take more swabs.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the swabs will not take, rub over the fresh blood or stick a needle into it so that some blood comes out and then place them on top; as soon as they sense the blood, they dry out; when you see that they fall off, sprinkle powder made from aloes and ground psyllium, or ashes, now they shall dry out.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here we have the book of fractures.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it deals with the restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know, dear son, that the foolish surgeon who ignores this chapter will never see any of the ancient books, nor read letters from them; and for this reason, knowledge is lost in our land, as I have never found a single good one; and I know nothing more than what I learned from the science of those ancient books, which I studied so much that I acquired knowledge, and through experience and practice in my life; and I have described to you in this chapter everything it contains, I have summarized it at the end, and clearly shown the shapes of the instruments used, as I did in these two previous chapters.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is necessary then that we state in the prologue of this book the main points and the chapters where the sage puts his understanding, and remains focused on the truth, so that those who are experienced may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	When any fracture or dislocation or twisting or rupture occurs in someone, you must hasten to bleed the patient on one side and the other, unless something prevents it, such as physical weakness, childhood, old age; or if the weather is too hot, or too cold; avoid eating cold foods, like cold porridge, goat cheese, and do not drink wine, eat no fatty meats, and do not overindulge in meat that fills the veins with blood until you are certain there is no hot abscess, nor a spreading of matter into the limb; then may the patient return to their initial state of health as they have always done.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary that one feeds the patient with meats that have high nutritional value and are rich in fat, such as boiled wheat in water, rice, eggs, chicken feet, cow stomach, duck eggs, fresh fish, strong wine, and similar foods.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For if too much nutrition is taken, the healing process can be hindered and the fracture may occur again sooner.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that the broken bones of elderly and decrepit individuals cannot heal or fuse properly according to their natural bone density due to the weakness of their limbs; this also applies to those with overly tender bones, such as young children; but there is no cure, so one must apply large metal clamps which clamp down on the broken bone and keep the limb in place until it regains its former strength; do not remove these at all during the process, and for this reason they should be fed rich meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are diverse in many ways.
