Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from that of the arm, or the leg, and I shall tell you in this chapter all the ways fractures can occur.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is fracture that requires splinting, and another by sharpening, just like the cut of a quill to write.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if fracture with wound, and fracture with just a slight crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And for each type, there is its own method and proper tool for restoration, according to how the bone recalls its place; and bone fracture is known by the twisting of alignment, clearly seen from outside, and heard when pressed with hand; and if there is no twist or sound on touch, and the patient feels little pain, then it may not be a break; but could still have a twist, crack, or small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	You must not move it by hand, but apply the medicines that follow here, and then hold it firmly yet gently.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And know that the fracture which goes around in a circle, with its two parts disjoined, must now be brought back together evenly, otherwise hot abscesses will form there; and if hot abscesses do occur, leave it alone for one day until the abscess is eased; then reset it gently and skillfully, and know that its recovery is easier than that of those which have pieces; hold it as described below.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if there are pieces broken in the bone, stretch it in two parts, whether hand or foot, or with your hand if it is a small limb, or with two levers, or one lever and by hand; place the member according to its natural shape so that when the broken parts of the limb are apart, bring them together using all devices at your disposal as skillfully as you can, taking care not to cause any further injury or pain to the patient; fit the two ends of bone well according to their best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And he feels it well with his hand if it seems to you that it is not right: so gently straighten it, and do not hold or press too tightly, as those who cause hot abscesses and contractions in the limb through their work often do.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the limb is in place, admonish the patient well not to move it, neither while awake nor sleeping, turning over, or in any other way; and watch closely that the limb is so secure that they feel no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when they feel no pain, it is not yet in place, and you must put it into such a position that they feel no pain; and be careful that it is set straight, lest crookedness come about once it is restored; and the qualities of the broken limb are according to what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken limbs vary in size, length, and shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For smaller limbs, such as arms and fingers, you must wrap them in soft, fine linen cloths; for larger ones, like thighs and legs, use wide, strong bindings, for the broad binding embraces all of the large limb and constricts it evenly from all sides so that there is no pressure. Then bind with light bandages, three or four turns according to the limb, tighten your hand slightly on the entire binding; then go above the break and tighten less so that the break can move away a little; ease off the binding gradually until you reach most of the healthy part, then take another binding and wrap it again over the broken area. Then return to the area below the break and bind moderately, neither too tight nor too loose as we have said above; put linen cloths or bandages between the bindings so that they are all even, then bind everything with a splint above this, and finally apply your well-made splints if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	Et s'il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l'enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d'une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; 
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is injured by the bones of the stars after the restriction in their veins, place beneath them pads of linen or woolen dressings so they do not wound themselves.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is accompanied by broken ribs, and the heart is ruptured, I will speak of its treatment hereafter.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not fitting to reset all broken bones on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the limb is large, you should not apply splints until after five or seven days, or more depending on your assessment of the developing abscess; and see here the method of ancient poultices to restore broken bones, dislocations, and twists: it is that you take flour from the mill's walls, and mix it with an abundance of egg, and place this mixture, neither too runny nor too thick, upon it, and use it thus; this is the common way of applying a restorative poultice for broken limbs in various positions, especially for women and small children, as it is neither too hot nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana V З.; alechil VIIII З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another type of restorative plaster for fractures, dislocations and sprains: take З abaris, ladanum, nettle, asafetida and arabic gum and mugwort, each X З; myrrh and aloe, each V З; alchimen, VIII З; make a powder from these, mixing it with egg white; if the constitution of the man is hot, use this plaster, since it has a good composition, and restores broken bones rapidly, being beneficial to many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another type of plaster beneficial for sprains: take mugwort and viscarium mallow, each X З; myrrh and aloe, each VIII З; acacia VI З; Armenian bole X З., grind well and mix with water or egg white, then apply it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another method of a plaster for joints and bones dislocated from their places, to ease the pain arising from the abrasion of bone ends in fracture; take new linen, soak it with lye and oil, and apply it to the site.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	This plaster does not restore [the bone], but it is good to ease a hot abscess, and properly removes pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another method of a plaster to restore broken bones: take dry fig leaves and earthweed leaves, grind them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another method of a plaster for the restoration of bone fractures and to reduce the remainder of an abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take the root of marshmallow, chamomile, violets' flowers, vetch flour, each in equal parts; grind and mix them with wine, and if the limb is hot, use moist coriander water or plain water to make a mixture, then apply it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another plaster method stronger than the first one for when a persistent abscess affects limb restoration.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take the roots of marshmallow and flax seeds, pomegranate peel, honey plant, as well as valerian root, violet's flowers and chamomile flowers, all in equal parts; grind them and mix with salted water or fresh water, or wine, depending on the limb temperature and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates said in his book that one should not put a broken limb together to restore its strength with anything other than wax and oil; he also says it must be neither too soft nor hard but between the two.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems to Galen that one must place on the broken limb, to restore, dry things a little warm, such as myrrh and aloe and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way of making a plaster that is good for injury and pain: take mugwort and chopped men's hair, or bird feathers, and viscous mallow, and equal amounts of each, grind them up, make a plaster from this mixture, then bind it in place.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then you should untie it a little after, and pay attention if the patient does not feel any pain, or that the bone has not moved out of place: do not untie by hand for two days. And if pain returns to the spot, or itching, restlessness or swelling occur, then hurry up and undo it, remove the plaster now; take a light cloth, and sea sponge moistened, dip in water, clean the area until the itching stops, and the pain is soothed; then let the limb rest for an hour, then apply dry woolen fabric, moistened with water or rose oil, bind it lightly overnight, to make sure abscess does not heat up again. Then stop inflammation of the limb, and when pain has gone away, start the gentle binding process again, with a little plaster, do not tie too tightly as before; act delicately until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess has drained and the redness, pain, and swelling have all gone, and you need to use poultices and bandages, then start it over again just as you did originally.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	If nothing of what we have said happens to the limb, you should not release it until after three or four or five or seven days; and sometimes leave it for twenty days, as is seen, until the fracture heals, and the flesh approaches the bone; then restrain it more than before, and thicken its flesh, just as I said earlier; if you see that the place becomes drier than necessary, know that nourishment cannot reach it; therefore, bathe it with warm water every time you release it, and do this every three days, and loosen the bandage slightly; by this process, then, nourishment reaches the limb, and amends the damage done by those foolish doctors who restore a limb in a crooked way: this is evil, and such procedures are fearful, and I see nothing else but to leave it alone and treat it properly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Of the diverse manners of fracture
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	There are many types of fractures and various forms, and their causes are distinct; for there are fractures caused by the impact of a sword, where the blow removes all bone down to the marrow beneath it, as if struck with an axe or pole; therefore this type is named 'ax fracture'.
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	Or the sword strikes the bone without piercing it, and this type is called 'absolute fracture'; both types of fractures can be large or small wounds.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is embedded impact, or cracks due to stone fragments, or falling on stones, or similar occurrences.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a penetrating fracture, which reaches the membrane beneath the bone or above it on the bone, and this wound is either large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if there is a wound that pierces the bone as subtle as a hair, and the fracture is small, it is called this "capillary" break; and if the wound is made by striking with a stone, or by falling, or by similar things, and causes a piece of bone to be driven inwards, and the hairline crack is like what blacksmiths do when they hammer on cauldrons; so too does the stone go inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this happens more often to those who have moist bones underneath their skull, such as children's skulls; and it occurs in all these types of breaks where small fragments are detached like stars; I will speak about them at the right time.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	We know all kinds of fractures through their deformity, and we inquire about them by touch, and from the corrupt flesh that is on top.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The resemblance of hair is understood by the fact that when you uncover the bone and rub it repeatedly, the black fracture appears.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In treating the fracture, take heed of the patient's symptoms, and if you see no ill symptom, such as vomiting bile, loss of consciousness, fainting, feverishness, chills, redness around the eyes, and other similar conditions in many cases, then it cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you see no alarming symptom and expect recovery, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the wound comes to you first, and it is in winter, you must remove the bone before the fourteenth day so that you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in the summer, hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, lest the membrane beneath the bone become corrupted, and the accidents we have mentioned occur.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the bone fracture extends to the membrane covering the brain, you must split the fractured part like this: take the wounded person's head and uncover over the bone in every way possible, and on the face of the wound more gently than you can, and if there is an outflow of blood upon uncovering the bone or hot abscess, treat it with what is appropriate, and fill the place with moistened dressings in rose oil; let the wound rest until the hot abscess is soothed, and be assured that the bleeding has stopped; then begin to remove [something] around the bone, and this is done according to two methods of work: one method is that you cut a narrow incision in front, and its shape is
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then he makes another incision greater than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	The second method is to have various incisions, some narrow and others wide, all pointed, made of hard iron; work on them lightly so as not to hurt the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is strong and hard, you must drill it all around rather than making incisions with trepans which are not perfect in that they do not penetrate beyond the skull bone, and there should be a margin or circle above the point to prevent the passage of the point beyond the bone; and you need many such tools so that each one fits into its place on the surface of the bone, thus providing trepans for the whole head; these are the three types of trepan.
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The qualities required to pierce around the broken bone are that you place the trephine on the bone and rotate it with your hands until you know the bone is pierced; then move the trephine elsewhere a little bit after, and do this all around, then cut the space of the bone which is between the holes using the incisor forceps, do this as finely as you can, and lightly, just like we said so that you extract the bone from your hand or some instrument such as pincers or tongs; be careful not to touch the brain nor the meninges.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have pierced and extracted the bone, it is necessary that you remove any remaining bits of bone with every other instrument resembling an incisor forcep, but they must be more pointed and finer than the one before; if there remains anything from small bones or scales, then take them off lightly using some instruments such as a scalpel or scissors; finally treat the wound with ointments and tents like we said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other method of work is that which Galen describes, which is safer; and he praises it strongly, and these are his words.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	You must first expose a part of the bone where the fracture appears, so that when you have uncovered this area, you will place underneath the head of this lens-shaped instrument; and here is its shape:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	Do not cut from one side only, and its cutting edge has two sides so that the sharp edges face towards the bone; then strike gently with a small mallet above it, so that you tap lightly around the bone, and be very careful of the membrane underneath; if it is attached to the bone, remove it slightly, because it can be removed without harm or fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	Et if the bone fracture does not pierce through to the marrow, and the bone is merely cut above, with small pieces present, you must smooth out this roughness, and remove the scales with a fine rasp which you should have in varying quantities, to apply appropriately in each place according to the work and shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	Use large rasps first, then finer ones, and do not cease until it is well done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other delicate cuts and fractures you must adapt your technique according to its direction, and this is something that cannot be fully explained by one who has dedicated their studies to this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And if the wound is uncovered, you must take a piece of linen cloth, according to the size of the wound, and moisten it in rose oil, placing it upon the wound; then take another piece of cloth, doubled over once or twice, and dampen it with wine and rose oil, placing it upon the first cloth; do this gently so as not to aggravate the wound, then apply another bandage, but do not tighten it excessively - just enough to hold the wound in place. Leave it like this for a day or two until the hot abscess is eased, then untie it and apply other medicinal treatments such as lily roots, barley flour, incense powder, and similar substances; make these into a powder and put it on the wound, then administer soothing medicines without any biting sensation. Ensure that the wound remains clean at all times, do not let it become dirty or allow flesh to grow over it, for when flesh grows over the marrow of the skull, it corrodes and decays, causing great harm to the patient; and when one applies biting substances to a wound, they will cauterize it.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take heed therefore, if any bad accident befalls the patient, as we have said, it is undoubtedly doubtful.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if blackness does not come about due to the medicine that has been applied, which may have such an effect, then you must take a portion of honey and three parts of rose oil, glue one dressing with it, and place it on the wound; cure it in the manner of treatments as is fitting, until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that sometimes both parts of the kneecap are broken, or one by itself, for there are two bones; and the lower one is cartilaginous and does not break, but only bends or twists, and then it heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, you must insert your little finger into the gap of the kneecap and place that fracture equally within it against your index finger, pushing from without until the kneecap returns to its natural shape; do this gently, and watch for pain caused by your work in the patient.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the fracture is above the nose and cannot be properly set with fingers alone, you must put a stick, slightly thicker than a finger, equal to the head of the shoulder bone.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the fracture is in two places, do likewise and try to restore it on the first day if you can; otherwise, after the seventh or tenth day, when the hot abscess has cooled down somewhat, place at the head of the nose a bit of linen cloth, if the fracture is in one piece.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Where you place the other one elsewhere if there is a fracture there; and let the bits of cloth be so large that they fill up the holes of the nose.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And some restorers say that one must wet the bits of cloth with butter, changing them every day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	It seems not good to me, but they must be moistened in a concoction of egg white and flour powder; then leave the tent until the bone is firm and the cartilage hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	Sometimes goose feathers are inserted instead of tents, and if so wrap soft cloth around them, and the patient holds it over the break, breathing on it; do as you wish.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if abscesses form in the nose while you are working, put some wax ointment or cotton moistened with rose oil, or a piece of diachylon there.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if abscesses do not form there, apply a plaster externally, made of flax seed flour and incense powder, mixed with egg white; then put light tow over it, and do not tie the nose; but if the bone is broken in small pieces, take them out with suitable instruments to that effect, then sew up the wound, and treat it like other wounds by applying plasters and ointments appropriate for this; and if there is no internal wound in the nose, treat it with tents (splints), placing thin reeds over it until healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	From a fracture of the jaw
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is fractured sideways, and there are no external wounds, and the fracture is only outwards, without splitting it in two, unless the edges overlap slightly inside, one may easily detect this.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	If the fracture is on the right side, you should place your index finger inside the patient's mouth; if it is on the left side of the jaw, use the index finger of your right hand and gently push inwards on the fracture, adjust with the other hand externally, and align them.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the jaw fracture is separated in two, you must administer traction on both sides until they are aligned.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if there are movements of the teeth or fractures occur, bind them with a thread made from gold, silver, or silk; then place crushed cerate on the broken jaw and cover it with a double piece of cloth; over this lay a large well-made starched dressing or an equal sized piece of leather which is long and wide according to the jawbone, secure it as firmly as you can, instruct the patient to rest, and eat light meats.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	And if you see that the arrangement changes, then release it on the third day and reset what has changed; apply an ointment of fine powder made from bran or sesame flour mixed with egg white over this after removing the cerate; cover the ointment with a light woolen cloth, and should the plaster dry out but there is no change in the patient's condition then allow them to remain in place until they heal; many times healing occurs within three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if a hot abscess arises, so treat it as we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture with an accompanying wound, remove any pieces of bone that have been displaced; do so carefully using appropriate instruments.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, then widen it with flame according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Once you have removed all the displaced pieces and there are no remnants left, clean the wound, if it is wide, then apply suitable dressings to promote flesh growth until it heals.
de la forcele	Forceps.
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	Forceps break many times near the shoulder, and the fracture occurs in three ways: either it is broken and split into two, with pieces, and this is the easiest to reset; or there is a fracture with an accompanying wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the treatment is for when there is a fracture without an open wound, you must have two assistants, one to hold the shoulder in place where it feels the fracture's pressure; and the other extends the neck towards that part of the body; then align the fracture evenly between your two hands so that its shape is as it should be, with neither appearance nor outcome.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend further, place beneath the patient's shoulder a round sphere of cloth or wool, as thick as your necessity requires; stretch and lift the fractured bone, and press the sphere with your hand so that you align the fracture evenly, as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the bone out because it is too deep, due to that reason, the patient must often lie on their back, and place a medium-sized pillow beneath their shoulder, and have your assistants push the shoulder downwards so that the bone of the fracture is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then direct the fracture to your two hands, and if you find it splintered, you must split it open further; and draw out the pieces gently, and if the bone cannot be joined by any means, cut into it with one of the incising instruments that you have; but do so using this instrument underneath, to prevent pressure on the soft parts:
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and resembles a spoon, and is not sharp-edged, and be as broad as it needs to be, according to the size of the bone and the strength of the work; and have two ends, as you see, one broad, and the other narrow, just like the fissure in the wound that you made when you drew out the bones; and when you are sure of a hot abscess, cut open the wound, and if the fissure is small, or where you suspect a hot abscess, pack the wound with lint and dressings, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if a warm abscess appears, dampen a cloth with rose oil and vinegar and wine, and apply it.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	You bind the bone when it is injured but not cut with an ointment of mill powder and egg white, then place light dressings on top, and put a rod under the armpit if needed; take a very wide bandage one palm in width, then apply double cloth over the dressings, along with the ointment; now find thin sticks three fingers in breadth and length, and wrap them around the bandages so that its head is still hanging down; place the stick on top of the break, roll up the bandage around the neck, and underneath both armpits - one healthy, one injured. Tighten it from each side until you can see the ligament holding the fracture properly, and if the rod remains immobile over the broken bone, then re-dress every day as required; when the bindings loosen, tighten them again; make the patient lie on their back during sleep with a small pillow under their armpit to raise up the shoulder - this will ease the breakage by aligning the force of the shoulder. Bind the arm to the neck and keep it in place for twenty days unless adverse conditions appear, then begin anew if you see fit. Allow him to remain like that until he's fully recovered; it'll take a month at most but less time for some men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	For a broken shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	Before the shoulder breaks or moves from its place, whether by force or touch; adjust it according to the shape of the fracture, and reset it following its natural form in every way possible; then apply fine flour mixed with egg whites, light compresses, and a double layer of cloth; then place on top a broad and thin strip of material slightly larger than the shoulder, and if there are any gaps beneath the bandage fill them with linen wadding so that the bandage lies evenly; then tightly bind it all with a large bandage, ensuring the bandage does not move from its position, and check the binding each day; every time it loosens, retighten it, and reapply the bandages if they are displaced from their original position, and have the patient lie on his side; after twenty or twenty-five days the shoulder will be healed. Once this period is complete, remove the bindings, being confident that no bone has moved lightly.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a fragment of the bone protrudes before and pierces beneath the heart, they should do as follows: remove it and treat any abscess with cauterization, as we have mentioned for fractures previously.
de la brisure dou pis	Of the fracture of the humerus...
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The humerus is sometimes fractured in the middle, but this rarely happens. It often breaks at its upper end.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, it bends downwards and causes great pain for the patient due to a lack of alignment, resulting in shaking and trembling movements. Sometimes they vomit blood and one can see the ends of the bone through the skin, which indicates a severe fracture. 
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	The method of treatment is as follows: keep the patient lying on their back and place a cushion between their shoulder blades before pressing them together with your hands. Then bring the two sides of the ribs closer to each other using your fingers, aligning the bone fragments in such a way that they form the correct shape of the humerus. Next apply plaster and cover it with fine powder made from salt or some other light material, wrapping this in cloth and tying it firmly around the fractured bone so that it cannot move; fasten the bandage tightly behind their back using a circular knot, tightening it little by little until you are certain there is no more movement. Loosen the binding every hour if necessary to prevent damage from pressure sores or itching caused by corrosion which can lead to infection; hasten this process where required due to inflammation and swelling which might occur around the injury site either because of pain  or abscess formation. Finally, once healed reapply fresh plaster over wounds ensuring it remains tight enough not cause any further damage until full recovery is achieved.
de la brisure des costes	Of broken ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that the rib-breaker only comes from the back and to the head within, and they are bent because of their fragility; one feels it well through interrogation by two people.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the treatment is that you set the break evenly, as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	Then apply the plaster, and restrain with a splint if you need to.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	If the rib break is angled inward, the patient feels great pain and piercing, like a tearing, as the bone pierces the tissue; they have difficulty breathing, cough up large clots of blood, and it is quickly fatal, with ancient ones having applied major measures.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And there are some who say it is necessary to administer foods that bloat the belly in order to push the rupture outward.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this unless heat has already come to the abscess.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has, then drain it.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And some of you say to put cups over the place to strongly suck out the contents, and this seems reasonable; however, there is doubt that the cup will draw the excesses back to the site due to its weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And some of you say to cover the site with damp wool in warm oil, and put tents between the ribs to make even the length around, then be cured by the treatment for pleurisy, food, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that they cannot bear due to the bone pricking the skin, and there is doubt in the patient's condition, one must cut over the location of the broken rib, and place an instrument beneath it to protect the soft tissues; then one should cut into the bone, draw out gently, and afterward sew together the two lips of the wound if it is large, treating it with emollient plasters until it heals.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if heated abscesses appear, apply dampened linen cloths soaked in rose oil onto the affected area; treat it while considering what is necessary for an abscess, and let it lie frequently on its side where needed until healed.
de la brisure dou col	Regarding the broken neck...
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Sometimes there is breakage of bones in the neck, and it happens that they bend; this also occurs in the backbone.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to someone, and you wish to know if they will heal or not, take note: if you see their hands become soft, swollen, and lifeless, unable to move or stretch, and when pricked with a needle, there is no sensation.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that it is deadly in many positions, and if they feel better when you move them and apply pressure, know that the bone's socket is saved, and the patient can be cured with proper treatment.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if a similar thing happens to the backbone, and you wish to know if they will recover or not, take note: if their feet become soft, and there is an accident involving what was in their hands, along with wind and involuntary excretion on their back; and when turned onto their stomach, there is also involuntary excretion.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when he is reminded of it on his back and wants to mount, he cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	Know that it is mortal; do not labour in vain in its treatment.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if these accidents do not befall him, then the matter is more trivial.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the cure is such that you remove heat if there is a hot abscess, then apply raw pork fat or egg yolk until it is soothed; afterwards, place on one of the comforting and drying emplasters, and bind it with a bandage, and instruct the patient to rest; let them not sleep upon this part where they feel pain, until it is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bone is severed, you must cut above the heart; remove the bone, then bring together the two lips of the wound, if it is large, with a suture, then treat it with a healing ointment that encourages flesh growth until it is healed; and if the head of the bone is shattered, which is called the "bone's head", thrust your fist from your left hand into it, and make it equal to the other hand of your strength, then apply the plaster and the star upon it, if you have need of them; then hold it tight, and if there are severed bones present, fix them together, remove any, and treat the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	Of the broken hip bone.
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	If there is a break in the hip bone, and if it occurs, then only slight reduction at the head; they fracture lengthwise, and incline downward, and comes to the patient pain at the site, and stabbing, and swells what breaks.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is such that you extend your hand above it so that you are on top of the break; and know what type of fracture there is and its shape; and if the break is only at the head, then make this fracture even, as much as possible to natural form.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is lengthwise or inclines inward, then make the patient lie on their belly so that you can see this break clearly to restore it.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have set it evenly, apply the plaster on top, then place a piece of wood or heartwood above it, and compress the fracture so that it does not move; secure its position under the armpit until the ligament is aligned.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	Instruct the patient to sleep on their healthy side or on their back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if a warm abscess develops there, do not touch it until the warm abscess is healed, and apply what we have mentioned before; then return to the restoration process, compressing as necessary if no complications arise; this is the method.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	On the fracture of the shoulder.
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The adjutoires is what lies between the cut and the head of the shoulder, and if it is broken, you must restore it according to one of two methods. One method uses a piece of wood of medium thickness, as follows:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And bind the two ends of the two pieces together, and bend them upwards. Lay the patient on a seat, then place their broken arm onto the wood until it reaches the elbow, and put half a piece of curved wood under it; then let assistants pull downwards while keeping the break in alignment with the hands joined together until it heals properly.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	The other method is to lift the patient onto their back and bind their hand to their neck; command two assistants to hold what is above the break with their hands joined together, while another holds below at all points of the binding, stretching each part as required.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is stronger, tighten the cord below the fracture, and above it, and extend each of the assistants to their respective positions.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the fracture is close to the shoulder joint, you should place a cord halfway below the socket, and the other towards the arm, under the fracture; likewise, if the fracture is towards the arm, it should be fixed gently without force so that the fracture aligns with the joint and the arm; then align the break as required, and secure it tightly, provided no abscesses appear.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if an abscess appears, do not tighten it for seven days, and apply moist wool soaked in rose oil until the abscess subsides; then secure it tightly, but be aware that to do so you must place a plaster over the fracture, then bring the arm towards the support, and place your hand on their shoulder or chest; wrap with fabric, securing both onto the support and the arm, such that the arm remains in this position for weeks unless something prevents it, or if the bone has moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone will move, use splints, and place on the fracture a splint wider and stronger than the others, with one finger-width of space between each splint; let each splint be so large as to extend three fingers' width beyond the break on either side. Then bind tightly over the splints, just as I said at the beginning of this chapter regarding fractures, binding more firmly but less severely in its application.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	And if you see the positioning of the splints and the binding, as we have said, when you restore the broken limb, and you suspect a hot abscess, let it remain bound until the seventh day, as we have mentioned; then inspect every three days to ensure that itching or swelling does not occur in the area, nor any suppuration reach the limb because of too tight a binding.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If the treatment succeeds, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And if none of these accidents occur, you should not release the patient until after three days or more, and let the patient sleep on their back with their hands on their stomach; place beneath the affected limb a pillow filled evenly with wool; check every hour during the day or night that the position of the broken limb does not change, nor do the ligaments relax; if it succeeds through the virtue of medicine, then give them food as we have mentioned before, in such a way that the first foods are delicate; and when they start to improve, let their diet become more substantial.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	It is customary that the limb and its support should be changed after forty days altogether; then you must release them from it, and provide a bath along with medicinal ointments to correct their position.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the dislocation is bad and tight, it may take one day or two months to loosen.
de la brisure du bras	Of arm fractures:
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the 'humerus' (the upper arm bone), one being small and joining the wrist, while the other is larger and located underneath the little finger; perhaps only the large humerus breaks, or maybe just the smaller one, or possibly both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the smaller bone is fractured, the restoration is light and healing swift; but when only the larger one breaks, the mending is difficult, and worse than if both were broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is only the small bone that is broken, you should slightly extend it and set it evenly.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	And if it is the large bone that is broken, you should bind it more tightly; extend it on a cushion, and hold the wrist of the hand higher than the others, and the little finger lower than the other fingers, and have the patient cross their arms over themselves, with the cushion in front of them at a higher level so they do not strain themselves; then let one minister hold their arm by the part below the hand or wrist, while another holds it from above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	Then place them in an even position according to their best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if it has broken into pieces, place each one back in its position; and if there is a piece missing that holds the heart, and you cannot restore it to its place, then make an incision above and remove it as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with a fracture causing injury, I have spoken of it in the singular chapter; then take its treatment.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if in the beginning of restoration warm abscesses appear, make a soft cerote plaster from rose oil and white wax, that is neither too hard nor too soft; tie it gently over, so that the warm abscesses are eased.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	Then remove the cerote and apply a mill powder plaster with much egg white, then place the splints, making sure that the splint of the fracture is closest to and slightly wider than the others; know that there must be six splints or arms in various arrangements: whether the fracture is in one bone or two; bind tighter above the fracture and looser as you move away, as I said at the beginning of this chapter; let the cloths over the fracture be soft and moist and not hard nor rough; and ensure that the thread used for binding, which we have already discussed, is made from linen, neither too thick nor too thin.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And support the limb and the joint after a few days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if any bad accident befalls the limb, such as an itch that arises in the limb, you must wash the limb with warm water until the itching is soothed; and let the limb rest without restriction.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	Then resume the binding, and if the ligaments are softened and the bones dislocated, or something similar occurs, address it accordingly.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if you suspect that nourishment cannot reach the limb due to its restriction, it is necessary to soften it a little, and leave it thus for a few days until circulation returns, then bind it again.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things we have said come to pass for the patient, do not release him until twenty days have passed.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	For this ailment, wrap cloth around his neck, then paint his hands with it, ensuring the two sides are equal, and guard against movement and turning; he should sleep on his back. Know that this fracture will be healed in thirty or thirty-five days, perhaps even twenty according to different compositions and qualities of medicine.
de la brisure de la main	On the breaking of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that the back of the hand and the knuckles rarely experience breaks but rather frequent dislocations.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	And when the palm of the hand is broken or dislocated, it's necessary for the patient to be laid crosswise, sitting upright directly before him evenly. Next place his hand on a flat surface and extend the broken bones with your hands until they are aligned and properly joined; then apply plaster and bandages unless abscesses develop, followed by a splint according to the size of the area; lastly wrap it all in one piece of linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the fracture is around the area of the pelvis or abdomen, make a sphere with some bandages, and instruct the patient to bind it tightly to their broken hip; then take a long piece of fabric, and let the heart's sinew be as big as the palm of one's hand, and tie them together accordingly.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is on the outside, it must be that you place a splint above and another below the broken bone so that the hand remains open and straight, then bind the whole thing around the hand, and tighten the binding between the fingers.
