Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the fracture occurs in one of our fingers, say the thumb, make it even and bind it with a splint to the hand; and if you see that an upright small splint is needed to lift the broken bone without moving it, then do so; and if the break is in another finger such as the index or any other, set them straight and tie it together with the healthy adjacent finger; or bind all five fingers together, holding them in a natural position of extension, whichever you prefer. Or place an upright splint over the thumb as if it were the whole hand; and take care to avoid the hot abscess which is there, and treat those who suffer from this accordingly, as I have said before.
de la cuixe brisie	of the broken thigh
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	The bone of the thigh is often broken, and it can be easily seen when the leg twists forward and backward; and its restoration lies in binding a ligature above the fracture and another below it.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient lies on his face, then each minister extends his ligature to their respective side equally; this is when the fracture is within the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the fracture is close to the hip joint, let one of the ligatures be towards the armpit and the other ligature below the break.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	Also, if the fracture is close to the knee, let the ligatures be around the knee and have their extension downwards; then place the broken ends of bone together with your two hands until they are aligned according to their natural shape, and apply a plaster cast and bind it, unless there is an abscess present.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is a hot abscess there, let it subside before returning to your work and treatment; the binding is done in this manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	You must wrap the fracture with I hard bandage doubled in II or III, leaving excess material, then turn the leg so that the heel comes to the root of the thigh, and thread I long wire between the thigh and the leg, below the knee, bringing the end of the wire above; then return the bandage over the leg and thigh, then place rods on top of the fracture, and place a rod over the bone of the leg; then fill the empty space between the leg and the thigh with soft cloth to ensure an even constriction, then begin binding strongly III or IV turns around the fracture; and as you go up past the fracture, tighten less; then take II ends of the wire that you threaded between the leg and the thigh, and bind III rods above it, then return below to the end of the wire, until you reach near the foot; and secure so that there is no movement from its place, then leave in this way for some time, so that neither abscess nor swelling or other similar things occur.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if it happens, then dislodge it and treat the cause, as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of bone caught in the joint, you must remove them if possible; and if one cannot, then one must cut open the area and pull out the offending piece; then cure it as we have said, until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And at times the thigh is broken and fixed with pins, as in a shoulder or arm injury; however, despite this restoration being complete, the patient still suffers.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the thigh is restored in an average of 50 days, perhaps a little less or more depending on the diversity of temperaments.
de la ruelle dou genoil	From the groove of the knee.
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	Know that at the knee area there are few breaks, but it bends many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, it is only a crack, or a hole, and this happens to every wound, and unhealed wounds, and one feels it well.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	The restoration is done by putting something equal to what is round at the two sides, until it is assembled as much as possible; then apply the plaster, and place a round stick if needed, and hold it as required, then follow all the arrangements we mentioned for other breaks, such as hot abscesses or similar; assign each accident with what suits it, until it heals.
de la brisure de la jambe	On the break of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	Know that in the leg there are two bones, one is rightly named 'tibia', and the other is called 'fibula'; they both suffer breaks like those of the arm, so their restoration is likewise equal to that of an arm, and the work involved is all the same. If both bones are broken together, then the leg becomes twisted in all directions.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the fine bone is broken, it twists forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the thick bone is broken, there is great pain felt, and it is clearly seen; it twists downwards.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	So provide traction and make it even, bind the splints evenly; however, if the fracture is severe with many fragments, let your traction be less strong and more gentle; ease off according to your skill.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, and lie em mileu ausi, and a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, and ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, and s’est de fust, and i met on la jambe por warder de movement, and proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; and remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.
de la brisure des os dou piet	Of broken bones of the foot.
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle, there is no fracture, but in the bones of the foot, there may be a break or crack, and it can be crushed in various ways.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	If there is a break in the bones of the foot and you see these bones protruding from each other, have the patient place their foot on the ground, as if they were about to walk, then place your foot over theirs, where the bones are raised, and press until they return to their places; then apply a plaster cast and bandages on top, and place beneath the belly of the foot a small board with two handles, then secure it to the foot appropriately, having wrapped linens around, and other things as required.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, untie the binding, for you will find the bones equalized, whether broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	If there are any of the toes broken, restore them as we have said for the fingers of the hand; then place in the broken toe a peg according to the length of the toe, and let it be a little wider; then put beneath the foot that board I mentioned, and strain it suitably; and if there are two or three, or more, broken, place on each toe a peg according to its size, wrapped in a piece of linen cloth, and tighten the board underneath the foot; and let it extend over the top of the board from outside the belly of the foot so that it holds well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And you must not forget the other things I mentioned for treating other fractures, as we have said before; and treat each accident appropriately.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	Of the fracture of the bone in the wrist.
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Have her sit with an enlarged opening, then lean her towards the back part and support her from behind; next fill the opening of the woman's nature with cotton until it is as full as it can be; then make the woman stand up and lift her slightly by the back several times so that the cotton leaps out at the entrance to the nature, bringing the bone together with the stool; whenever she needs to urinate take out the cotton, but put it back when she has finished, for seven days or thereabouts: thus will the fracture be restored, if you wish do this instead get a goat's bladder and attach a cane to its opening, then fill the entire bladder with air by blowing through the cane until the bladder is inflated inside; so shall the nature of the woman be healed from the fracture; then fill it once more with cotton, let her remain thus for several days until she is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And when the bone of the wrist is broken in a man or a woman, restore it as we have said for the hip bone; and these fractures are not hidden from those who apply their study and practice to them, and read my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For the fracture indicates in many ways the right path to restoration; understand this, then.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the penis, when it is broken, take a goose's gullet and insert it into the penis; then wrap it with fine cloths around, and leave it there for three days, and it will heal quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	When fracture is associated with wound:
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for one who has a fracture with wound, especially if it's large, such as the bone of the thigh or shoulder, to be immediately treated so that the wounds we have described may testify (to its efficacy).
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals, treat it with vitriol to stop bleeding, unless you have other means, then restart restoring the fracture that very hour or day, provided no hot abscesses arise.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if hot abscesses do arise, leave the restoration until the ninth day, until the abscess is pacified, and do not touch it on the third or fourth day, for you will bring about an evil event.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is visible on an exposed heart, you must set it gently with your hands at a small extent.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extent of the break is not apparent to set equal with your hands, reset it with this iron instrument which is seven or eight fingers long, and its width depends on the quantity of the wound; and for this, the surgeon needs three or four of them, according to his need in each treatment of a fracture; and let them be round and somewhat thick, so they do not bend under pressure on the limb during your work, and let it taper forward, and be large from mid-length onwards like so:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And it is called "palainche", for this reason the curved head should be placed on top of the prominent bone; push it once until it returns and make sure they are aligned opposite each other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is subtle, and the instrument cannot grasp the bone well, then you must cut off the head of the bone until the instrument has a hold of it.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot reset the bone as we have said, then cut it off with an appropriate instrument, whether it be a scalpel or knife, to your ability; remove what remains in the bone of roughness and small bark-like pieces.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is reset, and the patient feels great pain afterward, know that it is not in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	Si make sure it is in its place, then moisten a cloth with black styptic wine, and properly if it is on the skin; do not put any ointment or oily substance onto the wound, as this can cause infection and corruption; administer splints once you have restored the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, cover the area all around according to the size of the wound, and be careful that the wound is not restrained with the fracture; many foolish doctors have done this, causing harm or even death to their patients, and these restraints should be looser than those used for other fractures.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is bad or large, and you fear that complications may arise as we have mentioned before, and find pain in that area, it is not advisable to apply splints; instead wrap around it with hard cloths in place of splints, and tie them securely.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one or two days that the wound is swelling again, remove what you have put on it previously and apply a healing ointment, such as tetrapharmacon ointment and similar ones.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And you should loosen the limb twice daily, in the morning and at dusk, until it is fused and healed.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And the limb should be bandaged in such a way that the swelling flows downwards gently.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if after many days it does not heal but swells again, know that there are small bone fragments present, which is why you must examine the wound with a probe and remove all these troublesome pieces causing this pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula forms at that spot or some other kind of infection develops, you must treat it according to what he said in his previous chapter.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	When the bone is broken and exposed on a limb, such as in the thigh or shoulder bones, and other similar cases of large limbs, do not extract it, for many times death results from this, but leave it until it rots; perhaps it will fall off by itself after twenty or thirty days, then treat the wound if you can; and if you cannot, just let it be.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	The scabs that form over the suture.
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	We often see complications after the healing of fractures, especially when they are close to joints, and it is an unpleasant sight to behold the disfigurement of the limb; perhaps the limb will be unable to perform its natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take care then if the wound is fresh: administer styptic medicines such as aloe, incense, myrrh, storax, galbanum, and similar others; prepare any of these or all together with astringent wine or egg white or honey; place it on a lint soaked in this substance and bind it well; do not untie it for two days at least; then loosen the bandage and start another one until swelling disappears; you can also press gently over an adequately cut piece of wood, since the property of wood is to remove all swellings from limbs; if the swelling has already hardened like a stone and needs to be removed, incise it, clean its excess; or shave it with a razor as long as the skin appears healthy.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	Of the limb which is weak after recovery
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the broken bone is mended, and the limb remains weak and fragile, it happens for many reasons: one is that it was bound too tightly, and not bound as it should have been; or because there were too many bindings, preventing nourishment from reaching the limb; or due to excessive bleeding; or because of large movements, at the wrong time; or because there is little blood in their body, thus they are weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is such that you make the patient eat, and soften their body, so that blood multiplies within them; and administer a bath, giving joy and leisure; then place poultice on the limb, so that the poultice attracts great nourishment, and often moisten it with warm water, until the nourishment flows to the limb; and return it to its natural form.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	Of a twisted limb after the sanctity.
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is twisted after restoration and the broken bone remains apparent, and its form is unsightly, nevertheless it does not lose its natural function; do not believe those foolish people who say that one must break the member anew, and many foolish doctors have done this in our land; these practices are to be condemned, as they cause much harm and perhaps even death; however, if the knots or swellings are fresh, then they should be bathed in warm water, or softening herbs can be cooked such as leaves of mallow, roots, marshmallow root, and similar things; and apply a softening plaster like well-made diakylon, and take mucilage from mallow, mix it with goose fat or sesame oil, and make a poultice to spread over the injury; you may also use figs cooked in honey, crushed with fennel seed, and other medicines that reduce inflammation.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And sometimes the swelling is removed by rubbing continually and for a long time with moist hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	Let there be gentle movements to the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	If the twisting and hardening are like stone and must be removed with iron, it should be cut to the bone using fine, lightweight scissors; and pack with stitches and give care to its healing.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation occurs in someone, you must reset it immediately without delay.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if one delays, the joint swells, and perhaps it is reset with difficulty in place; therefore, it must not be moved when swollen: often causes spasm and other pains; nevertheless, when this occurs, let the patient bleed, then leave them until the abscesses subside; then bathe the limb in hot water and oil, then gently reset it, and treat each member as its cure comes to place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters on dislocations from head to foot.
des mandibules	Of jaws.
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	Sometimes jaws become dislocated on both sides, and there are two types of dislocations: either they are slightly out of place and softened; or they are fully dislocated, hanging downwards, with saliva running from the mouth which cannot be contained, nor can they close their mouth or speak clearly with their tongue.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When a dislocation is minor, one can recover through many treatments.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if it is complete and fully dislocated, you must reset it immediately without delay; do not hesitate. In such a manner that the assistant holds the patient's head, and pushes one hand into their mouth towards the root of the jaw dislocation, if the dislocation is in two parts; the other hand should be outside to provide equal pressure; instruct the patient to relax their jaws and move them around freely.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	The assistant should apply equal pressure until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if resetting is difficult, especially when both jaws are dislocated together, warm them with hot water and oil until they can be gently reset; do not delay the procedure as we mentioned earlier.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are brought back evenly, and the patient's wound is well closed without softening, apply moistened cloths in a cerote made of rose oil and wax, then bind it lightly with soft bandages; let the patient sleep on their back, and place two pillows under their head so that it does not move to the right or left, and they must not strain themselves nor try to chew, but take light food until the pains are gone, and the jaws must be bound; and then eat gently whatever they want, and do not exert themselves by opening their mouth to eat or drink, until the jaw is well bound and healed.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jaws cannot be brought back to their proper place within an hour, and they do not return to their correct position, fevers and persistent soreness will occur, and possibly violent purging, and perhaps vomiting of clear fluid.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	And when you see this, know that it is destruction; and many times the one who experiences it dies within nine days.
de la forcelle	Of the fork.
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The fork cannot be dislocated from the inside, along its length or at the base; and is sometimes dislocated outwards, which can easily be felt.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And its restoration is such that the patient often lies on their back and extends their arms; then you press the place firmly with your palm, and it will return; next apply a plaster and bandage, holding it in place; the head which is towards the neck cannot be dislocated; if not, and if it dislocates at any time, then reset it to its place as we have said; next apply a plaster and bandage, securing it; instruct the patient to rest until they are healed; similarly is the shoulder head restored when it is displaced from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	Of shoulder dislocation
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	Know that the shoulder dislocates in three ways: first, it dislocates at the bottom part near the armpit; second, it dislocates at the back part towards the chest; and occasionally it dislocates upwards, which is rare; it does not dislocate behind due to the bone structure, nor does it dislocate inwardly toward the nerves. It often dislocates downwards toward the armpit, especially in those with little flesh, as it happens quickly there; for those with more flesh, it dislocates and goes back in with difficulty.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And occasionally it happens to some men that there is a blow or fracture, and the shoulder swells from a hot abscess, and they think it has dislocated because of this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	You must therefore test it until you are certain; and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	It is recognized as dislocation when it falls towards the armpit, and creates a difference between the affected shoulder and the healthy one, and you will notice an obvious disparity between them; and at the head of the shoulder, you'll find a hollow, and beneath the armpit where the shoulder meets the body, like a goose egg; and the patient cannot return their hand to their nose, nor move in any way; and if it is dislocated upwards, it is not hidden, for you will clearly feel it upon touch; and this type of dislocation is not difficult to reset, when it is recent, or if the child is ill.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the manner is that the ministers lift the patient's hand upwards, then place your palms underneath the shoulder blade, and raise the joint forcefully upwards to its proper place; the ministers lift the patient's hand, and extend it upwards before placing it below; this will bring relief.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	If it does not come about as we have said with hands-on approach afterwards, then the patient must be bathed in warm water; and the attendant applies a softening and soothing ointment such as a decoction of althea, fenugreek, and mellilot in water, which is applied gently; thereafter the patient should be remembered upon their back, and place underneath the shoulder blade a cushion made of wool that is equal, neither too soft nor too hard, then let the physician's heel rest on this cushion, and lift the head of the afflicted shoulder virtuously, and pull on the patient's hand; another attendant holds the patient's head so it does not move downwards; this shoulder returns at once, and if you wish to reset it in such a manner: and that there should be present one man who is larger than the patient; and he must stand upright by the side of the afflicted, then push their shoulder underneath the other's shoulder blade, and lift the blade upwards so the patient hangs in mid-air; another attendant pulls on the patients hand downwards towards the stomach.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, you may use something heavy with them, and the dislocation will return now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	You may also reset it in another way: you insert a long pole into the ground, so that the shoulder is as round as a pestle, and not too thick or thin; then place it underneath the patient, but have soft cloth beneath, and the patient should lie along the length of the pole; then extend their arm downwards on the other side quite firmly, and the joint will return to its place in time; if it does not wish to return for all these things that we have said, then do this treatment: take a pole two arms long and four palms wide, with a rounded head so as to be able to enter perfectly underneath the shoulder blade, according to this form:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then lie upon the head of the wounded person a linen cloth so that it does not wound the patient, then put him under the sick man's bedstead; and stretch his arm over the long side of the bed, and bind the shoulder on the bed, and the arm to the head of the hand, then place the arm on the corner of a bench which is broad, and let the hands hang downwards, and let the body be left hanging from another part: now the joint will return.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is thus, in whatever way, you must put under the bedstead a woollen pad of equal size, then apply the plaster prepared with flour of mill, together with incense and egg white, over the whole shoulder and around it; then strain the binding under the bedstead suitably, and turn the bandage back upon the plaster, and embrace the hand to his neck, and let the hands remain thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And he must eat little, until the limb is strengthened, for it will heal faster; then let him eat more after 5 or 7 days, and move it; if it is firm and not softened, it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is dislocated due to moisture that has entered it or for another reason, you must apply cauterization to three openings, as described earlier in the chapter on cautery.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this and it still dislocates after 7 days, and the joint does not hold, and he cannot lift his arm above him, then know that the nerve at the head of the shoulder is cut or stretched or softened; and know that the joint will never be properly fixed in place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation that affects the hip and breasts or the rear is caused by a thrusting motion and stretching of hands, and in another place we administer treatment; and it heals as soon as it is cured.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after the healing process the member becomes cracked and moves slowly, the patient should bathe frequently until this cracking is alleviated, and it returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	On the dislocation of the neck
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the joint of the neck is partially and repeatedly dislocated, and it returns to its normal position; and if it is completely dislocated, especially at the front and back, and the dislocation is not reset, because it can be clearly seen and felt; and it dislocates according to each individual's physique.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the sick person's wound with the healthy one, you can see it clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is separated, and cannot bend the arm or reach their shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And you must reset it before abscesses form, because if they do come up, the resetting will be difficult; and perhaps it cannot be completely reset at all, especially when it is at the back; thus, this type of dislocation is worse than others, causing more severe pain, and sometimes leading to death.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	The restoration process is as follows: when it can be reset, extend their arm with both your hands; spread the arms wide and place the hands of the patient mirror-like according to the cut around, above, and below; push the joint towards its sockets or at the root of their palm until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is at the front, it returns when he bends his hand towards his hand, and press firmly on the root of the damaged palm's wrist.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	If it does not want to return to its place, then administer strong extension; the two assistants should extend the arm, and the second assistant should bend the arm so that there is no movement in the extension; then turn the arm from side to side, after you have wrapped a double-length wide cloth around it; when the physician joins the joint to the hand, apply some oil to soften the joint, then set the joint firmly until it returns; and once it is in place, put on a dry poultice with egg white, strain it tightly, and bend the arm onto the patient's neck, leaving it there for a few days before removing it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firmly in its place, untie the bandage and leave it alone; but if you see that the joint does not hold well, reapply the poultice and bandage, and leave it for a few days until it is securely set; then undo the bandage.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	If he feels stiffness after the joint is reset and it becomes inflamed, bathe and gently massage it until it subsides; or apply to the joint a dressing of fat mutton's wool, leaving it for one day and night before removing it, then put him in a bath; when he perspires, gently rub the joint, then reapply the dressing, followed by another visit to the bath; repeat this twice or three times until it heals; if you wish, apply moist warm cow dung mixed with butter and leave it on - the joint will return to its normal state.
li dislocation de la main	The dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The joint of the hand is dislocated and its return is light, more so than other joints. However, it must be put back in place immediately when it is dislocated, unless the area is swollen or an abscess forms.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	And for the reset, you place the injured hand on a table, and have the assistants stretch out the hand, and align it so that its palm is over the joint, then push until it returns to its proper position. However, ensure it is indeed in the right place; have the patient put the back of their hand on a table for extension and reset.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is on the back of the hand, have the patient put the back of their hand on the table, and place your hand over that joint's area.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If it returns now, that's good But if not, apply a strain of soothing emollient plasters to hot abscesses, and leave them be without reapplication.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	And if he cannot bear it, and you are unable to put it back in place after some days, the joint remains dislocated; and this causes no harm to the patient as long as the hand is weak, and can grasp nothing at all: then know that the nerves or arteries are cut, or there is another hindrance preventing movement, other than by cauterization near the case, and perhaps nothing else will help.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is in place, apply the plaster we mentioned, then strain it and leave for five days, then release and leave as such.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it cannot move well, and there is any injury, then bathe it in warm water, and rub until it is healed.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	Of the dislocation of the fingers of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	Sometimes the finger of the hand is dislocated on both sides, sometimes on the palm or on the back; then stretch the finger, and push the dislocation with your fingers until it returns, then hold the head of the finger, and bend it towards the side where it is dislocated; let it rest for two days, and then make it equal that day; at night bind it as we have said, and in the day untie it, and exercise it, and tie it again at night; do this often until it is tight, and do likewise if it is dislocated on the palm of the hand, and proceed as you did before until it is healed; and do the same when it is dislocated elsewhere.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	Of dislocation of the spine from the back
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the spine from the back or neck is dislocated, or there are multiple dislocations, there is no treatment, as death comes swiftly to the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	And the signs are that the faeces come out involuntarily, and they cannot be contained, and often certain limbs weaken, such as both thighs or both arms or one, and often the spine twists in four parts; this twisting at the rear is called 'gilbositez': the treatment is to turn if the 'gilbositez' came from childhood: there is no cure nor full recovery.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	And that which comes from falling or blows or similar things, the old ways of treatment say there is not much benefit in all of it; but I have shortened [the treatments] according to my intention, and have formed instruments in diverse manners.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I say that in the hump which develops on the breastbone in front, no physician or surgeon understands it; and likewise with those that develop directly at II sides (on both sides), they cannot be cured except for properly when they occur on the back, as I have said; the patient must be laid out face down on a level surface, with something under him so he doesn't get hurt. Then drive one iron rod into his head firmly in the ground and another at his feet, tie ropes around each joint of the patient's body: to the head, hips, knees, and ankles; have two assistants hold these ropes tight (one for the head and one for the feet), between the II iron rods, they must be well secured. The rods should be as we described earlier, the doctor then places his palms on the spine firmly until it returns to its natural position.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And if it does not return to its place with this treatment, take a board of three arms length long, and place it underneath the wall, let the patient be on their side, push the head of the board under the wall, then put the middle of the board on the spine; have the surgeons put their feet on the other end of the board, and press hard until it returns to its place; if you wish, do this with a lever that turns towards the hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	Put two stakes at the head of the patient's shoulder, each one an arm's length apart, and place two others towards their feet, also an arm's length apart; have a space of one palm's width between each stake; in each stake make a hole where the lever will go through, and ensure that these are firmly placed in the ground so they do not move; between each pair of stakes put a turning stake, with smaller ones on either end to turn the lever; tie the straps from amongst the axles to the levers at the head and foot ends respectively, then have each attendant turn their respective lever until all the straps are taut, and the master surgeon adjusts the spine accordingly as we have mentioned.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	And when it is even, apply a desiccative poultice with an abundance of eggs, then wrap with bandages, and use a splint made from a tablet three inches long to support the area of curvature and the healthy part of the spine, then bind it with a ligature as we have said, and let the patient consume subtle nourishment until healed; if anything arises towards the end of healing, you must administer softening and soothing medicines along with the splint we mentioned earlier; sometimes one administers a piece of lead, and at times an appearance emerges in the lower vertebra of the back, which is mistaken for dislocation; it is actually bone that has appeared, so there should be no presumption: death might result.
des dislocations de la hainche	Hip dislocations.
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the recognition of its dislocation is as follows: when you join the sick leg with the healthy one, it will be longer, and the patient's knee will appear more prominent than the healthy one, and the sick person cannot bend their knee; and the area nearby is swollen with a warm abscess due to the thigh bone having come loose.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of him for whom it happens in reverse is that this affliction stands contrary to what came before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the sign of him for whom it happens beforehand is that he stretches his leg according to its progress; however, he cannot bend his knee without pain, and if one wishes him to walk, he cannot at first, and retains his urine, and his ankle swells, and when he urinates, he does so on his heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of him who has it behind are such that he cannot bend his knee or double up, and one leg is more twisted than the other, the groin is softened, and the shoulder head is in place under the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	We reset this type of dislocation by bringing it back into place if the dislocation is old and remains according to its position, for there is no treatment; and one must not be presumptuous.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And for the one with a fresh dislocation, which can be of four types, you must hurry to return the joint and stretch it both inside and out, and move it to the right and left; perhaps it will go back into place, and no other treatment is needed.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And if it does not return in this manner, you must prepare a strong assistant, and they should hold the leg firmly with both hands, or with a rope tied above the knee; another assistant places their hand over his shoulders in such a way that he pushes their hands under their armpits, then binds them tightly with a cord around the thigh; another holds the head of the cord; and all pull upward and downward at once until the patient is raised from the ground and remains suspended.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of extension is common for the four similar cases, and if the dislocation has been corrected, as we have said, it is good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If not, you must apply the cure suited to its similar case. When the dislocation is on the outside, you should lay the patient down on his healthy side, then place the rope around the root of the thigh and the part below the groin, pulling the rope upwards towards the groin and towards the hip joint; another assistant takes hold of his arms, embraces the upper part of the sick thigh, and stretches it outwards forcibly: it will now return to its place; and this kind of dislocation is lighter than the others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	And if you cannot secure it in this manner as we have said, then you must bind the two feet of the patient together with a strong soft bandage over the two heels and above the knees, let the affected leg be extended twice more than the other one; then suspend him from the top of a pole, being two arms' lengths above the ground; instruct a minister to embrace the head of the thigh, and have another minister hanging alongside the patient who firmly embraces the thigh, for the joint is now rapidly dislocating.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	When the dislocations are outward, let the patient lie down as we have said for someone with curvature, and bind the bands tightly over the affected leg and also on the foot; then place two burning brands, one at his head and another at his feet, then insert a brand between his thighs in the form; have moist cloths planted around it so that it does not burn the patient, then stretch each minister towards him, and let the surgeon place himself equally to his hand with respect to the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, it's good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, place [the patient] on a board, i.e. a plank, and press them as we have described for 'gilbosse', and let the patient lie on their sound side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is in front, one must extend the sick leg as much as possible, and according to what I have said; place the healthy side of their body on the ground, then press with the other hand, and stretch [the leg] downwards towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocation is on the outside, one must not stretch the affected leg downwards or lift it off the ground, but rather, it should be positioned as if the hip were dislocated outwards, as we have described for lying on both hips; let them lie on their face, and bind [the limb] as we have said before, and press on the joint with a board; it will be ready when the patient can stretch out their legs evenly, and they are of equal length; then adjust the thighs, apply an ointment, and strain [the hip] with a bandage so that it does not move; let them rest for three or four days, then release the binding and reapply the ointment; if you see that [the limbs] are even, bind [the patient], as before, for three days; then release [the binding], and let them walk gently until their limb is strengthened.
de la dislocation dou genoil	Of the dislocation of the knee
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The knees are dislocated in three ways: namely, from within and without, and behind; and it does not dislocate forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the sign is that you instruct the patient to bend their leg at the thigh, and if it does not reach the thigh, know that it is dislocated; and the restoration of all this is that you make the patient sit upright, and stretch out their leg if they can, and place your back on their face, and put their foot on your feet; then take their kneecap in your palms, and pull between your hands, then bend the two sides of the knee sharply; and another assistant stretches their foot until the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that it lightly reaches their leg to their thigh; and apply the poultice, and make the leg touch the thigh, and bind them together strongly for three or four days, then untie [the bandage]; and the patient must not exert themselves with walking until the limb has been strengthened.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limb is not aligned, apply strong traction, as we have mentioned in the treatment of hip injuries, until it is healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	Of the dislocation of the heel...
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heels may be partially or fully dislocated, internally or externally...
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the sign of this is that the ankle is swollen and more so in the area where it is dislocated; the reduction should be gentle, and when only partially dislocated, one must gently extend it with their hands...
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	...and when it is fully dislocated, you must have the patient sit up straight and hold the ministers aside with one hand on his leg above the ankle; then pull the foot towards you with your right hand, and then to the left twice, extend it upwards, and push the foot gently upwards; do this twice as we've said, pushing and pulling the foot; if it returns, that's good; but if not, repeat the process for it does return; and if it cannot be returned thus, have the patient lie on their back on the ground, and firmly fix a pole in the earth between their thighs, binding the drapels around it so as to not hurt the patient; then let one minister hold his thigh, while another extends the foot with their hands or a rope tied above the ankle; each minister should pull equally, and the pole should be next to the patient's hips to support them during extension; place your hands evenly over the dislocation, while another minister holds the healthy leg below it, and the dislocation will return swiftly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And when it is ready, apply the plaster and wads on top of it, then bandage firmly, binding the foot to the leg, and ensure the nerves above the ankle are not too tight; leave it for two or three days, and if the bandages loosen, rebind them. Then remove the bindings after the third day or fourth day, but prevent the patient from walking for four days; if they walk before that time period is over, it is not safe as it may dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If an abscess forms here, you must treat it as we have said elsewhere until it is healed.
des dois	Twice.
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the thumb is dislocated, it should be gently stretched without work, and this is a minor thing.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is in any of the small bones of the foot, you must make the patient sit on a flat surface or on an upright table, and place your foot on what appears to be these joints, then press firmly with your foot until it returns; when it is aligned, and nothing seems wrong, put under the sole of the foot a two-legged table, then strain it strongly, and leave it for three days, then release it; and let him rest until he is healed.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	Of wounds and dislocations together.
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound comes with dislocation and one wishes to restore it, many times the patient dies: do not be presumptuous in treatment if you are not wise in this art and have not practiced it long enough; nor pitiless or merciless and too eager either—but rather use at first things that cool hot abscesses, and leave the patient in God's hands should you see no hope of recovery. When there is hope however, reset now the limb into place even though hot abscesses will come with this process; and when the limb is in its proper position administer things to cool down hot abscesses, and treat the wound as needed with drying ointments. If bones are broken along with dislocation, and small bits of bone have been torn away, then remove these, and do what we said for simple ailments above. Beware of entering into a state of fear according to my previous statements—for this is your Creator's will, so that you may preserve your soul and body.
Amen	Amen
